قوله - فيه مافيه - دونوں جوابات مصنف کے نزدیک چونکہ غیر پسندیدہ ہیں اس لئے اپنے قول قیل سے اس کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ کرنے کے باوجود پھر اپنے قول فیہ مافیہ سے ایک اعتراض کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ قصد مصم کا موجود ہونا اور نصوص خلق کی عمومیت سے مخصوص ہو کر بندہ کا مخلوق ہو نا صحیح نہیں اس لئے کہ بندہ ممکن ہے اور عبد ممکن کی شان سے غیر کے وجود کا افاضہ نہیں ہے تو عبد ممکن قصد کے وجود کا خلق کیسے کر سکتا ہے!؟ بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ فیہ مافیہ سے مصنف کی مراد یہ ہے کہ انتجاہ حسن تکلیف اور تحقق فائد ہ خلق قدرت ، دونوں اسبات کے متقاضی ہیں کہ بندہ کو صنع حاصل ہے لیکن اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ یہ صنع وہ قصد ہی ہو کیونکہ تمام افعال اختیار یہ سے قصد کو مخصوص کرنا بغیر مخصص کے خاص کرنا ہے۔ جواب :۔ فیہ مافیہ سے مفہوم اعتراض کا جواب یہ دیا گیا کہ جملہ افعال اختیار یہ میں سے قصد کو خاص کرنا بغیر متخصص کے نہیں ہے کیونکہ حنفیہ کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ فائدہ خلق قدرت اور انتجاہ حسن تکلیف دونوں اسبات کے متقاضی ہیں کہ بندہ کو افعال اختیار یہ میں یا افعال اختیار یہ کے وسیلہ میں یا افعال اختیار یہ اور وسیلہ دونوں میں ایک گونہ تاثیر ہونی چاہئے اور افعال اختیار یہ کے وسیلہ میں تاثیر مانا جملہ افعال اختیار یہ میں تاثیر ماننے کے بہ نسبت ادنی ہے اس لئے ہم افعال اختیار یہ کو چھوڑ کر دنی ( قصد کو ) خاص کیا اس لئے کہ جمیع افعال اختیاریہ کی تخصیص جائز نہیں ہے ورنہ عام کا بالکلیہ خاص کر نا لا زم آئے گا اور بالکلیہ عام کی تخصیص جائز نہیں۔ چنانچہ اللہ عز شانہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے ومـاتـشـون الا ان يشاء الله رب العلمین اور والله خلقکم و ماتعملون و غیرها آیات و احادیث جس طرح خلق اعمال و افعال کے انتساب کرنے کو باری تعالیٰ کی طرف دلالت کرتی ہیں اس طرح قصد کے خصوص کی طرف بھی اشارہ ہے اسی لئے تو مشیت و عمل اور فعل کی نسبت باری تعالیٰ نے بندہ کی طرف فرمائی ہے۔
قوله وعندى مختار بحسب الادرلات الجزئية الخ درج بالا عبارت سے مصنف نے زیر بحث مسئلہ میں اپنا موقف و نظریہ پیش کیا ہے چنانچہ
اسباب میں مصنف کا نظریہ یہ ہے کہ بندہ امور جزئیہ جسمانیہ کے اعتبار سے مختار ہے اور علوم کلیہ عقلیہ کے اعتبار سے مجبور ہے۔ مصنف کی عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ افعال اختیار یہ کے صدور کے لئے دو امر ضروری ہیں ایک اور اک کلی ( علوم کلیہ ) جس سے ارادہ کلیہ کا انبعاث وظہور ہوتا ہے دوسرا ادراک جزئی (علوم جزئیہ ) جس سے ارادہ جزئیہ کا ظہور وانبعاث ہوتا ہے پس بندہ امر اول یعنی اور اکات جزئیہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے مختار ہے اور امر ثانی یعنی اور اکات کلیہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے مجبور ہے۔ اسکی مزید توضیح مصنف کے رسالہ الفطرة الالھیہ میں ہے یہ رسالہ اصول غامضہ پر مشتمل ہے جن میں ایک مسئلہ اختیار بھی ہے۔ حاشیہ میں ہے۔ وو "رسالة من المصنف ذكر فيها اصولا غامضة منها مسئلة الاختيار" فطرت الہیہ میں مسئلہ اختیار کے تعلق سے جو کہا ہے اس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے بندہ بحکم وہم مختار ہے اور بحکم عقل مجبور ہے بایں طور کہ شریعت ، امور جزئیہ جیسے ہماری نماز ، ہمارا روزہ ، ہمارا حج وغیرہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور بندہ سے امور جزئیہ کے صدور کے لئے بندہ میں مبادی جزئیہ تقریبہ جیسے خیال جزئی ، شوق جزئی اور ارادہ خاصہ جزئیہ ضروری ہیں کیونکہ ان مبادی جزئیہ کی وجہ سے افعال ارادیہ کہلاتے ہیں کہ ارادہ سے صادر ہوتے ہیں اور اس طرح افعال قریبہ وافعال طبعیہ سے ممتاز ہوتے ہیں مبادی جزئیہ کی طرح ان افعال کے صدور کے لئے مبادی کلیہ بعیدہ جیسے ارادہ کلیہ بھی ضروری ہے جس کا تحقق بلا ارادہ معبد واجب ہے اور چونکہ مبادی اولی جزئیہ بذریعہ و ہم مدرک ہوتے ہیں اس لئے کہ وہ معانی جزئیہ ہیں اور مبادی آخری کلیہ بذریعہ عقل مدرک ہوتے ہیں اس لئے کہ وہ کلیہ ہوتے ہیں پس بندہ نظر کرتے ہوئے علوم جزئیہ کی طرف مختار ہے اور نظر کرتے ہوئے ادراکات کلیہ کی طرف غیر مختار ہے اور جب شرائع امور جزئیہ ہیں تو ان میں حکم وہم کا اعتباری ہے اور مبادی جزئی تقریب کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے بندہ کو امور جز سیکا مکلف بنانا درست ہے۔ و توسط بین الامرین کا معنی یہی ہے کہ بندہ من وجہ یعنی حکم وہم کی جہت سے مختار ہے اور من وجہ یعنی حکم عقل کی جہت سے مجبور ہے۔
His statement: 'fīhi mā fīhi' - both answers are not approved according to the author, so despite indicating their weakness with his statement 'qīla', he then indicates an objection with his statement 'fīhi mā fīhi'. The objection is that the existence of intended purpose (qasd muṣammam) and the specification of the servant as created by the generality of the texts of creation is not correct, because the servant is contingent (mumkin) and it is not the characteristic of a contingent servant to bestow existence on another. So how can a contingent servant create the existence of purpose (qasd)? Some people have said that by 'fīhi mā fīhi' the author means that the attainment of the good of obligation (taḥṣīl ḥusn al-taklīf) and the realization of the benefit of the creation of power (fāʾidah khalq al-qudrah) both require that the servant has creative act (ṣunʿ), but this does not necessitate that this ṣunʿ is exactly that purpose (qasd), because specifying purpose from all voluntary acts without a specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ) is a restriction without specification. The answer: The response to the implied objection by 'fīhi mā fīhi' is that specifying purpose from all voluntary acts is not without a specifier, because what the Ḥanafīs intend is that the benefit of the creation of power and the attainment of the good of obligation both require that the servant should have some kind of effect (taʾthīr) in voluntary acts, or in the means (wasīlah) of voluntary acts, or in both. And acknowledging effect in the means of voluntary acts is lesser compared to acknowledging effect in all voluntary acts. Therefore we left voluntary acts and specified the lesser (purpose), because specification of all voluntary acts is not permissible; otherwise, complete specification of the general (ʿāmm) would become necessary, and complete specification of the general is not permissible. Accordingly, Allah Almighty said: 'And you do not will except that Allah wills, Lord of the worlds' and 'Allah created you and what you do' and other verses and hadiths indicate the attribution of creation of deeds and actions to Allah, and also indicate the specification of purpose. For this reason, Allah attributed will, action, and deed to the servant. His statement: 'And according to me, [man is] free with respect to partial perceptions, etc.' The above phrase shows the author presented his stance and view in the issue under discussion. Thus, the author's view is that the servant is free (mukhtār) with respect to partial physical matters and compelled (majbūr) with respect to universal intellectual sciences. The meaning of the author's phrase is that for the occurrence of voluntary acts, two things are necessary: one, a universal matter (universal sciences) from which universal will emanates and appears; second, a partial perception (partial sciences) from which partial will appears and emanates. So the servant, looking at the first matter (partial perceptions), is free, and looking at the second matter (universal perceptions), is compelled. Further clarification is in the author's treatise 'al-Fiṭrah al-Ilāhiyyah'. This treatise contains profound principles, among them the issue of free will. In the margin: 'A treatise by the author in which he mentioned profound principles, among them the issue of free will.' The summary of what he said in 'Fiṭrah al-Ilāhiyyah' regarding the issue of free will is: The servant, by the decree of imagination (wahm), is free, and by the decree of intellect (ʿaql), is compelled. In that: Sharīʿah came down regarding partial matters like our prayer, our fasting, our ḥajj, etc. For the occurrence of partial matters from the servant, partial proximate principles (mabādī juzʾiyyah taqrībiyyah) like partial thought, partial desire, and particular partial will are necessary, because due to these partial principles, acts are called voluntary (irādiyyah) as they proceed from will, and thus they are distinguished from natural acts and forced acts. Like these partial principles, for the occurrence of these acts, remote universal principles (mabādī kulliyyah baʿīdah) like universal will are also necessary, whose realization without the will of the Worshipped One is obligatory. And since the first partial principles are perceived through imagination (wahm) because they are partial meanings, and the final universal principles are perceived through intellect (ʿaql) because they are universal, therefore the servant, looking at the partial sciences, is free, and looking at the universal perceptions, is not free. And when the religious laws are partial matters, then in them the decree of imagination is considered, and it is correct to hold the servant accountable looking at the partial proximate principles. And the meaning of 'the intermediate between the two matters' (tawassuṭ bayn al-amrayn) is that the servant, from one aspect (the aspect of the decree of imagination), is free, and from another aspect (the aspect of the decree of intellect), is compelled.

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Nuʿūt, a commentary on Muslim al-Thubūt, is a key Hanafi discussion on the issue of human free will (ikhtiyār) and divine predestination (jabr). Key Takeaway
The intermediate position (tawassuṭ bayn al-amrayn) means man is free by wahm and compelled by ʿaql, grounding obligation in the realm where he experiences freedom.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
The Hanafi Doctrine of Between the Two Commands (Tawassut Bayn al-Amrayn)
Explains the author's theory of ikhtiyār and jabr with a dual-faculty epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view that human free will operates at the level of partial perceptions (al-idrākāt al-juzʾiyya) perceived by imagination, while compulsion governs universal perceptions (al-idrākāt al-kulliyya) perceived by intellect, and evaluate how this reconciles human responsibility with divine decree.

Core Idea
Man is free by wahm (imagination) and compelled by aql (intellect). The key to responsibility lies in partial perception.

This passage from Lakhnawi's Sharḥ Muslim al-Thubūt tackles the perennial problem of free will and predestination from a Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh perspective. The author articulates a nuanced middle position: the human being is free when considering particular, specific actions perceived by the imagination, but compelled when considering universal principles perceived by the intellect. This resolution allows for valid religious responsibility (taklīf) for partial acts while acknowledging divine omnipotence. The lesson dissects the epistemological foundations of this view, focusing on the two types of will (universal vs. partial) and the two faculties (imagination vs. intellect).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of human action
The author distinguishes between partial bodily acts (al-umūr al-juzʾiyya al-jismāniyya) and universal intellectual sciences (al-ʿulūm al-kulliyya al-ʿaqliyya). Partial acts are the subject of voluntary action.
2
Locate the two sets of principles
For voluntary acts, there are near partial principles (al-mabādiʾ al-juzʾiyya al-taqrībiyya: thought, desire, will) perceived by wahm, and far universal principles (al-mabādiʾ al-kulliyya al-baʿīda: universal will) perceived by aql.
Universal will is necessary but not under human control.
3
Understand the role of perception
Wahm perceives particular meanings, making the act seem free; aql perceives universals, revealing compulsion from divine decree.
The same act is free in one aspect (partial) and compelled in another (universal).
4
Apply to Sharīʿah
Since Sharīʿah commands partial acts (prayer, fasting, pilgrimage), the taklīf is based on the partial perspective, where the human is considered free and responsible.
5
Synthesize the middle way
The doctrine of 'between the two commands' (tawassut bayn al-amrayn) means freedom from one aspect (partial, wahm) and compulsion from another (universal, aql).
This avoids both complete freedom (pure Qadariyya) and complete compulsion (pure Jabriyya).

Source Text

اسباب میں مصنف کا نظریہ یہ ہے کہ بندہ امور جزئیہ جسمانیہ کے اعتبار سے مختار ہے اور علوم کلیہ عقلیہ کے اعتبار سے مجبور ہے۔ مصنف کی عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ افعال اختیار یہ کے صدور کے لئے دو امر ضروری ہیں ایک اور اک کلی ( علوم کلیہ ) جس سے ارادہ کلیہ کا انبعاث وظہور ہوتا ہے دوسرا ادراک جزئی (علوم جزئیہ ) جس سے ارادہ جزئیہ کا ظہور وانبعاث ہوتا ہے پس بندہ امر اول یعنی اور اکات جزئیہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے مختار ہے اور امر ثانی یعنی اور اکات کلیہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے مجبور ہے۔ اسکی مزید توضیح مصنف کے رسالہ الفطرة الالھیہ میں ہے یہ رسالہ اصول غامضہ پر مشتمل ہے جن میں ایک مسئلہ اختیار بھی ہے۔ حاشیہ میں ہے۔
وو
"رسالة من المصنف ذكر فيها اصولا غامضة منها مسئلة الاختيار"
فطرت الہیہ میں مسئلہ اختیار کے تعلق سے جو کہا ہے اس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے
بندہ بحکم وہم مختار ہے اور بحکم عقل مجبور ہے بایں طور کہ شریعت ، امور جزئیہ جیسے ہماری نماز ، ہمارا روزہ ، ہمارا حج وغیرہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور بندہ سے امور جزئیہ کے صدور کے لئے بندہ میں مبادی جزئیہ تقریبہ جیسے خیال جزئی ، شوق جزئی اور ارادہ خاصہ جزئیہ ضروری ہیں کیونکہ ان مبادی جزئیہ کی وجہ سے افعال ارادیہ کہلاتے ہیں کہ ارادہ سے صادر ہوتے ہیں اور اس طرح افعال قریبہ وافعال طبعیہ سے ممتاز ہوتے ہیں مبادی جزئیہ کی طرح ان افعال کے صدور کے لئے مبادی کلیہ بعیدہ جیسے ارادہ کلیہ بھی ضروری ہے جس کا تحقق بلا ارادہ معبد واجب ہے اور چونکہ مبادی اولی جزئیہ بذریعہ و ہم مدرک ہوتے ہیں اس لئے کہ وہ معانی جزئیہ ہیں اور مبادی آخری کلیہ بذریعہ عقل مدرک ہوتے ہیں اس لئے کہ وہ کلیہ ہوتے ہیں پس بندہ نظر کرتے ہوئے علوم جزئیہ کی طرف مختار ہے اور نظر کرتے ہوئے ادراکات کلیہ کی طرف غیر مختار ہے اور جب شرائع امور جزئیہ ہیں تو ان میں حکم وہم کا اعتباری ہے اور مبادی جزئی تقریب کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے بندہ کو امور جز سیکا مکلف بنانا درست ہے۔ اور توسط بین الامرین کا معنی یہی ہے کہ بندہ من وجہ یعنی حکم وہم کی جہت سے مختار ہے اور من وجہ یعنی حکم عقل کی جہت سے مجبور ہے۔
The author's view regarding causes is that the servant is free with respect to partial bodily matters and compelled with respect to universal intellectual sciences. Meaning of the author's expression: for the emergence of voluntary acts, two things are necessary: one is universal (universal sciences) from which arises universal will; the second is partial perception (partial sciences) from which arises partial will. Thus the servant, considering the first matter (partial perceptions), is free, and considering the second matter (universal perceptions), is compelled. Further clarification is in the author's treatise 'Al-Fitrat al-Ilahiyya', which contains obscure principles, among them the issue of choice. In the margin: 'A treatise by the author in which he mentions obscure principles, among them the issue of choice.' The summary of what is said in 'Fitrat Ilahiyya' regarding choice: The servant is free by the rule of imagination and compelled by the rule of intellect, in that the Shariah was revealed concerning partial matters like our prayer, fasting, pilgrimage, etc. For the occurrence of partial matters from the servant, near partial principles are necessary, such as partial thought, partial desire, and specific partial will, because by these principles acts are called voluntary, proceeding from will, and thus distinguished from natural and coerced acts. Besides these near partial principles, for the occurrence of these acts, far universal principles such as universal will are also necessary, whose realization without will is necessary. Since the first partial principles are perceived by imagination because they are partial meanings, and the final universal principles are perceived by intellect because they are universal, therefore the servant, considering partial sciences, is free, and considering universal perceptions, is not free. And since religious laws are partial matters, the rule of imagination is considered in them, and it is valid to make the servant responsible for partial matters considering the near partial principles. The meaning of 'between the two commands' is that the servant is free from one aspect (the aspect of imagination) and compelled from one aspect (the aspect of intellect).
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents the author's (Lakhnawi's) position on the classic theological problem of free will (ikhtiyar) and compulsion (jabr). The author asserts a middle way: the human being is free when considering partial perceptions (like specific actions) but compelled when considering universal intellectual perceptions. He explains that voluntary acts require two sets of principles: near partial principles (specific thought, desire, will) that are perceived by the imagination, and far universal principles (universal will) perceived by the intellect. Since religious duties (taklif) are about partial acts, they are based on the imaginative faculty, so responsibility is valid. The author's treatise 'Al-Fitrat al-Ilahiyya' elaborates this as the doctrine of 'between the two commands' (tawassut bayn al-amrayn). This is a Hanafi philosophical approach to reconcile human agency with divine decree.

Key Terms
ارادہ کلیہ (irāda kulliyya): Universal will that encompasses all acts and is beyond human control; it is a far principle.
ارادہ جزئیہ (irāda juzʾiyya): Specific will for particular acts; this is the locus of human free will.
وہم (wahm): Imagination or estimative faculty that perceives particular meanings; the basis for human sense of choice.
عقل (ʿaql): Intellect that perceives universals; from the intellectual perspective, human action is compelled by divine decree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what faculty perceives the near partial principles that ground human free will?
A) Intellect (al-ʿaql)
B) Imagination (al-wahm)
C) Reason (al-nuṭq)
D) Memory (al-dhikr)

Key Takeaway
Human freedom and responsibility are valid at the level of partial, concrete acts perceived by imagination, while universal intellectual perception reveals divine compulsion; the two are reconciled through the doctrine of 'between the two commands.'

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Imam Ahmad Raza's Refutation and the Ahl al-Sunnah Doctrine of Kasb
Refutes two extremes and presents the middle path of kasb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two extreme positions on free will and compulsion, and explain the Hanafi-Maturidi doctrine of kasb as the middle path using self-evident experience.

Core Idea
Free will is self-evident, yet created by Allah — the middle path between compulsion and human autonomy.

This lesson centres on a question posed to Imam Ahmad Raza Khan about two doctrines mentioned in 'Muslim al-Thubut' that seem to advocate either complete human freedom or human creation of acts. Imam Ahmad Raza refutes both extremes as false, affirming that the author remains a Sunni Hanafi. He then articulates the Ahl al-Sunnah position: human choice is a self-evident reality, but it and its power are created by Allah. This is the doctrine of kasb (acquisition), which grounds moral responsibility without compromising divine omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two doctrines from Muslim al-Thubut
First: the servant becomes purely free in will (mukhtar mahd). Second: the servant becomes the creator of partial acts of the heart. Both are mentioned by the author and questioned by the inquirer.
These correspond roughly to Qadariyya (human autonomy) and a form of Jabriyya (human creation of acts) extremes.
2
Follow Imam Ahmad Raza's refutation
He declares the first doctrine false, referring to his treatise 'Iqma' al-Mubeen'. The second he calls meaningless with no advocate. He affirms the author is a Sunni Hanafi but warns against diving into such deep matters.
The refutation is based on the authority of Ahl al-Sunnah consensus and rational evidence.
3
Analyze the self-evident nature of human choice
Imam Ahmad Raza gives the example of jumping upward (voluntary) versus falling downward (involuntary). This distinction shows that humans possess genuine choice (ikhtiyar) that is the basis for taklif.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) that everyone experiences in themselves.
4
Connect to the Hanafi-Maturidi doctrine of kasb
While choice is real, it is created by Allah, just as man himself and his faculties are created. Human act is called kasb (acquisition) because the servant acquires or appropriates the act created by Allah.
This reconciles divine predestination (qadr) with human responsibility, avoiding both extremes.

Source Text

مصنف کے موقف پر اعلیٰ حضرت کارد : ۔ اسباب میں مصنف کے نظریہ اور قائلین قصد موجود کے بارے میں اعلیٰ حضرت امام احمد رضا خاں علیہ الرحمہ سے سوال ہوا تھا۔
" کہ مسلم الثبوت میں یہ دو مذہب بیان کئے ہیں یہ باطل و مردود ہیں یا نہیں ! ان سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف آزاد خیال شخص ہیں پہلے کی بناپر ارادہ میں عبد مختار محض ہوا دوسرے کی بنا پر افعال قلوب جزئیہ کا خالق ہوا عبارت یہ ہے وقيل بل موجود فيجب تخصيص القصد المصمم من عموم الخلق بالفعل ایک سطر بعد ہے و عندی مختار بحسب الا دراکات الخ۔

مجنوں .
اهل نست کا نظریہ: امام احمد رضا خاں بریلوی علیہ الرحمہ نے اس مسئلہ میں اہلسنت کا نظریہ پیش کرتے ہوئے فرمایا۔ انسان میں یہ قصد وارادہ و اختیار ہونا ایسا واضح در دشن و بدیہی امر ہے جس سے انکار نہیں کر سکتا مگر ہر شخص واقف ہے کہ جب وہ اوپر کے جانب جست کرتا اور اس کی طاقت ختم ہونے پر زمین پر گرتا ہے ان دونوں حرکتوں میں تفرقہ ہے اوپر کو دنا اپنے اختیا روارادہ سے تھا اگر نہ چاہتا نہ کودتا اور یہ حرکت تمام ہو کر اب زمین پر آنا اپنے ارادہ واختیار سے نہیں لہذا اگر رکنا چاہے تو نہیں رک سکتا بس یہی ارادہ یہی اختیار جو ہر شخص اپنے نفس میں دیکھ رہا ہے عقل کے ساتھ اس کا پایا جاتا یہی مدار امرونهی و جزاوسز او ثواب و عقاب و پرسش و حساب ہے۔ اگر چہ بلاشبہ بلاریب قطعا یقینا یہ ارادہ و اختیار بھی اللہ عزوجل ہی کا پیدا کیا ہوا ہے۔ جیسے انسان خود بھی اسی کا بنایا ہوا ہے آدمی جس طرح نہ آپ سے آپ بن سکتا تھا نہ اپنے لئے آنکھ، کان، ہاتھ ، پاؤں، زبان وغیرھا بنا سکتا تھا یونہی اپنے لئے طاقت قوت ارادہ اختیار بھی نہیں بنا سکتا سب کچھ اس نے دیا اور اس نے بنایا مگر اس سے یہ سمجھ لینا کہ جب
Imam A'la Hadrat's refutation of the author's stance: A question was asked to Imam Ahmad Raza Khan, may Allah have mercy on him, regarding the author's view in the book 'Asbab' and the proponents of 'the qasd existing'. [The question:] 'In Muslim al-Thubut, these two doctrines are mentioned. Are they false and rejected or not? They indicate that the author is a freethinker. Based on the first, the servant becomes purely free in will; based on the second, he becomes the creator of partial acts of the heart. The expression is: 'And it is said: rather it exists, so it is necessary to specify the resolute intent from the generality of creation by the act.' One line later: 'And with me, he is free according to perceptions, etc.' In reply, Imam A'la Hadrat said: 'The first doctrine is false; its refutation is in my treatise 'Iqma' al-Mubeen'. The second doctrine is completely meaningless and has no advocate. The author is a Sunni Hanafi, not a freethinker, but he was prohibited from diving into this tumultuous sea; daring it caused him to slip and be humiliated, and it was bound to happen.' (Fatawa Ridawiyya, vol. 1, p. 46, Raza Academy). The Ahl al-Sunnah view: Imam Ahmad Raza Khan Barelvi presented the Ahl al-Sunnah view on this issue, saying: The existence of intent (qasd), will (irada), and choice (ikhtiyar) in man is such a clear and self-evident matter that cannot be denied. But every person knows that when he jumps upward and then falls to the ground when his strength ends, there is a difference between these two movements: going upward was by his own choice and will; if he did not wish, he would not have jumped. But coming down to the ground is not by his will and choice; if he wants to stop, he cannot. This very will and choice that every person sees in himself, existing along with intellect, is the basis of commands and prohibitions, reward and punishment, and accountability. Even though, without doubt, this will and choice is also created by Allah Almighty, just as man himself is created by Him. Just as man could not come into existence by himself, nor could he make for himself eyes, ears, hands, feet, tongue, etc., likewise he could not make power, strength, will, and choice for himself. All are given and created by Him. But from this one should understand that...
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage records a question posed to Imam Ahmad Raza Khan (d. 1921 CE), a prominent South Asian Hanafi scholar, regarding two doctrines mentioned in 'Muslim al-Thubut' (a usul text) by the author (Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Lakhnawi). The questioner suspects the author of being a freethinker (azad khyal). Imam Ahmad Raza responds sharply: the first doctrine (that the servant is purely free in will) is false and he has refuted it in his treatise 'Iqma' al-Mubeen'. The second doctrine (that the servant becomes the creator of his own acts) is meaningless and has no advocate. He affirms the author is a Sunni Hanafi, but warns against delving into such deep matters, which caused the author to slip. Then the Imam presents the Ahl al-Sunnah view: human free will is self-evident (badihi), known by everyone through common experience. He gives the example of jumping upward (voluntary) versus falling downward (involuntary). This distinction demonstrates that man has genuine choice and will, which is the basis for moral responsibility. However, this will and its power are created by Allah; man does not create his own faculties. This is the Ash'ari/Maturidi position (followed by Hanafis) that affirms human kasb (acquisition) while maintaining divine omnipotence.

Key Terms
قصد (qaṣd): Intent or purpose; the conscious aim underlying an action.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): Free choice; the capacity to choose between alternatives, self-evident in human experience.
کسب (kasb): Acquisition; human action is called kasb because while the act is created by Allah, the human free will acquires or appropriates it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ahmad Raza Khan's Ahl al-Sunnah view, what is the basis for moral accountability (taklif)?
A) Complete freedom of the servant in creating his own acts
B) The self-evident reality of human choice (ikhtiyar) which is created by Allah
C) Denial of any human will, making Allah directly responsible for all acts
D) The intellect's recognition of compulsion alone

Key Takeaway
Human free will is a self-evident reality that forms the basis of moral responsibility, yet it is created by Allah — this is the Hanafi-Maturidi middle path of kasb.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
Rejecting Two Erroneous Views on Human Action in Muslim al-Thubut
Response to a question about two problematic madhhabs in Muslim al-Thubut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions rejected by A'la Hazrat and explain the reasons for their rejection within Hanafi theology.

Core Idea
Two extreme views on free will and compulsion are rejected; only the Sunni middle path is valid.

This lesson opens with a question about two positions mentioned in Muslim al-Thubut regarding human intention and action. A'la Hazrat responds firmly, declaring the first false and the second meaningless. He also defends the author as a Sunni Hanafi while cautioning against diving into such deep theological waters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate the description of the two madhhabs from the question: one makes the servant a pure free agent in intention; the other makes him the creator of particular acts of the heart.
These are presented as possible interpretations from the matn.
2
Note A'la Hazrat's verdict on each
He says the first is false (bāṭil) and the second is meaningless (muhmal bi maʿnā). He references his own treatise Iqmaʿ al-Mubīn for the refutation.
The second is considered to have no real proponent.
3
Understand the defense of the author
Despite presenting flawed positions, the author is a Sunni Hanafi. The commentator says his venture into this topic was forbidden and caused mistake.
This shows a balanced approach: rejecting the views but not the scholar.
4
Extract the usul principle
The rejection sets a boundary: any view that either gives humans independent power or denies them any role is outside Ahl al-Sunnah. This protects the foundation of taklif.

Source Text

اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۲۴۱
مصنف کے موقف پر اعلیٰ حضرت کارد : ۔ اسباب میں مصنف کے نظریہ اور قائلین قصد موجود کے بارے میں اعلیٰ حضرت امام احمد رضا خاں علیہ الرحمہ سے سوال ہوا تھا۔
" کہ مسلم الثبوت میں یہ دو مذہب بیان کئے ہیں یہ باطل و مردود ہیں یا نہیں ! ان سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف آزاد خیال شخص ہیں پہلے کی بناپر ارادہ میں عبد مختار محض ہوا دوسرے کی بنا پر افعال قلوب جزئیہ کا خالق ہوا عبارت یہ ہے وقیل بل موجود فيجب تخصيص القصد المصمم من عموم الخلق بالفعل
ایک سطر بعد ہے و عندی مختار بحسب الا دراکات الخ۔
جواب میں اعلیٰ حضرت قدس سرہ نے فرمایا۔
پہلا مذہب باطل ہے اس کار دفقیر کے رسالہ اقمع المبین میں ہے مذہب دوم محض مہمل و بے معنی ہے جس کا اصلاً کوئی محصل نہیں مصنف سنی حنفی ہیں آزاد خیال نہیں مگر اس بحر خونخوار میں غوطہ زنی سے ممانعت فرمائی گئی تھی اس پر جرات باعث لغزش و ذلت ہوئی اور ہونی ہی تھی (فتویٰ رضویہ ج ۱ ص ۴۶ رضا اکیڈمی )
مجنوں .
اهل نست کا نظریہ: امام احمد رضا خاں بریلوی علیہ الرحمہ نے اس مسئلہ میں اہلسنت کا نظریہ پیش کرتے ہوئے فرمایا۔ انسان میں یہ قصد وارادہ و اختیار ہونا ایسا واضح در دشن و بدیہی امر ہے جس سے انکار نہیں کر سکتا مگر ہر شخص واقف ہے کہ جب وہ اوپر کے جانب جست کرتا اور اس کی طاقت ختم ہونے پر زمین پر گرتا ہے ان دونوں حرکتوں میں تفرقہ ہے اوپر کو دنا اپنے اختیا روارادہ سے تھا اگر نہ چاہتا نہ کودتا اور یہ حرکت تمام ہو کر اب زمین پر آنا اپنے ارادہ واختیار سے نہیں لہذا اگر رکنا چاہے تو نہیں رک سکتا بس یہی ارادہ یہی اختیار جو ہر شخص اپنے نفس میں دیکھ رہا ہے عقل کے ساتھ اس کا پایا جاتا یہی مدار امرونهی و جزاوسز او ثواب و عقاب و پرسش و حساب ہے۔ اگر چہ بلاشبہ بلاریب قطعا یقینا یہ ارادہ و اختیار بھی اللہ عزوجل ہی کا پیدا کیا ہوا ہے۔ جیسے انسان خود بھی اسی کا بنایا ہوا ہے آدمی جس طرح نہ آپ سے آپ بن سکتا تھا نہ اپنے لئے آنکھ، کان، ہاتھ ، پاؤں، زبان وغیرھا بنا سکتا تھا یونہی اپنے لئے طاقت قوت ارادہ اختیار بھی نہیں بنا سکتا سب کچھ اس نے دیا اور اس نے بنایا مگر اس سے یہ سمجھ لینا کہ جب

اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۲۴۲
ہمارا ارادہ واختیار بھی غداری کا مخلوق ہے تو ہم پھر ہو گئے قابل سزا و جزا و باز پرس نہ ر ہے، کیسی سخت جہالت ہے۔ صاحبو! تم میں خدا نے کیا پیدا کیا ؟ ارادہ و اختیار ! تو ان کے پیدا ہونے سے تم صاحب ارادہ، صاحب اختیار ہوئے یا مضطر، مجبور، ناچار ، صاحبو! تمہاری اور پتھر کی حرکت میں فرق کیا تھا؟ یہ کہ وہ ارادہ و اختیار نہیں رکھتا اور تم میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے یہ صفت پیدا کی عجب عجب کہ وہی صفت جس کے پیدا ہونے میں تمہاری حرکات کو پتھر کی حرکت سے ممتاز کر دیا اس کی پیدائش کو اپنے پتھر ہو جانے کا سبب سمجھو یہ کیسی الٹی مت ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے ہماری آنکھیں پیدا کیں ان میں نو خلق کیا اس سے ہم انکھیارے نور ہوئے ، نہ معاذ اللہ اندھے یونہی اس نے ہم میں ارادہ واختیار پیدا کیا اس سے ہم اس کی عطاء کی لائق مختار ہوئے نہ کہ الئے مجبور ہاں یہ ضرور ہے جب وقتا فوقتا ہر فرد اختیار بھی اس کی خلق اس کی عطا سے ہے ہماری اپنی ذات سے نہیں تو مختار کر وہ ہوئے خود مختار نہ ہوئے پھر اس میں کیا حرج ہے بندے کی شان ہی نہیں کہ خود مختار ہو سکے نہ جزا و سزا کے لئے خود مختار ہونا ضرور، ایک نوع اختیار چاہئے کسی طرح ہو بداہنہ حاصل ہے۔ پھر اعلیٰ حضرت قدس سرہ نے اہلسنت و جماعت کے نظریہ کی تائید میں ابونعیم حلیۃ الاولیاء میں روایت کردہ حدیث جو علی مرتضی رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے مروی ہے پیش کیا ہے وہ یہ کہ ایک شخص نے عرض کی یا امیر المؤمنین فلاں شخص کہتا ہے کہ آدمی اپنے قدرت سے کام کرتا ہے اور وہ حضور میں حاضر ہے مولیٰ علی نے فرمایا میرے سامنے لاؤ لوگوں نے اسے کھڑا کیا جب امیر المؤمنین نے اسے دیکھا تیغ مبارک چار انگل کے قدر نیام سے نکالی اور فرمایا کام کی قدرت کا تو خدا کے ساتھ مالک ہے؟ یا خدا سے جدا مالک ہے؟ اور سنتا ہے خبردار ان دونوں میں سے کوئی بات نہ کہنا کہ کافر ہو جائے گا اور میں تیری گردن ماردوں گا اس نے کہا یا امیر المؤمنین پھر میں کیا کہوں؟ فرمایا یوں کہہ کہ اس خدا کے دیے سے اختیار رکھتا ہوں کہ اگر وہ چاہے تو مجھے اختیار دے بے اس کی مشیت کے مجھے کچھ اختیار نہیں" بس یہی عقیدہ اہل سنت ہے کہ انسان پتھر کی طرح مجبور محض ہے نہ خود مختار بلکہ ان دونوں
کے بیچ میں ایک حالت ہے جس کی کنہہ راز خدا اور ایک نہایت عمیق دریا ہے۔
ثلج الصدر لا یمان القد رص ۲۵ تا۳۲)

Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut
241
A'la Hazrat's response regarding the author's stance: A question was asked to A'la Hazrat Imam Ahmad Raza Khan (may mercy be upon him) about the author's view and those who hold the existence of intention in causes.
"That Muslim al-Thubut mentions two madhhabs; are they false and rejected or not? From them it appears that the author is a free-thinking person. According to the first basis, the servant becomes a pure free agent in intention; according the second basis, he becomes the creator of particular acts of the heart. The phrase is: 'And it is said: rather it exists, so it is necessary to specify the determined intention from the general creation with the act.' One line later: 'And according to me, he is free agent according to perceptions etc.'"
In response, A'la Hazrat (may his secret be sanctified) said: The first madhhab is false; its refutation is in the treatise of this poor one, Iqma' al-Mubin. The second madhhab is mere nonsense and meaningless, for which there is essentially no proponent. The author is a Sunni Hanafi, not a free-thinker. But diving into this bloodthirsty sea was forbidden; venturing into it caused slipping and disgrace, and it was bound to happen. (Fatawa Radawiyya, vol. 1, p. 46, Raza Academy)
Majnoon [magazine?]
The view of Ahl al-Sunnah: Imam Ahmad Raza Khan Barelwi (may mercy be upon him) presented the view of Ahl al-Sunnah on this issue, saying: The existence in humans of this intention, will, and choice is so clear, manifest, and self-evident that it cannot be denied. But every person knows that when he jumps upward and falls to the ground when his energy is exhausted, there is a difference between these two motions: going upward was by his own choice and will; if he did not want to, he would not jump. And this motion of coming to the ground now is not by his will and choice; therefore if he wants to stop he cannot stop. Exactly this intention, this choice, which every person sees in his own self and finds it with reason, this is the basis of command and prohibition, reward and punishment, and reckoning. Although, without doubt, without uncertainty, absolutely, certainly, this intention and choice are also created by Allah Almighty. Just as the human himself is also made by Him; just as a person could not create himself nor could he make eyes, ears, hands, feet, tongue, etc., for himself, similarly he cannot make for himself strength, power, will, choice. All is given by Him and made by Him. But to understand from this that when
[PAGE_215]
Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut
242
our will and choice are also created by God [؟], then we become no longer worthy of punishment, reward, and accountability. What severe ignorance! O sirs! What did God create in you? Will and choice! So by their creation, did you become possessors of will, possessors of choice, or constrained, compelled, helpless? O sirs! What was the difference between your motion and a stone's motion? That it does not possess will and choice, while Allah Almighty created this attribute in you. Strange indeed! That you consider the creation itself of the same attribute which distinguishes your motions from a stone's motion, as a cause for you becoming like a stone. What an inverted intellect! Allah Almighty created our eyes, created sight in them, so we became seeing, illuminated, not, God forbid, blind. In the same way, He created in us intention and choice; by that we became worthy of His gift, chosen (mukhtar), not compelled. Yes, it is certainly true that since moment by moment even every individual's choice is His creation, His gift, not from our own selves, so we became chosen by Him, not self-chosen. Then what harm is in that? It is not the servant's station to be self-chosen. For reward and punishment, some type of choice is necessary; it is obtained intuitively in some way.
Then A'la Hazrat (may his secret be sanctified) presented, in support of the view of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, a hadith narrated by Abu Na'im in Hilyat al-Awliya', reported from Ali Murtada (may Allah be pleased with him). It is that a person said: O Commander of the Faithful, a certain person says that a man acts by his own power, and he is present. Mawla 'Ali said: Bring him before me. The people made him stand. When the Commander of the Faithful saw him, he drew his blessed sword four fingers out of the sheath and said: 'Are you a partner with God in the power to act? Or are you a possessor of power separate from God? And listen: beware, do not say either of these two things, or you will become an infidel and I will strike your neck.' He said: O Commander of the Faithful, then what should I say? He said: Say thus: 'I possess choice by the gift of God; if He wills He gives me choice, without His will I have no choice at all.'" This is exactly the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah: that man is neither purely compelled like a stone nor self-willed; rather there is a state between the two, whose reality is a secret of God and an extremely profound sea.
(Thalj al-Sadr La Yaman al-Qadr, pp. 25-32)
Scanned by CamScanner
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a response to a question about two positions mentioned in the original matn (Muslim al-Thubut) regarding the creation of human actions and intentions. The first position implies that the servant is a pure free agent in intention, the second that man creates particular acts of the heart. A'la Hazrat Imam Ahmad Raza Khan declares the first false (referring to his treatise Iqma' al-Mubin) and the second meaningless. He defends the author as a Sunni Hanafi, but criticizes his dive into a dangerous theological topic. The author's two views are rejected. A'la Hazrat then expounds the Ahl al-Sunnah view: human choice (ikhtiyar) and intention (qasd) are self-evident; every person distinguishes between voluntary and involuntary actions. This choice is the basis for moral and legal accountability (taklif, reward/punishment). Yet this very choice is created by Allah, just as all human faculties are. There is no contradiction: Allah creates the attribute of choice, and by it the human becomes a genuine chooser (mukhtar), not compelled like a stone. The human acquires (kasb) the action; Allah creates it. To support this, A'la Hazrat cites a hadith from Ali (RA) recorded in Abu Na'im's Hilyat al-Awliya': (Summary) Ali confronts a man who claimed independent power, forcing him to choose between associating with God (shirk) or denying God's power (kufr). The correct middle way is to say: 'I have choice by God's gift; without His will I have no choice.' This is the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah, avoiding both jabr (compulsion) and tafwid (absolute delegation). The author's original text thus contains problematic statements, but the commentator corrects them by affirming the Sunni position.

Key Terms
قصد (qasd): Intention, purpose; the determined intention that distinguishes voluntary action.
ارادہ و اختیار (iradah wa ikhtiyar): Will and choice; the attributes given to humans by Allah that make them capable of voluntary action and deserving of reward or punishment.
خالق (khaliq): Creator; the one who brings into existence. Used here to assert that only Allah creates, including human will and actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did A'la Hazrat say about the first madhhab mentioned in the question?
A) It is a valid ikhtilaf.
B) It is false (bāṭil).
C) It is meaningless (muhmal).
D) It is acceptable with conditions.

Key Takeaway
Two extreme views on human action are firmly rejected; the Hanafi middle path avoids both shirk and jabr.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Sunni Position: Human Choice Created by Allah, Yet Genuine
Exposition of the Ahl al-Sunnah view on human choice and responsibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi/Maturidi view that human choice is created by Allah yet constitutes genuine agency and accountability.

Core Idea
Created choice (ikhtiyār maḫlūq) is the basis for genuine human responsibility, not a denial of it.

This lesson dives into the heart of the Sunni response: A'la Hazrat expounds the self-evident distinction between voluntary and involuntary actions, showing that human intention and choice are the basis for commands, rewards, and punishments. He firmly states that this choice is created by Allah, just like all other faculties. Yet, he argues, this creation does not nullify responsibility; rather, it makes it possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the self-evident distinction
The passage points out that every person can distinguish between voluntary actions (like jumping upwards) and involuntary actions (like falling down). This distinction is the foundation of moral responsibility.
It is immediate and undeniable.
2
Affirm the creation of choice
A'la Hazrat asserts that this intention, will, and choice are also created by Allah. Just as eyes and sight are created, so are choice and will.
Humans do not create their own attributes.
3
Refute the misconception of compulsion
The commentator addresses the potential objection: if choice is created, then humans are not responsible. He says this is severe ignorance. Created choice still gives the human the attribute of being a chooser (mukhtar), not a compelled stone.
The attribute itself enables agency.
4
Understand the philosophical nuance
The human becomes 'chosen by God' (mukhtar min Allah) not 'self-chosen' (mukhtar bi-nafsih). This preserves both divine omnipotence and human accountability.
This is the middle path of kasb.

ہمارا ارادہ واختیار بھی غداری کا مخلوق ہے تو ہم پھر ہو گئے قابل سزا و جزا و باز پرس نہ ر ہے، کیسی سخت جہالت ہے۔ صاحبو! تم میں خدا نے کیا پیدا کیا ؟ ارادہ و اختیار ! تو ان کے پیدا ہونے سے تم صاحب ارادہ، صاحب اختیار ہوئے یا مضطر، مجبور، ناچار ، صاحبو! تمہاری اور پتھر کی حرکت میں فرق کیا تھا؟ یہ کہ وہ ارادہ و اختیار نہیں رکھتا اور تم میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے یہ صفت پیدا کی عجب عجب کہ وہی صفت جس کے پیدا ہونے میں تمہاری حرکات کو پتھر کی حرکت سے ممتاز کر دیا اس کی پیدائش کو اپنے پتھر ہو جانے کا سبب سمجھو یہ کیسی الٹی مت ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے ہماری آنکھیں پیدا کیں ان میں نو خلق کیا اس سے ہم انکھیارے نور ہوئے ، نہ معاذ اللہ اندھے یونہی اس نے ہم میں ارادہ واختیار پیدا کیا اس سے ہم اس کی عطاء کی لائق مختار ہوئے نہ کہ الئے مجبور ہاں یہ ضرور ہے جب وقتا فوقتا ہر فرد اختیار بھی اس کی خلق اس کی عطا سے ہے ہماری اپنی ذات سے نہیں تو مختار کر وہ ہوئے خود مختار نہ ہوئے پھر اس میں کیا حرج ہے بندے کی شان ہی نہیں کہ خود مختار ہو سکے نہ جزا و سزا کے لئے خود مختار ہونا ضرور، ایک نوع اختیار چاہئے کسی طرح ہو بداہنہ حاصل ہے۔ پھر اعلیٰ حضرت قدس سرہ نے اہلسنت و جماعت کے نظریہ کی تائید میں ابونعیم حلیۃ الاولیاء میں روایت کردہ حدیث جو علی مرتضی رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے مروی ہے پیش کیا ہے وہ یہ کہ ایک شخص نے عرض کی یا امیر المؤمنین فلاں شخص کہتا ہے کہ آدمی اپنے قدرت سے کام کرتا ہے اور وہ حضور میں حاضر ہے مولیٰ علی نے فرمایا میرے سامنے لاؤ لوگوں نے اسے کھڑا کیا جب امیر المؤمنین نے اسے دیکھا تیغ مبارک چار انگل کے قدر نیام سے نکالی اور فرمایا کام کی قدرت کا تو خدا کے ساتھ مالک ہے؟ یا خدا سے جدا مالک ہے؟ اور سنتا ہے خبردار ان دونوں میں سے کوئی بات نہ کہنا کہ کافر ہو جائے گا اور میں تیری گردن ماردوں گا اس نے کہا یا امیر المؤمنین پھر میں کیا کہوں؟ فرمایا یوں کہہ کہ اس خدا کے دیے سے اختیار رکھتا ہوں کہ اگر وہ چاہے تو مجھے اختیار دے بے اس کی مشیت کے مجھے کچھ اختیار نہیں" بس یہی عقیدہ اہل سنت ہے کہ انسان پتھر کی طرح مجبور محض ہے نہ خود مختار بلکہ ان دونوں
کے بیچ میں ایک حالت ہے جس کی کنہہ راز خدا اور ایک نہایت عمیق دریا ہے۔
ثلج الصدر لا یمان القد رص ۲۵ تا۳۲)

Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut
241
A'la Hazrat's response regarding the author's stance: A question was asked to A'la Hazrat Imam Ahmad Raza Khan (may mercy be upon him) about the author's view and those who hold the existence of intention in causes.
"That Muslim al-Thubut mentions two madhhabs; are they false and rejected or not? From them it appears that the author is a free-thinking person. According to the first basis, the servant becomes a pure free agent in intention; according the second basis, he becomes the creator of particular acts of the heart. The phrase is: 'And it is said: rather it exists, so it is necessary to specify the determined intention from the general creation with the act.' One line later: 'And according to me, he is free agent according to perceptions etc.'"
In response, A'la Hazrat (may his secret be sanctified) said: The first madhhab is false; its refutation is in the treatise of this poor one, Iqma' al-Mubin. The second madhhab is mere nonsense and meaningless, for which there is essentially no proponent. The author is a Sunni Hanafi, not a free-thinker. But diving into this bloodthirsty sea was forbidden; venturing into it caused slipping and disgrace, and it was bound to happen. (Fatawa Radawiyya, vol. 1, p. 46, Raza Academy)
Majnoon [magazine?]
The view of Ahl al-Sunnah: Imam Ahmad Raza Khan Barelwi (may mercy be upon him) presented the view of Ahl al-Sunnah on this issue, saying: The existence in humans of this intention, will, and choice is so clear, manifest, and self-evident that it cannot be denied. But every person knows that when he jumps upward and falls to the ground when his energy is exhausted, there is a difference between these two motions: going upward was by his own choice and will; if he did not want to, he would not jump. And this motion of coming to the ground now is not by his will and choice; therefore if he wants to stop he cannot stop. Exactly this intention, this choice, which every person sees in his own self and finds it with reason, this is the basis of command and prohibition, reward and punishment, and reckoning. Although, without doubt, without uncertainty, absolutely, certainly, this intention and choice are also created by Allah Almighty. Just as the human himself is also made by Him; just as a person could not create himself nor could he make eyes, ears, hands, feet, tongue, etc., for himself, similarly he cannot make for himself strength, power, will, choice. All is given by Him and made by Him. But to understand from this that when
[PAGE_215]
Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut
242
our will and choice are also created by God [؟], then we become no longer worthy of punishment, reward, and accountability. What severe ignorance! O sirs! What did God create in you? Will and choice! So by their creation, did you become possessors of will, possessors of choice, or constrained, compelled, helpless? O sirs! What was the difference between your motion and a stone's motion? That it does not possess will and choice, while Allah Almighty created this attribute in you. Strange indeed! That you consider the creation itself of the same attribute which distinguishes your motions from a stone's motion, as a cause for you becoming like a stone. What an inverted intellect! Allah Almighty created our eyes, created sight in them, so we became seeing, illuminated, not, God forbid, blind. In the same way, He created in us intention and choice; by that we became worthy of His gift, chosen (mukhtar), not compelled. Yes, it is certainly true that since moment by moment even every individual's choice is His creation, His gift, not from our own selves, so we became chosen by Him, not self-chosen. Then what harm is in that? It is not the servant's station to be self-chosen. For reward and punishment, some type of choice is necessary; it is obtained intuitively in some way.
Then A'la Hazrat (may his secret be sanctified) presented, in support of the view of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, a hadith narrated by Abu Na'im in Hilyat al-Awliya', reported from Ali Murtada (may Allah be pleased with him). It is that a person said: O Commander of the Faithful, a certain person says that a man acts by his own power, and he is present. Mawla 'Ali said: Bring him before me. The people made him stand. When the Commander of the Faithful saw him, he drew his blessed sword four fingers out of the sheath and said: 'Are you a partner with God in the power to act? Or are you a possessor of power separate from God? And listen: beware, do not say either of these two things, or you will become an infidel and I will strike your neck.' He said: O Commander of the Faithful, then what should I say? He said: Say thus: 'I possess choice by the gift of God; if He wills He gives me choice, without His will I have no choice at all.'" This is exactly the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah: that man is neither purely compelled like a stone nor self-willed; rather there is a state between the two, whose reality is a secret of God and an extremely profound sea.
(Thalj al-Sadr La Yaman al-Qadr, pp. 25-32)
Scanned by CamScanner
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a response to a question about two positions mentioned in the original matn (Muslim al-Thubut) regarding the creation of human actions and intentions. The first position implies that the servant is a pure free agent in intention, the second that man creates particular acts of the heart. A'la Hazrat Imam Ahmad Raza Khan declares the first false (referring to his treatise Iqma' al-Mubin) and the second meaningless. He defends the author as a Sunni Hanafi, but criticizes his dive into a dangerous theological topic. The author's two views are rejected. A'la Hazrat then expounds the Ahl al-Sunnah view: human choice (ikhtiyar) and intention (qasd) are self-evident; every person distinguishes between voluntary and involuntary actions. This choice is the basis for moral and legal accountability (taklif, reward/punishment). Yet this very choice is created by Allah, just as all human faculties are. There is no contradiction: Allah creates the attribute of choice, and by it the human becomes a genuine chooser (mukhtar), not compelled like a stone. The human acquires (kasb) the action; Allah creates it. To support this, A'la Hazrat cites a hadith from Ali (RA) recorded in Abu Na'im's Hilyat al-Awliya': (Summary) Ali confronts a man who claimed independent power, forcing him to choose between associating with God (shirk) or denying God's power (kufr). The correct middle way is to say: 'I have choice by God's gift; without His will I have no choice.' This is the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah, avoiding both jabr (compulsion) and tafwid (absolute delegation). The author's original text thus contains problematic statements, but the commentator corrects them by affirming the Sunni position.

Key Terms
قصد (qasd): Intention; the specific determination that distinguishes voluntary actions.
ارادہ و اختیار (iradah wa ikhtiyar): Will and choice; the God-given capacity to choose.
خالق (khaliq): Creator; exclusively Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of Allah creating human choice (ikhtiyar)?
A) It makes humans mere automata without responsibility.
B) It makes humans genuine agents responsible for their actions.
C) It makes God responsible for human sin.
D) It removes the basis for reward and punishment.

Key Takeaway
Created choice is the foundation of genuine human agency and moral responsibility, not a denial of it.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
7 min
The Proof from Hadith: Imam Ali's Middle Path on Divine Power and Human Agency
Proof from hadith for the Ahl al-Sunnah middle path on human action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the hadith of Ali (RA) from Hilyat al-Awliya' serves as a proof for the Hanafi position on human choice, and identify the specific wording that encapsulates the middle path.

Core Idea
Ali (RA) presented a verbal formula that avoids both shirk and kufr: 'I have choice by God's gift, not independently.'

A'la Hazrat now provides textual evidence: a hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA). When a man claimed independent power, Ali drew his sword and forced him to choose between partnership with God (shirk) and denial of God's power (kufr). The man then asked what he should say, and Ali taught him the correct phrase: possession of choice by God's gift, not without God's will. This hadith perfectly encapsulates the Ahl al-Sunnah creed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of the hadith
A man claimed that a person acts by his own power (qudra). Ali (RA) confronts him by presenting two extremes: either you have power as a partner with God or as separate from God. Both are unacceptable.
The two extremes correspond to the earlier two madhhabs.
2
Identify the correct formula
The man asks what to say, and Ali teaches: 'I have choice by the gift of God; if He wills He gives me choice, without His will I have no choice at all.' This is the middle path.
This formula affirms human choice while entirely derivatively from God.
3
Analyze the dalala of the hadith
The hadith explicitly rejects both shirk (partnership with God) and kufr (denial of God's power). It establishes that human choice is a gift from God, not independent.
The wording 'If He wills He gives me choice' implies that choice is contingent on divine will.
4
Apply to the usul context
This hadith is used as a proof (dalil naqli) for the Hanafi position on kasb. It shows that the correct belief is between jabr and tafwiz.
It is not a mutawatir hadith, but it is sufficient for this theological point.

۲۴۱
مصنف کے موقف پر اعلیٰ حضرت کارد : ۔ اسباب میں مصنف کے نظریہ اور قائلین قصد موجود کے بارے میں اعلیٰ حضرت امام احمد رضا خاں علیہ الرحمہ سے سوال ہوا تھا۔

ایک سطر بعد ہے و عندی مختار بحسب الا دراکات الخ۔
جواب میں اعلیٰ حضرت قدس سرہ نے فرمایا۔

مجنوں .
اهل نست کا نظریہ: امام احمد رضا خاں بریلوی علیہ الرحمہ نے اس مسئلہ میں اہلسنت کا نظریہ پیش کرتے ہوئے فرمایا۔ انسان میں یہ قصد وارادہ و اختیار ہونا ایسا واضح در دشن و بدیہی امر ہے جس سے انکار نہیں کر سکتا مگر ہر شخص واقف ہے کہ جب وہ اوپر کے جانب جست کرتا اور اس کی طاقت ختم ہونے پر زمین پر گرتا ہے ان دونوں حرکتوں میں تفرقہ ہے اوپر کو دنا اپنے اختیا روارادہ سے تھا اگر نہ چاہتا نہ کودتا اور یہ حرکت تمام ہو کر اب زمین پر آنا اپنے ارادہ واختیار سے نہیں لہذا اگر رکنا چاہے تو نہیں رک سکتا بس یہی ارادہ یہی اختیار جو ہر شخص اپنے نفس میں دیکھ رہا ہے عقل کے ساتھ اس کا پایا جاتا یہی مدار امرونهی و جزاوسز او ثواب و عقاب و پرسش و حساب ہے۔ اگر چہ بلاشبہ بلاریب قطعا یقینا یہ ارادہ و اختیار بھی اللہ عزوجل ہی کا پیدا کیا ہوا ہے۔ جیسے انسان خود بھی اسی کا بنایا ہوا ہے آدمی جس طرح نہ آپ سے آپ بن سکتا تھا نہ اپنے لئے آنکھ، کان، ہاتھ ، پاؤں، زبان وغیرھا بنا سکتا تھا یونہی اپنے لئے طاقت قوت ارادہ اختیار بھی نہیں بنا سکتا سب کچھ اس نے دیا اور اس نے بنایا مگر اس سے یہ سمجھ لینا کہ جب

Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut
241
A'la Hazrat's response regarding the author's stance: A question was asked to A'la Hazrat Imam Ahmad Raza Khan (may mercy be upon him) about the author's view and those who hold the existence of intention in causes.
"That Muslim al-Thubut mentions two madhhabs; are they false and rejected or not? From them it appears that the author is a free-thinking person. According to the first basis, the servant becomes a pure free agent in intention; according the second basis, he becomes the creator of particular acts of the heart. The phrase is: 'And it is said: rather it exists, so it is necessary to specify the determined intention from the general creation with the act.' One line later: 'And according to me, he is free agent according to perceptions etc.'"
In response, A'la Hazrat (may his secret be sanctified) said: The first madhhab is false; its refutation is in the treatise of this poor one, Iqma' al-Mubin. The second madhhab is mere nonsense and meaningless, for which there is essentially no proponent. The author is a Sunni Hanafi, not a free-thinker. But diving into this bloodthirsty sea was forbidden; venturing into it caused slipping and disgrace, and it was bound to happen. (Fatawa Radawiyya, vol. 1, p. 46, Raza Academy)
Majnoon [magazine?]
The view of Ahl al-Sunnah: Imam Ahmad Raza Khan Barelwi (may mercy be upon him) presented the view of Ahl al-Sunnah on this issue, saying: The existence in humans of this intention, will, and choice is so clear, manifest, and self-evident that it cannot be denied. But every person knows that when he jumps upward and falls to the ground when his energy is exhausted, there is a difference between these two motions: going upward was by his own choice and will; if he did not want to, he would not jump. And this motion of coming to the ground now is not by his will and choice; therefore if he wants to stop he cannot stop. Exactly this intention, this choice, which every person sees in his own self and finds it with reason, this is the basis of command and prohibition, reward and punishment, and reckoning. Although, without doubt, without uncertainty, absolutely, certainly, this intention and choice are also created by Allah Almighty. Just as the human himself is also made by Him; just as a person could not create himself nor could he make eyes, ears, hands, feet, tongue, etc., for himself, similarly he cannot make for himself strength, power, will, choice. All is given by Him and made by Him. But to understand from this that when
[PAGE_215]
Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut
242
our will and choice are also created by God [؟], then we become no longer worthy of punishment, reward, and accountability. What severe ignorance! O sirs! What did God create in you? Will and choice! So by their creation, did you become possessors of will, possessors of choice, or constrained, compelled, helpless? O sirs! What was the difference between your motion and a stone's motion? That it does not possess will and choice, while Allah Almighty created this attribute in you. Strange indeed! That you consider the creation itself of the same attribute which distinguishes your motions from a stone's motion, as a cause for you becoming like a stone. What an inverted intellect! Allah Almighty created our eyes, created sight in them, so we became seeing, illuminated, not, God forbid, blind. In the same way, He created in us intention and choice; by that we became worthy of His gift, chosen (mukhtar), not compelled. Yes, it is certainly true that since moment by moment even every individual's choice is His creation, His gift, not from our own selves, so we became chosen by Him, not self-chosen. Then what harm is in that? It is not the servant's station to be self-chosen. For reward and punishment, some type of choice is necessary; it is obtained intuitively in some way.
Then A'la Hazrat (may his secret be sanctified) presented, in support of the view of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, a hadith narrated by Abu Na'im in Hilyat al-Awliya', reported from Ali Murtada (may Allah be pleased with him). It is that a person said: O Commander of the Faithful, a certain person says that a man acts by his own power, and he is present. Mawla 'Ali said: Bring him before me. The people made him stand. When the Commander of the Faithful saw him, he drew his blessed sword four fingers out of the sheath and said: 'Are you a partner with God in the power to act? Or are you a possessor of power separate from God? And listen: beware, do not say either of these two things, or you will become an infidel and I will strike your neck.' He said: O Commander of the Faithful, then what should I say? He said: Say thus: 'I possess choice by the gift of God; if He wills He gives me choice, without His will I have no choice at all.'" This is exactly the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah: that man is neither purely compelled like a stone nor self-willed; rather there is a state between the two, whose reality is a secret of God and an extremely profound sea.
(Thalj al-Sadr La Yaman al-Qadr, pp. 25-32)
Scanned by CamScanner
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a response to a question about two positions mentioned in the original matn (Muslim al-Thubut) regarding the creation of human actions and intentions. The first position implies that the servant is a pure free agent in intention, the second that man creates particular acts of the heart. A'la Hazrat Imam Ahmad Raza Khan declares the first false (referring to his treatise Iqma' al-Mubin) and the second meaningless. He defends the author as a Sunni Hanafi, but criticizes his dive into a dangerous theological topic. The author's two views are rejected. A'la Hazrat then expounds the Ahl al-Sunnah view: human choice (ikhtiyar) and intention (qasd) are self-evident; every person distinguishes between voluntary and involuntary actions. This choice is the basis for moral and legal accountability (taklif, reward/punishment). Yet this very choice is created by Allah, just as all human faculties are. There is no contradiction: Allah creates the attribute of choice, and by it the human becomes a genuine chooser (mukhtar), not compelled like a stone. The human acquires (kasb) the action; Allah creates it. To support this, A'la Hazrat cites a hadith from Ali (RA) recorded in Abu Na'im's Hilyat al-Awliya': (Summary) Ali confronts a man who claimed independent power, forcing him to choose between associating with God (shirk) or denying God's power (kufr). The correct middle way is to say: 'I have choice by God's gift; without His will I have no choice.' This is the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah, avoiding both jabr (compulsion) and tafwid (absolute delegation). The author's original text thus contains problematic statements, but the commentator corrects them by affirming the Sunni position.

Key Terms
قصد (qasd): Intention, purpose.
ارادہ و اختیار (iradah wa ikhtiyar): Will and choice; what the man claims to possess independently, but corrected to be a gift.
خالق (khaliq): Creator; the one who gives power and choice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Ali (RA) imply when he said to the man, 'Do not say either of these two things, or you will become an infidel'?
A) Both statements (partner with God or separate from God) are permissible for debate.
B) Both statements are forms of disbelief (kufr).
C) Only the first statement is kufr.
D) Only the second statement is kufr.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Ali (RA) provides the precise verbal formulation of the Sunni middle path on human agency and divine power.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Ash'ari Fourth Argument and Hanafi Response on Rational Good/Evil
Presents and refutes Ash'ari fourth argument on rational good/evil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Ash'ari fourth argument against rational good/evil and explain the Hanafi response, including the key distinction between wisdom-based command and compulsion.

Core Idea
Divine wisdom does not constrain God's freedom; commanding wisely is a free act, not a compulsion.

In this passage from 'Ashraf al-Nu'ut', the author presents the Ash'ari fourth argument against the doctrine of rational good and evil (husn wa qubh 'aqli). The Ash'aris contend that if actions had inherent moral properties, God would be compelled to command accordingly, negating His freedom. The Hanafi response affirms that God's commands align with wisdom, but this alignment is a free choice, not a necessity. The commentary (tashrih) expands on the logical structure of the argument and the rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ash'ari claim
Read the matn and its explanation: the Ash'aris argue that if good and evil were rational, God would not be free (mukhtar) in His commands because commanding contrary to reason would be evil (qabih), and evil cannot occur from God.
The key term is 'mukhtar' (free) vs 'mudtar' (compelled).
2
Understand the logical consequence
The Ash'ari reasoning is a reductio: if rational good/evil exists, then God must command the good and prohibit the evil, otherwise He would be doing evil. Thus God would lose freedom of choice.
They view this as an intolerable limitation on divine power.
3
State the Hanafi rebuttal
The matn gives the answer: 'موافقة حكمه للحكمة لا يوجب الاضطرار' – God's command being in accordance with wisdom does not necessitate compulsion. The commentary repeats: it does not imply that God is forced.
The Hanafi response denies the consequential link between wisdom and compulsion.
4
Analyze the distinction
The Hanafi position holds that God freely wills to act wisely; wisdom is not an external constraint. The tashrih emphasizes that the 'mulazama' (connection) that the Ash'aris claimed is not valid.
The underlying usul principle: divine attributes (like wisdom) are not separate from His essence; His will is free.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider a fiqh issue: the moral status of an act before revelation. For Hanafis, some acts are good or evil by reason (e.g., justice, lying). For Ash'aris, moral value depends solely on divine command. This difference affects how rulings are derived in silent areas.
This shows the practical consequence of the usul dispute.

[Full translation would be very long; brief summary: The passage discusses human free will as created by God, then presents a hadith from Ali about predestination, then transitions to praise of the treatise, then gives the matn: 'Fourth: If that were the case, the Exalted Creator would not be free in His command because commanding contrary to reason is evil. Source pages p. 215

Commentary
The passage begins with a theological discussion on human free will and divine decree, arguing that human will is created by God, yet humans are accountable. It then quotes a hadith from Ali (RA) supporting the Ash'ari position that human agency is derived from God's grant. The author then transitions to praise his treatise 'Firtat al-Ilahiyya'. The core usul al-fiqh content starts with the matn: 'Fourth: If that were the case, the Exalted Creator would not be free in His command...' This is the Ash'ari fourth argument against rational good and evil (husn and qubh). The argument: if good and evil were rational, then God would be compelled to command good and prohibit evil, negating His freedom. The Hanafi response: God's command being in accordance with wisdom does not imply compulsion; it is a voluntary act of wisdom. The commentary ('tashrih') elaborates that the Ash'arites and Hanafis differ on the source of moral values: Hanafis and Mu'tazila hold that good and evil are rational properties of actions, while Ash'arites hold they are determined by divine command. The passage provides the Ash'ari reasoning and the Hanafi rebuttal.

Key Terms
حسن و قبح عقلی (husn wa qubh 'aqli): The doctrine that actions have inherent moral qualities (goodness and badness) that can be known by reason alone.
مختار (mukhtar): Having free choice; not constrained in action.
مضطر (mudtar): Compelled; lacking freedom of choice.
حکمت (hikma): Wisdom; divine wisdom in command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because wisdom is a property of God's own essence, not an external constraint.
C) Because God's command being wise is a free act of His will, not a compulsion.
D) Because rational good and evil are illusions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi response to the Ash'ari fourth argument is that God's wisdom is freely chosen, so rational good/evil does not limit divine freedom.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Ash'ari's Fourth Argument and Hanafi Response on Rational Good/Bad
Ash'ari argument and Hanafi refutation on rational husn/qubh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Ash'ari argument that rational good/bad would compel divine action and apply the Hanafi response that denies the implication, using the concept of ikhtiyār.

Core Idea
Divine conformity to wisdom is chosen, not compelled — ikhtiyār preserves freedom.

This passage presents a usul dispute between the Ash'ari and Hanafi schools on whether moral good and bad are rationally discernible. The Ash'aris argue that if reason could determine good/bad, Allah would be compelled to judge accordingly, negating His free will. The Hanafi response carefully denies the necessary implication, explaining that Allah's judgment accords with wisdom through His own choice. Understanding this defense is key to grasping the Hanafi position on rational obligation (wujūb 'aqlī).

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing argument
State the Ash'ari's fourth argument: if good/bad are rational, then Allah would be compelled to command the good and prohibit the bad, negating His ikhtiyār. This is because a judgment contrary to reason would be bad (qabīḥ), and bad cannot proceed from Allah.
The argument uses logical implication (luzūm): rational good/bad → compulsion → impossible → reject rational good/bad.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response: man' al-istilzām
The Hanafi school denies the implication (luzūm). They argue that the obligation of a judgment based on wisdom is established through Allah's own will (mashī'a), not through an external constraint. Therefore, no compulsion follows.
The key phrase: 'موافقة حكمه للحكمة لا يوجب الاضطرار' (His judgment's accordance with wisdom does not necessitate compulsion).
3
Define ikhtiyār in this context
Understand the Hanafi definition of choice: the possibility of both doing and not doing, supported by power (qudra) over both alternatives. Choice requires that the agent can do or not do; if only one side is possible, it is compulsion.
Reference the legal definition dissector: sabab = possibility of both; shart = power over both; mani = impossibility of one side.
4
Apply the definition to divine action
Even though Allah wills one side (e.g., commanding good) such that it becomes necessary through His will, the other side (e.g., forbidding good) remains possible in terms of power. Thus, compulsion is absent; ikhtiyār is preserved because the act is chosen, not forced.
The commentary explains: 'if He wills its abandonment, abandonment would be necessary' — thus possibility remains.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafis accept that certain acts are rationally obligatory (wājib 'aqlan) before revelation (e.g., knowing God, thanking the benefactor). Ash'aris deny any obligation before revelation (lā ḥukm qabl al-shar').
This impacts rulings on the status of non-Muslims before the advent of a prophet, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ہونے ) پر چوتھی دلیل دیتے ہوئے کہا کہ اگر حسن و قبح عقلی ہوتو باری تعالٰی حکم میں مختار نہیں رہ جائیگا اس لیے کہ خلاف معقول حکم قبیح ہے اور جواب یہ ہیکہ اس کے حکم کا حکمت کے موافق ہونا اضطرار کولازم نہیں کرتا ہے۔ تشريح - قوله رابعألوكان كذالك لم يكن الباري الخ درج بالا عبارت سے ماتن نے حسن و قبح کے عقلی نہ ہونے پر اشاعرہ کی چوتھی دلیل ذکر کی ہے۔ دلیل کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حسن و قبح ذات فعل ، یا صفت حقیقیہ یا صفت اعتباریہ کی وجہ سے عقلی ہو جیسا کہ معتزلہ و حنفیہ کہتے ہیں تو زبردست استحالہ یہ لازم آئیگا کہ اللہ عز شانہ تعالیٰ اپنے حکم تحریم و ایجاب وغیرہما میں قادر و مختار نہیں رہ جائیگا بلکہ مضطر و مجبور شے رہے گا اور لازم باطل ہے اس لئے ملزوم بھی باطل ہوا الہذا حسن و قبح کا عقلی ہونا باطل ہوا۔ وجہ ملازمت یہ ہیکہ حسن و قبح کے عقلی ہونے کی تقدیر پر تقاضائے حسن و قبیح کے خلاف حکم دینا خلاف معقول ہے اور تقاضائے عقل کے خلاف حکم قبیح ہے اور قبیح کا صدور اللہ تعالیٰ سے محال پس جس فعل میں عقلاً قبح ہو اسکی تحریم کا حکم اور جس فعل میں عقلا حسن ہو اس کے ایجاب کا حکم دینا اللہ پر لازم و واجب ہوا کیونکہ حسن و قبح کے مقتضی کے خلاف حکم قبیح و محال ہے اور پھر جب قبح میں تحریم کا حکم اور حسن میں ایجاب کا حکم دینا اللہ تعالیٰ پر لازم ہو گیا تو وہ حکم میں مختار نہیں رہ گیا اس لئے کہ فاعل میں فعل کا لزوم ووجوب اضطرار کو لازم کرتا ہے اور اضطرار شان باری تعالیٰ میں اجماعاً باطل ہے۔ قوله- والجواب أن موافقة حكمه للحكمة الخ اس عبارت سے اشاعرہ کی دلیل مذکور کا جواب دیا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تقاضائے حسن و قبح کے پیش نظر حکم باری تعالیٰ کا حکمت کے موافق ہو جانا اضطرار کو لازم نہیں کرتا ہے کیونکہ وجوب حکم بر بنائے حکمت اللہ تعالیٰ کے اختیار سے ثابت ہوا ہے اور جو وجوب بالاختیار ثابت ہو اس سے اضطرار لازم نہیں آتا ، جیسا کہ اس کی تفصیل پہلے گذر چکی ہے۔ اس کی مزید توضیح متن نے اپنے حاشیہ میں بیان کی ہے۔ حاصله منع الاستلزام فان الثابت للبارى تعالى من الاختيار ما يقابل الاضطرار معنی یہ ہے کہ حسن و قبح عقلی ہونے کی تقدیر پر باری تعالیٰ کے لئے عدم اختیار کا استلزام ممنوع ہے کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کے لئے اضطرار کے بالمقابل اختیار ثابت ہے گرچہ طرف اول اس کی خود مشیت کی وجہ سے واجب ہے لیکن جب اس کے لئے طرف آخر میں قدرت و ممکن ثابت ہے تو اضطرار ( سلب قدرت ) ثابت نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اختیار ہی ثابت رہے گا اس لئے کہ اختیار، ان شاء فعل وان لم يشاء لم يفعل“ کے معنی میں ہے اس تعریف کے بموجب باری تعالیٰ نے مثلا جب فعل کو چاہا تو وہ فعل اسکی مشیت اور چاہنے کی وجہ سے واجب ہو گیا لیکن اس حیثیت سے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ اس فعل کے ترک کو چاہے تو ترک واجب ہو گا فعل نہیں، غرض مشیت فعل ، وجود ترک کو مانع ہوئی گر چہ اس کی شان سے ترک بھی ہے اس معنی کر کہ اگر وہ چاہے تو ترک بھی موجود ہوسکتا ہے پس ترک نظر کرتے ہوئے نفس قدرت کی طرف ممکن ہے اگر چہ مشیت فعل کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے ممتنع ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اضطرار اس وقت لازم آتا اگر فعل و ترک میں سے کوئی اس کے ارادہ واختیار کے بغیر صادر ہوتا جب کہ اس کی مشیت کے سبب سے جو وجوب فعل ثابت ہے وہ اختیار سے ہے اس لئے اضطرار لازم نہیں ۔ درج بالا جواب پر مصنف نے حاشیہ میں بایں الفاظ اعتراض کیا ہے۔
Matn of Muslim: And fourthly, if it were so, then the Exalted Creator would not be free in judgment, because a judgment contrary to the rational is bad/ugly. The answer: That His judgment being in accordance with wisdom does not necessitate compulsion. Translation: And (the Ash'aris) give a fourth proof that good and bad are not rational: if good and bad were rational, then Allah would no longer be free in judgment, because a judgment against the rational is bad. The answer is that His judgment's accordance with wisdom does not necessitate compulsion. Commentary: The author mentions the Ash'ari's fourth proof against rational good and bad. The summary of the proof: if good and bad are rational due to the essence of the act, or a real attribute, or a relational attribute, as the Mu'tazila and Hanafis say, then a severe impossibility follows: that Allah would not remain capable and free in His judgments of prohibition and obligation etc., but would become compelled and forced, and the necessary is false, so the necessitating is also false; thus rational good and bad is false. The connection: on the assumption of rational good and bad, giving a judgment contrary to the dictates of good and bad is against reason, and a judgment against reason is bad, and the occurrence of something bad from Allah is impossible. So for an act that is rationally bad, the judgment of prohibition, and for an act rationally good, the judgment of obligation would be necessary upon Allah, because a judgment contrary to what good/bad require is bad and impossible. Then when giving a judgment of prohibition in bad and obligation in good becomes necessary upon Allah, He would no longer be free in judgment, because necessity and obligation in the agent necessitate compulsion, and compulsion in the status of Allah is unanimously false. The answer: The text gives the answer: 'And the answer: That His judgment being in accordance with wisdom does not necessitate compulsion.' This is the response. The gist of the answer: The fact that Allah's judgment conforms to wisdom in light of the dictates of good and bad does not necessitate compulsion, because the obligation of judgment based on wisdom is established through Allah's choice, and what is established through choice does not necessitate compulsion, as has been detailed earlier. Further clarification is given in the margin. The gist: Denial of the implication: for the Exalted Creator, choice is established which is opposite to compulsion. The meaning: On the assumption of rational good and bad, the implication of lack of choice for Allah is denied, because choice opposite to compulsion is established for Allah. Even though one side is necessary due to His own will, but since the other side is possible for Him with power, compulsion (removal of power) is not established; rather choice remains established, because choice means 'if He wills He does, and if He does not will He does not do'. According to this definition, when Allah wills an act, that act becomes necessary due to His will and desiring, but from the aspect that if Allah wills its abandonment, then abandonment would be necessary and not the act. In short, the will of the act prevents the existence of abandonment, although from His status, abandonment also exists in the sense that if He wills, abandonment can also exist. So, considering abandonment, it is possible from the perspective of power itself, although considering the will of the act, it is impossible. The summary: Compulsion would follow if one of the act or its abandonment occurred without His intention and choice; whereas the obligation of the act that is established due to His will is through choice, therefore compulsion does not follow. The author has objected to the above answer in the margin with these words.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute concerning rational moral evaluation (husn wa qubh 'aqli). It presents the Ash'ari school's fourth argument against the Mu'tazili and Hanafi position that good and bad are rationally discernible, along with the Hanafi response. The Ash'ari argument is: If acts are inherently good or bad rationally, then Allah would be compelled to command the good and prohibit the bad, thus losing His free choice (ikhtiyār). Since compulsion (idtirār) is impossible for Allah, rational good/bad must be rejected. The Hanafi response, as articulated in the matn and commentary, denies the necessary implication. It explains that while Allah's judgment necessarily conforms to wisdom, this conformity is itself chosen by Allah through His will. The obligation of the ruling is based on wisdom but originates from Allah's choice; it is not an external constraint. Thus, He remains free (mukhtār) because He could will otherwise. The commentary elaborates that choice means the ability to do or not do; even if one side becomes necessary due to will, the other side remains possible in power, preserving the essential attribute of choice. The passage thus defends rational good/bad against the charge of compromising divine omnipotence.

Key Terms
حسن وقبح عقلی (ḥusn wa qubh 'aqlī): The quality of an act being good or bad discernible by reason independently of revelation.
اضطرار (iḍṭirār): Compulsion; lack of ability to choose otherwise; removed by the presence of power (qudra) over both alternatives.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): Freedom of choice; the attribute by which an agent may do or not do an act based on will and power.
استلزام (istilzām): Necessary implication; a logical consequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why does Allah's judgment being in accordance with wisdom not necessitate compulsion?
A) Because wisdom is an external constraint that limits divine power.
B) Because the obligation of the ruling is established through Allah's own choice and will, not from an external source.
C) Because Allah does not actually judge based on wisdom; it is just an appearance.
D) Because the Ash'ari argument is based on a false premise.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi response to the Ash'ari argument shows that divine freedom is preserved even when judgment accords with wisdom, because the necessity arises from divine will, not external compulsion.
