Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Obligation of Looking at Miracles: Refutation of Infinite Regress
Response to Mu'tazili argument on obligation of looking at miracles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of wujub nafs al-amrī and evaluate how it resolves the Mu'tazili infinite regress argument regarding the obligation to look at miracles.

Core Idea
The obligation to look at miracles is ontologically fixed (nafs al-amrī) and does not depend on the subject's act of looking, thus no infinite regress arises.

In this lesson, we examine a classic usul al-fiqh debate: Must a person look at a miracle to recognize prophethood, and does the obligation itself require an infinite chain of looks? The Mu'tazila argued that such an obligation leads to infinite regress, making it impossible. The Hanafi response introduces the concept of wujub nafs al-amrī, an obligation fixed in reality independent of the subject's awareness. This lesson walks through the argument, refutation, and subsequent objection regarding obligating the heedless (taklif al-ghafil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Recognize that the Mu'tazila claim the obligation of looking at miracles requires a prior look to know the obligation, leading to infinite regress, while the Hanafis reject this.
2
Understand the Hanafi response: wujub nafs al-amrī
Grasp the concept that the obligation is fixed in reality (nafs al-amr) and does not depend on the subject's actual looking or knowledge.
This is the key principle that blocks regress.
3
Analyze the objection of taklif al-ghafil
Note the Mu'tazili-inspired objection: Isn't this obligating the heedless? The Hanafi distinction between heedlessness of conception (tasawwur) vs. confirmation (tasdiq) provides the answer.
The person can understand the address even if he does not affirm it.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
See how the ruling differs: Hanafis hold the disbeliever sinful for not looking even if unaware; Mu'tazila argue no sin if ignorant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر مکلف منکر نے رسول سے کہا کہ میں معجزہ میں نظر نہیں کرونگا اس لئے کہ وہ غیر واجب ہے اس پر نبی نے کہا تم پر عقلا نظر وفکر واجب ہے پس اگر اس کے جواب میں مکلف نے یہ کہا کہ یہ ایسا نظری مسئلہ ہے جس کے لئے دوسرے نظر کی ضرورت ہے اور دوسرا بھی نظری ہے تو اس کے لئے تیسری نظر کی ضرورت ہے علی ھذا القیاس الی غیر انھا یہ نظر کا تسلسل جاری رہے گا اور جس چیز کے وجوب کا علم مجھے نہ ہو اس کے حصول کی خاطر انظار غیر متناہیہ کے حصول کا مجھے موقع اور وقت نہیں ہے کہ میں وجوب نظر فی المعجزات کو جان سکوں لہذا اس صورت میں بھی انجام رسول لا زم آئے گا۔
جواب :۔ جواب شبہ یہ ہے کہ انظار کا سلسلہ غیر متناحیہ تک پہونچنا باطل ہے پس مکلف کے لئے اس نظر صحیح تک منتھی لازم ہے جو مفید علم ہو اور شئی کی حجت بن سکے لہذا مکلف کو مجال عند ر نہیں ہے اس لئے انجام رسول لا زم نہ آئے گا۔
قوله والجواب انا لانسلم أن الوجوب الخ
مندرجہ بالا عبارت سے ماتن نے معتزلہ کی دلیل کا جواب دیا ہے یہ جواب علامہ ابن حاجب وغیرہ علمائے اصول کے طرز پر واقع ہے چنانچہ قاضی عضد نے شرح مختصر میں تقریر کی ہے کہ معتزلہ کی دلیل کا مقدمہ ثانیہ یعنی النظر لا یجب عالم انظر پر منع وارد ہے منع کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ معتزلہ کا یہ کہنا کہ وجوب النظر فی انجز و موقوف ہے نظر فی المعجزہ پر ہمکو تسلیم نہیں ہے کیونکہ کسی شٹی کے علم کے لئے اور ناظر کے پاس اس شئی کے علم کے ثبوت وحصول کے لئے نظر کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے مگر نفس الامر میں کسی شئی کے علم یا تحقیق کے لئے نظر کی چنداں ضرروت نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور وجوب نظر فی المعجزات ہمارے نزدیک نفس الامری ہے یعنی معجزہ میں نظر کا وجوب نفس الامر میں شرع سے ثابت ہے اب خواہ مکلف معجزہ میں نظر کرے خواہ نظر نہ کرے۔ چاہے شریعت اس کے نزدیک ثابت ہو چاہے نہ ثابت ہو بہر حال وجوب ثابت رہے گا کیونکہ وجوب نفس الامری کا تحقق مکلف کے علم بالوجوب پر موقوف نہیں رہتا اس لئے کہ اگر وجوب نفس الامری کا تعلق مکلف کے علم بالوجوب پر موقوف ہونے لگے تو دور لازم آئے گا کہ علم بالوجوب فی نفس الامر موقوف ہے وجوب فی نفس الامر سے تعلق پر ۔
قوله - وليس ذالك من تكليف الغافل فانه الخ
ماتن کے مندرجہ بالا جواب پر ایک شبہ وارد ہوتا ہے اس عبارت سے ماتن نے اس شبہ کا جواب دیا ہے۔ شبہ اور جواب شبہ دونوں ذیل میں ملاحظہ ہو۔
شبہ :۔ یہ ہے کہ وجوب نظر کو نفس الامری قرار دینا تکلیف غافل کے قبیل سے ہے اسلئے کہ وجوب نظر کا پابند و مکلف بنانا ایسے مکلف کو جو نہ شارع کو جانتا ہے نہ ہی وجوب کو جانتا ہے یقینا تکلیف غافل ہے اور تکلیف غافل جائز نہیں۔
جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ کسی عاقل بالغ شخص کو وجوب نفس الامری یا وجوب نظر کا پابند بنانا اور مکلف گردانا، نائم، مجنون ، اور صبی غیر عاقل و غیر هم غافلین کی طرح مکلف بنانے کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ نائم و مجنون وغیرہ خطاب کو نہیں سمجھتے ہیں مگر اول الذکر عاقل بالغ مکلف خطاب نازل کو سمجھ سکتا ہے گرچہ وہ اس کی تصدیق نہیں کرتا مگر یہ مضر نہیں کیونکہ حق تکلیف کے لئے تصدیق تکلیف شرط بھی نہیں ہے حاصل یہ کہ جو تصور سے غافل ہے اس کو مکلف بنا نا صیح نہیں لیکن جو تصدیق سے غافل ہو اس کو مکلف بنا نا صحیح ہے اور صورت محجو شہ میں یہی صورت متحقق ہے اس لئے شبہ کا لعدم ہے۔
قوله اقول لوقال لاامتثل مالم اعلم وجوب الخ
اس عبارت سے ماتن نے معتزلہ کی دلیل مذکور کو دوسرے انداز میں پیش کیا ہے تا کہ اس پر وجوب نفس الامری کا اعتراض نہ پڑے۔ دلیل : کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہمکو تسلیم ہے کہ وجوب نظر نفس الامر میں نظر پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا لیکن اس میں شک نہیں کہ مکلف وجوب نظر کو تو امر رسول ہی سے جانے گا۔ چنانچہ جس وقت نبی نے مکلف سے کہا معجزہ کو دیکھو اس لئے کہ نفس الامر میں تمپر نظر واجب ہے پس اسپر مکلف نے کہالا امتثل امرک بالنظر مالم اعلم بوجوب الامتثال ( یعنی میں آپ کے حکم نظر کی پیروی نہیں کروں گا جب تک میں وجوب امتثال کو نہ جان لوں اس لئے کہ مکلف کو جس چیز کے وجوب کا علم نہ ہو اس کو اس امر سے رکنا جائز ہے لہذا اسکو معجزہ میں نظر کرنے سے رکنا یا معجزہ میں نظر نہ کرنا جائز ہے کہ وہ وجوب نظر کو نہیں جانتا ہے ) پھر مکلف نے کہا اور مجھے وجوب امتثال کا علم اس وقت ہو گا جیتکہ کہ میں آپ کے امر نظر کی پیروی نہ کر
If the denier obligated person said to the Messenger: 'I will not look at the miracle because it is not obligatory,' then the Prophet said: 'Rational contemplation and reflection are obligatory upon you.' Then if the obligated person replied: 'This is a theoretical issue that requires another look, and the second is also theoretical, so it requires a third look, and so on ad infinitum — this chain of looks will continue, and I have no opportunity or time to obtain infinite looks in order to know the obligation of looking at the miracles. Therefore, even in this case, the consequence of the Messenger will follow.' Answer: The answer to the doubt is that the chain of looks reaching infinity is invalid. So the obligated person must stop at the correct look that provides knowledge and can serve as proof for the thing. Thus the obligated person has no recourse, so the consequence of the Messenger will not follow. His statement: 'And the answer is: We do not concede that the obligation...' Through the above passage, the author (al-matn) answered the Mu'tazila's proof. This answer is along the lines of Allamah Ibn Hajib and other scholars of usul. Accordingly, Qadi 'Adud stated in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that the second premise of the Mu'tazila's proof — i.e., 'looking is not obligated upon the knower of the looked-at thing' — is refuted. The explanation of the refutation is that we do not concede the Mu'tazila's claim that the obligation of looking at miracles depends on looking at the miracle, because for the knowledge of something and for the existence and acquisition of knowledge of that thing in the viewer, looking is needed. However, in reality (fi nafs al-amr), looking is not so necessary for the knowledge or verification of something. And in our view, the obligation of looking at miracles is nafs al-amrī (ontological), meaning the obligation of looking at the miracle is established in reality (nafs al-amr) by the Shari'ah, whether the obligated person looks at the miracle or not, whether the Shari'ah is established for him or not — in any case the obligation remains established, because the realization of nafs al-amrī obligation does not depend on the obligated person's knowledge of the obligation. For if the nafs al-amrī obligation depended on the obligated person's knowledge of the obligation, then circularity would follow: knowledge of the obligation in reality depends on the connection to the obligation in reality. His statement: 'And this is not from the category of obligating the heedless, for indeed...' On the above answer of the author, a doubt arises; through this phrase the author answers that doubt. The doubt and its answer are noted below. Doubt: Declaring the obligation of looking to be nafs al-amrī is from the category of obligating the heedless (taklif al-ghafil), because making an obligated person bound to the obligation of looking while he neither knows the Lawgiver nor knows the obligation is certainly obligating the heedless, and obligating the heedless is not permissible. Answer: This is that making a sane adult person bound to the nafs al-amrī obligation or the obligation of looking, and considering him obliged, is not of the same category as making the sleeping, insane, or non-sane child and similar heedless persons obliged, because the sleeping, insane, etc. do not understand the address (khitab), whereas the aforementioned sane adult obliged person can understand the revealed address, even if he does not confirm it, but this is not harmful, because for the right of obligation, confirmation of obligation is not even a condition. The conclusion is that one who is heedless of conception (tasawwur) cannot be rightly made obliged, but one who is heedless of confirmation (tasdiq) can be rightly made obliged, and in the disputed case this very situation is realized, so the doubt is nonexistent. His statement: 'I say: If he said, I will not comply as long as I do not know the obligation...' Through this phrase, the author presents the aforementioned Mu'tazila proof in a different style so that the objection of nafs al-amrī obligation does not fall upon it. The gist of the proof is: We concede that the obligation of looking in reality does not depend on looking, but there is no doubt that the obligated person will know the obligation of looking only through the command of the Messenger. Thus, when the Prophet said to the obligated person: 'Look at the miracle, because looking is obligatory upon you in reality,' then the obligated person said: 'I do not comply with your command to look as long as I do not know the obligation of compliance' (i.e., I will not follow your command to look until I know the obligation of compliance, because it is permissible for the obligated person to refrain from a thing whose obligation he does not know. Therefore, it is permissible for him to refrain from looking at the miracle or not to look, since he does not know the obligation of looking). Then the obligated person said: 'And I will know the obligation of compliance only when I do not follow your command to look...'
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This lesson presents a key usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafis and the Mu'tazila regarding the obligation of contemplating miracles (al-nazar fi al-mu'jizat). The author (al-matn) refutes the Mu'tazili argument that leads to an infinite regress of looks (tasalsul al-anzar). The Mu'tazila argued that if looking at a miracle is obligatory to know its miraculous nature, then one would need an infinite chain of looks to establish the obligation itself. The Hanafi response, as explained by the commentator, is that the obligation of looking is nafs al-amrī (fixed in reality) and does not depend on the subject's act of looking. Therefore, the obligation is intrinsic and not subject to infinite regress. A further objection is raised: that declaring such an obligation amounts to 'obligating the heedless' (taklif al-ghafil), since the person may not know the Lawgiver or the obligation. The Hanafi response distinguishes between heedlessness of conception (tasawwur) and heedlessness of confirmation (tasdiq). The person is capable of understanding the address (khitab) even if he does not confirm it; thus it is not taklif al-ghafil. Finally, the author re-presents the Mu'tazili argument in a way that avoids the earlier refutation, but the overall Hanafi position stands: the obligation is real and known through the Prophet's command, and the person's lack of knowledge does not negate the obligation.

Key Terms
النظر (al-nazar): Contemplation or reflective looking, especially at miracles to recognize prophethood.
الوجوب النفس الامري (al-wujub al-nafs al-amrī): An obligation that is fixed in reality (nafs al-amr), independent of the subject's knowledge or actual compliance.
تكليف الغافل (taklif al-ghafil): Obligating a person who is totally heedless and incapable of understanding the address.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why does the Mu'tazili argument of infinite regress (tasalsul al-anzar) fail?
A) Because the chain of looks terminates at the first look that provides knowledge.
B) Because the obligation of looking is in reality and does not depend on the subject's looking.
C) Because the Messenger's command itself is sufficient without any need for looking.
D) Because the Mu'tazila concede the point after rational debate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi concept of wujub nafs al-amrī resolves the infinite regress problem and establishes that obligations can be real even without the subject's awareness.

Refuting Takleef al-Ghafil: The Hanafi Defense of Wujub Nazar
Doubt and rebuttal on wujub nazar as takleef al-ghafil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between ghafla an al-tasawwur and ghafla an al-tasdiq to refute the claim that obligating nazar is takleef al-ghafil.

Core Idea
Takleef is valid if the mukallaf can understand the address, even without affirming it.

The Hanafi school holds that the obligation of nazar (rational inquiry into divine truths) is established objectively (nafs al-amr) and does not depend on the mukallaf's knowledge or acceptance. The Mu'tazila object that this is takleef al-ghafil (obligating the unaware), which is unjust. In this passage, the author responds by distinguishing two kinds of unawareness: one that invalidates takleef (ignorance of the concept) and one that does not (ignorance of the duty itself). Understanding this distinction is key to appreciating the Hanafi theory of takleef.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazili objection
Read the doubt presented: the Mu'tazila claim that making a mukallaf who knows neither the Shari' nor the obligation bound to wujub nazar is takleef al-ghafil, which is invalid.
Takleef al-ghafil is generally considered unjust by the Mu'tazila because it imposes a duty on someone incapable of knowing it.
2
Locate the Hanafi response's key distinction
The author distinguishes two types of unawareness: unawareness of the concept (tasawwur) and unawareness of affirmation (tasdiq). Identify which one the Mu'tazila conflate and which the Hanafis argue does not invalidate takleef.
The distinction is rational (aqlī), not textual.
3
Understand the condition for valid takleef
The Hanafi position: takleef requires the mukallaf to have the capacity to understand the address (ahliyyat al-adam), not necessarily to accept or affirm it. A sane adult, even if he rejects the obligation, can still be addressed.
This is based on the principle that 'the obligation exists in nafs al-amr regardless of the mukallaf's knowledge'.
4
Apply the distinction to the case of nazar
The person who does not yet know the Shari' is unaware of the affirmation (tasdiq) of the obligation, but he has the capacity to conceive (tasawwur) of a Creator and obligation. Therefore, the objection fails.
The practical result: obligation is actual for every sane adult from the moment of reason, not from the moment of belief.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
For Hanafis, an atheist who has never heard of Islam is still obligated to believe (nazar) once he reaches maturity and possesses reason. For Mu'tazila, such a person cannot be obligated until he receives the message and knows the Obliger.
This affects discussions about the fate of non-Muslims who die before receiving the call (the so-called 'People of the Fatrah').

Source Text

قوله - وليس ذالك من تكليف الغافل فانه الخ
ماتن کے مندرجہ بالا جواب پر ایک شبہ وارد ہوتا ہے اس عبارت سے ماتن نے اس شبہ
کا جواب دیا ہے۔ شبہ اور جواب شبہ دونوں ذیل میں ملاحظہ ہو۔
شبہ :۔ یہ ہے کہ وجوب نظر کو نفس الامری قرار دینا تکلیف غافل کے قبیل سے ہے اسلئے کہ وجوب نظر کا پابند و مکلف بنانا ایسے مکلف کو جو نہ شارع کو جانتا ہے نہ ہی وجوب کو جانتا ہے یقینا تکلیف غافل ہے اور تکلیف غافل جائز نہیں۔
جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ کسی عاقل بالغ شخص کو وجوب نفس الامری یا وجوب نظر کا پابند بنانا اور مکلف گردانا، نائم، مجنون ، اور صبی غیر عاقل و غیر هم غافلین کی طرح مکلف بنانے کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ نائم و مجنون وغیرہ خطاب کو نہیں سمجھتے ہیں مگر اول الذکر عاقل بالغ مکلف خطاب نازل کو سمجھ سکتا ہے گرچہ وہ اس کی تصدیق نہیں کرتا مگر یہ مضر نہیں کیونکہ حق تکلیف کے لئے تصدیق تکلیف شرط بھی نہیں ہے حاصل یہ کہ جو تصور سے غافل ہے اس کو مکلف بنا نا صیح نہیں لیکن جو تصدیق سے غافل ہو اس کو مکلف بنا نا صحیح ہے اور صورت محجو شہ میں یہی صورت متحقق ہے اس لئے شبہ کا لعدم ہے۔
He said: 'And that is not from takleef al-ghafil...' etc. A doubt arises on the matn's above answer. With this expression, the matn has responded to that doubt. The doubt and its answer are presented below.

Doubt: That declaring wujub nazar as al-amr al-nafsi is from the category of takleef al-ghafil. Because making a mukallaf obligated to wujub nazar who knows neither the Shari' nor the obligation is certainly takleef al-ghafil, and takleef al-ghafil is not permissible.

Answer: That making a sane adult person obligated to wujub al-amr al-nafsi or wujub nazar and considering him mukallaf is not from the category of making obligated like the sleeping, insane, and non-rational child and other such ghaflis. Because the sleeping, insane, etc. do not understand the address. But the aforementioned sane adult mukallaf can understand the descending address even if he does not affirm it. But this is not harmful, because affirmation of the obligation is not a condition for the right of takleef. The conclusion is that one who is unaware of the conception (tasawwur) cannot be made obligated, but one who is unaware of affirmation (tasdiq) can be made obligated. And in the case at hand, this situation is realized. So the doubt is void.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the Hanafi author and the Mu'tazila regarding the nature of wujub nazar. The Mu'tazila argue that wujub nazar being established as an objective and mind-independent (nafs al-amr) obligation constitutes takleef al-ghafil, which is invalid because the mukallaf is ignorant of both the Obliger and the obligation. The Hanafi response distinguishes two types of unawareness: unawareness of the concept (tasawwur) which makes takleef invalid, and unawareness of affirmation (tasdiq) which does not. A sane adult, even if he does not affirm the obligation, has the capacity to understand the address, so obligating him is not like obligating the sleeping or insane. The Mu'tazili objection conflates these two types. The author thus defends the validity of takleef in this context.

Key Terms
تکلیف غافل (takleef al-ghafil): Imposing an obligation on a person who is unaware of the obligation's existence or the obliger.
تصور (tasawwur): Conceptualization or mental representation; the ability to conceive of something.
تصدیق (tasdiq): Affirmation or assent; accepting a proposition as true.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, which of the following best explains why obligating nazar is not takleef al-ghafil?
A) The mukallaf knows the Shari' even if he does not affirm it.
B) The mukallaf has the capacity to understand the address even if he does not affirm it.
C) The obligation only applies after the mukallaf receives revelation.
D) The Mu'tazila do not understand the concept of nafs al-amr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates takleef based on capacity (tasawwur) rather than affirmation (tasdiq), thereby refuting the Mu'tazili claim that an objective obligation of nazar constitutes takleef al-ghafil.

Dispute on Viewing Miracles: Wujub 'Adah vs. Wujub 'Aqli
Refuting Ash'ari and Mu'tazila arguments on viewing miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to DISTINGUISH the Hanafi concept of wujub 'adah from the Mu'tazili wujub 'aqli and STATE the rational proof based on human nature.

Core Idea
A prophet's miracle compels viewing by divine custom, not rational obligation — human nature ensures it.

In this passage, the author defends the Hanafi-Ash'ari position that viewing a prophet's miracle is obligatory by Allah's established custom, not by rational necessity. He refutes two opposing arguments: the Ash'ari claim that mere probability of obligation suffices, and the Mu'tazili claim that Allah is rationally bound to show the miracle. Through a compelling analogy of a predator warning, he demonstrates that human nature drives us to look when warned of harm, especially eternal harm from a truthful prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State the Hanafi/Ash'ari position (wajib 'adah), the Mu'tazili position (wajib 'aqli), and the specific Ash'ari argument being refuted (probability of obligation suffices).
2
Analyze the first Ash'ari claim
The Ash'ari claim is that a mere probability of obligation is enough to obligate looking. The author rejects this: if obligation is religious (shar'i), reason cannot determine it, leading to an infinite regress.
3
Examine the second Ash'ari response
The gloss (hashiya) presents the argument from human nature (jiblah insaniyyah): any rational person naturally looks when warned of harm, as shown by the predator analogy.
This response is considered excellent but ultimately refers back to the author's correct view.
4
Contrast the Mu'tazili proof
The Mu'tazila argue that Allah is rationally obligated (wajib 'aqli) to show the miracle based on lutf (grace) and al-salah (the best course).
They hold that Allah must do what is best for His servants.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi/Ash'ari response: Allah is not bound by rational obligations; rather, His custom (sunnah ilahiyyah) ensures the miracle is seen inevitably, without any need for a verbal command to look.
This is the doctrine of wujub 'adah (obligation by custom).

احتمال سے نہ بچے۔ مصنف اشاعرہ کے خیال کا رد کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے ہیں کہ احتمال وجوب، وجوب نظر کے لئے کافی ہے اور اگر تسلیم کر لیتے ہیں پھر بھی تم اشاعرہ کے لئے مفید و کافی نہیں اسلئے کہ احتمال وجوب کا تحقق قضیہ عقل سے ہے اور جب حکم تمہارے نزدیک حکم شرعی ہے تو عقل کو اس میں کیونکر مداخلت ہوگی لہذا اس صورت میں علم وجوب کے لئے سوائے امتثال امر شارع کے کوئی اور چارہ نہیں رہ جاتا ہے تو مکلف شارع پر حجت قائم کر لے گا اور اس طرح انجام رسول لازم آئے گا۔ قوله فى الحاشية " ولوقيل ان الجبلة الانسانيه الخ مصنف کی دلیل کا اشاعرہ کی طرف سے دوسرا جواب ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ نبی کے معجزہ کا حکم دینے پر مکلف کا یہ کہنا انظر ولا امتثل مالم اعلم الوجوب تعنت وعناد پر مبنی ہے۔ اور راہ حق وصواب سے کجروی کی طرف مقتضی ہے اس لئے کہ وجوب وغیرہ جملہ احکام اگر چہ اس تقدیر پر شرعی ہیں مگر اشاعرہ وحنفیہ مصالح ومضار اور صفت کمال ونقصان کا عقلی طور پر اور اک کئے جانے کو انکار نہیں کرتے کہ حسن وفتح کا یہ دونوں معنی بالا تفاق عقلی ہے پس اشاعرہ و حنفیہ کے نزدیک بھی عقل اتنی سی بات کا بخوبی ادراک کر سکتی ہے کہ وہ مخبر صادق جن کے احوال و آثار سے صدق عیاں اور ظاہر ہے مضرت ابدیہ سے احتراز کی خبر دے رہے ہیں تو ایسے میں ہر عاقل کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ ان کے کلام میں اور ان چیزوں میں جو انکی صداقت پر دال ہونظر کرے پھر اس کی صداقت وحقانیت واضح ہو جانے کے بعد مضرت ابدیہ کے دفعیہ کی کوشش کرے اگر مکلف ایسے مخبر صادق کی خبر پر دھیان نہیں دیتا ہے اور یہ کہتے ہوئے راہ فرار اختیار کرلے کہ میں تمہارے کلام میں نظر نہ کرونگا جب تک مجھ پر تمہاری اتباع لازم نہ ہو گی تو ایسے شخص کو اہل عقل، عناد و حماقت کی طرف منسوب کرتے ہیں اس لئے کہ ہر عاقل پر لازم ہے کہ مصلحت کو طلب کرے اور مضرت سے احتراز کرے بلکہ جبلت انسانیہ اس پر پیدا ہی کی گئی ہے کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے کسی سے کہا کہ درندہ تمہارے پیچھے ہے تو وہ شخص اپنے پیچھے ضرور نظر کرتا ہے جب کہ کہنے والا عام شخص ہوتا ہے اور دنیا کی ادنی ہلاکت کے احتمالی سبب کے بارے میں خبر دے رہا ہے تو ہر شخص اس درندہ سے بچنے کی فکر کرتا ہے تو تمہارا کیا خیال ہے اس شخص کی خبر کے بارے میں جس کا صدق ظاہر وواضح ہے وہ بھی ایسی خبر دے رہا ہے جس کا تعلق آخرت کے عذاب اکبر سے ہے اس پر نہیں غور کرے گا مگر وہی شخص جسکے نصیبے میں دائی شقاوت لکھی ہے۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ اشاعرہ کا یہ جواب اس بحث میں بہت عمدہ تصور کیا جاتا ہے مگر حق یہ ہے کہ یہ جواب میرے جواب حق کی طرف راجع ہے۔ جو درج ذیل ہے قوله. والحق أن اراء ة المعجزات واجبة الخ اس عبارت سے معتزلہ کی دلیل کا جواب باصواب دیا ہے۔ دلیل : - کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دلیل و نظر کی طرف دیکھتے ہوئے اگر چہ انجام رسول جائز ہے تا ہم اللہ تعالی اس جواز کو کبھی واقع نہیں فرماتا کہ نبی معجزہ دکھاتے وقت ایک مکلف سے عاجز وساکت ہو جائے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ پر مکلف کو نبی کا معجزہ دکھانا بر قاعدہ اعتزال عقلاً اور برمذہب اہل حق عادۃ واجب ہے چنانچہ معتزلہ کہتے ہیں کہ عباد کے حق میں اللہ پر لطف واجب ہے لطف سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ امر جو بندہ کو قبائح سے دور رکھے اور حسنات کو پہچنوائے اللہ پر عقلاً واجب ہے اور اس کے برخلاف اشاعرہ و حنفیہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ امر اللہ پر عادۃ واجب ہے عادہ واجب ہونے کا معنی یہ ہے کہ سنت الہیہ اس پر جاری ہے کہ جب اس کی مشیت و مرضی کے مطابق کسی نبی کی بعثت ہوتی ہے تو نبی کے معجزہ کو وہ دیکھا کر ہی چھوڑتا ہے گرچہ مکلف اپنے تئیں لاکھ کوشش کرے کہ معجزہ نہ دیکھے گا لیکن اس کی یہ کوشش ناکام ہوتی ہے کہ اللہ نے معجزہ کو دکھانا اپنے ذمہ کرم پر واجب فرما لیا ہے اس لئے مکلف بالضرور اس کو دیکھتا ہے اس طرح اس شخص کے نزدیک نبی کی نبوت کا دعوی سچا ہو کر رہتا ہے جیسے کہ ہر ناظر و تعلم کو نظر کے بعد علم عادی و جو بی بلا اختیار بالضرورة حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ ہے کہ معجزہ صادر کرتے وقت نبی کو یہ حاجت ہی نہیں رہتی کہ وہ مکلف سے کہے انظر فی معجزتی۔ بلکہ ان کا کام صرف معجزہ صادر کر دینا ہے اور بس ! اسی سے مکلف کو بالضرورت رویت حاصل ہو جاتی ہے مزید نی کو انظرفی مجزتی کہنے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں پڑتی کہ انجام واسکات لازم آئے۔ اقول : اولا۔ نبی کے معجزہ اور امر خارق عادات صادر فرمانے کے وقت مکلف کو اس کی طرف نظر کرنا طبعاً واجب ہے۔ چونکہ عام مشاہدہ و تجربہ سے یہ بات پائے ثبوت کو پہونچ چکی ہے کہ جب کوئی ساحر ومفتری اور کا ہن کوئی حیرت انگیز کرتب دکھاتا ہے تو جہاں تک اس کے کرتب دکھانے کی
(The text continues the dispute). The author, refuting the Ash'ari view, says: We do not accept that probability of obligation is sufficient for the obligation of looking. And even if we accept, it is not useful for you Ash'aris because the realization of probability of obligation is a rational matter, and when according to you the ruling is a religious ruling, how can reason interfere? Therefore, in this case, for knowledge of obligation there is no recourse except acting upon the command of the Lawgiver. Then the obligated person will establish the proof against the Lawgiver, and thus the consequence of silence (of the prophet) would necessarily follow. His statement in the gloss 'And if it is said that human nature...' is the second response from the Ash'aris to the author's proof. Its summary is that the obligated person's saying 'Look, but I will not obey until I know the obligation' is based on stubbornness and obstinacy, and leads to deviation from the path of truth and right. Because all judgments, even if on this account are religious, but Ash'aris and Hanafis do not deny that benefits and harms and the attribute of perfection and deficiency are rational, and also do not deny that such things are acknowledged, because both meanings of beauty and conquest are unanimously rational. Therefore, according to Ash'aris and Hanafis, reason can perfectly understand this much: that the truthful informer, whose truthfulness is evident from his states and signs, is informing about avoiding eternal harm. So in such a case, it is necessary for every rational person to look into his words and into those things that indicate his truthfulness. Then after his truthfulness and correctness become clear, he should strive to avoid eternal harm. If the obligated person does not pay attention to the news of such a truthful informer and chooses the path of escape by saying 'I will not look into your words until following you becomes obligatory upon me', then people of intellect attribute such a person to obstinacy and foolishness. Because it is necessary for every rational person to seek benefit and avoid harm. Rather, human nature has been created for this. Do you not see that if a person says to someone 'a predator is behind you', that person will definitely look behind him, even though the speaker is an ordinary person and is informing about a probable cause of the slightest worldly destruction. Then every person strives to avoid that predator. So what is your opinion about the news of that person whose truthfulness is apparent and clear, and he is also giving such news which relates to the greatest punishment of the Hereafter? Will he not ponder over it? Only that person whose lot is written with eternal wretchedness. The author says that this response of the Ash'aris is considered very excellent in this discussion, but the truth is that this response refers back to my correct response which follows. He said: 'And the truth is that seeing the miracles is obligatory...' With this expression, a correct answer is given to the evidence of the Mu'tazila. The summary of the evidence is that by looking at the evidence and reasoning, even if the consequence of silence of the prophet is possible, but Allah Most High never actualizes this possibility, that when the prophet shows a miracle the obligated person becomes powerless and silent. Because showing the miracle to the obligated person is obligatory upon Allah: according to the Mu'tazila rationally, and according to the school of Ahl al-Haqq by custom. Thus, the Mu'tazila say that kindness (lutf) is obligatory upon Allah with respect to His servants. By kindness is meant that which keeps the servant away from evil deeds and makes him recognize good deeds; it is rationally obligatory upon Allah. In contrast, the Ash'aris and Hanafis say that this is obligatory upon Allah by custom. The meaning of being obligatory by custom is that the divine practice is such that when, according to His will and pleasure, a prophet is sent, then the miracle of the prophet will inevitably be seen. Even if the obligated person tries his utmost that he will not see the miracle, but his effort fails because Allah has made showing the miracle obligatory upon His grace. Therefore, the obligated person necessarily sees it. Thus, according to this person, the claim of prophethood of the prophet becomes true. Just as for every observer and learner, after seeing, acquired knowledge (al-ilm al-adi) necessarily comes unintentionally. The summary is that at the time of producing the miracle, the prophet has no need to say to the obligated person 'Look at my miracle'. Rather, his work is only to produce the miracle, and that's it! From this, the obligated person necessarily gains the vision. There is no need for the prophet to even say 'Look at my miracle' such that the consequence of silence would have to follow. I say: First, at the time when the prophet produces the miracle and the extraordinary thing, it is naturally obligatory for the obligated person to look at it. Because common observation and experience have established that when a sorcerer, impostor, or soothsayer shows some amazing trick, as far as the display of his trick is concerned.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
**Passage Type:** Inter-school dispute (Hanafi/Ash'ari vs. Mu'tazila) concerning the obligation to view prophetic miracles, with a rational proof based on human nature.

**Author's Refutation of Ash'ari:** The author first rejects the Ash'ari claim that a mere probability of obligation is sufficient to obligate looking at a miracle. He argues that if obligation is religious (shar'i), reason cannot determine it; therefore the obligated person would have no basis to act until the obligation is known, leading to the absurd conclusion that the prophet would be silenced.

**Second Ash'ari Response (from the gloss):** The Ash'aris counter that it is human nature (jiblah insaniyyah) to seek benefit and avoid harm. A truthful informer warning of eternal harm compels any rational person to look and investigate. Using the analogy of being warned about a predator, the author argues that even ordinary news prompts action; how much more so when the informer is a prophet whose truthfulness is evident. The author notes that this Ash'ari response is excellent but ultimately refers back to his own correct view.

**Hanafi/Mu'tazila Dispute on Obligation:** The core dispute is whether it is rationally obligatory (wajib 'aqli, Mu'tazila) or customarily obligatory (wajib 'adah, Ash'ari/Hanafi) for Allah to show miracles. The Mu'tazila base their view on the principle of lutf (grace) and al-salah (the best course). The Hanafi/Ash'ari position holds that Allah is not under any rational obligation; rather, His established custom (sunnah ilahiyyah) ensures that the miracle is seen inevitably, without the need for a separate command to look.

**Author's Conclusion:** The miracle itself compels the observer to look; there is no need for the prophet to request 'Look at my miracle.' This is proven by common experience: any extraordinary feat naturally draws attention.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar): Looking or reflecting upon the miracle of a prophet to recognize his truthfulness.
وجوب عادۃ (wujub 'adah): Obligation by divine custom (sunnah), meaning Allah's consistent practice that the miracle will be seen.
لطف (lutf): The act by which Allah keeps servants away from evil and leads them to good, considered rationally obligatory by Mu'tazila.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does the obligated person necessarily see the prophet's miracle?
A) Because the prophet commands him to look.
B) Because it is rationally obligatory upon Allah to show it.
C) Because Allah's custom (sunnah) ensures the miracle is seen inevitably.
D) Because the obligated person chooses to look voluntarily.

Key Takeaway
Viewing a prophetic miracle is wajib 'adah (obligatory by divine custom), not wajib 'aqli, as proven by the natural human tendency to avoid harm when warned by a truthful source.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
The Obligation of Witnessing Miracles: Mu'tazila vs. Ash'ari/Hanafi
Dispute over whether witnessing miracles is rationally or habitually obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between rational and habitual obligation in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and apply the concept of 'adah to the issue of witnessing miracles.

Core Idea
Hanafi/Ash'ari: witnessing miracles is habitual, not rational, obligation—natural inclination suffices.

The Mu'tazila argued that Allah must rationally grant grace (lutf) to ensure people witness miracles, otherwise prophets could fail. The Ash'ari and Hanafi schools countered that human nature and Allah's custom make witnessing inevitable, without any rational necessity. This lesson unpacks that classical usul dispute and its implications for understanding obligation in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue and positions
State the dispute: Mu'tazila claim witnessing miracles is rationally obligatory on Allah (wajib bi al-'aql) via lutf; Ash'ari/Hanafi say it is habitually obligatory (wajib bi al-'adah) based on divine custom and human nature.
Both agree on the outcome (obligation), but differ on the basis.
2
Analyze the Mu'tazila proof
Examine the Mu'tazila argument: Allah must grant grace (lutf) to remove obstacles, otherwise the prophet might fail if people refuse to look. This is rationally necessary.
Lutf is defined as that which keeps the servant from evil and leads to good.
3
Examine the Hanafi/Ash'ari response
Understand the counter-argument: (1) Human nature naturally compels people to look at astonishing things (analogy with sorcerers). (2) The prophet's impeccable character and societal context ensure attention. (3) Allah's custom (sunnat Allah) guarantees that the miracle is seen without a command.
The prophet does not need to say 'Look at my miracle'; the miracle itself suffices.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify practical difference: According to Mu'tazila, if a person refuses to look, the prophet would need to command, risking failure (ta'jiz). According to Hanafis, no command is needed; refusal is unnatural and blameworthy, but the prophet's success is guaranteed by Allah's custom.
This affects how we understand the role of miracles in proving prophethood.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author (Hanafi/Ash'ari) concludes that the Mu'tazila's rational obligation is unproven and their fear of the prophet's failure is groundless. The habitual/customary obligation is sufficient and aligns with observable human behavior.
The dispute is rooted in differing views on the nature of obligation: rational vs. customary.

اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۲۶۱
رہا ہے جس کا تعلق آخرت کے عذاب اکبر سے ہے اس پر نہیں غور کرے گا مگر وہی شخص جسکے نصیبے میں دائی شقاوت لکھی ہے۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ اشاعرہ کا یہ جواب اس بحث میں بہت عمدہ تصور کیا جاتا ہے مگر حق یہ ہے کہ یہ جواب میرے جواب حق کی طرف راجع ہے۔ جو درج ذیل ہے
قوله. والحق أن رؤية المعجزات واجبة الخ
اس عبارت سے معتزلہ کی دلیل کا جواب باصواب دیا ہے۔
دلیل : - کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دلیل و نظر کی طرف دیکھتے ہوئے اگر چہ انجام رسول جائز ہے تا ہم اللہ تعالی اس جواز کو کبھی واقع نہیں فرماتا کہ نبی معجزہ دکھاتے وقت ایک مکلف سے عاجز وساکت ہو جائے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ پر مکلف کو نبی کا معجزہ دکھانا بر قاعدہ اعتزال عقلاً اور برمذہب اہل حق عادۃ واجب ہے چنانچہ معتزلہ کہتے ہیں کہ عباد کے حق میں اللہ پر لطف واجب ہے لطف سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ امر جو بندہ کو قبائح سے دور رکھے اور حسنات کو پہچنوائے اللہ پر عقلاً واجب ہے اور اس کے برخلاف اشاعرہ و حنفیہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ امر اللہ پر عادۃ واجب ہے عادہ واجب ہونے کا معنی یہ ہے کہ سنت الہیہ اس پر جاری ہے کہ جب اس کی مشیت و مرضی کے مطابق کسی نبی کی بعثت ہوتی ہے تو نبی کے معجزہ کو وہ دیکھا کر ہی چھوڑتا ہے گرچہ مکلف اپنے تئیں لاکھ کوشش کرے کہ معجزہ نہ دیکھے گا لیکن اس کی یہ کوشش ناکام ہوتی ہے کہ اللہ نے معجزہ کو دکھانا اپنے ذمہ کرم پر واجب فرما لیا ہے اس لئے مکلف بالضرور اس کو دیکھتا ہے اس طرح اس شخص کے نزدیک نبی کی نبوت کا دعوی سچا ہو کر رہتا ہے جیسے کہ ہر ناظر و تعلم کو نظر کے بعد علم عادی و جو بی بلا اختیار بالضرورة حاصل ہوتا ہے۔
خلاصہ کلام یہ ہے کہ معجزہ صادر کرتے وقت نبی کو یہ حاجت ہی نہیں رہتی کہ وہ مکلف سے کہے انظر فی معجزتی۔ بلکہ ان کا کام صرف معجزہ صادر کر دینا ہے اور بس ! اسی سے مکلف کو بالضرورت رویت حاصل ہو جاتی ہے مزید نی کو انظرفی مجزتی کہنے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں پڑتی کہ انجام واسکات لازم آئے۔ اقول : اولا۔ نبی کے معجزہ اور امر خارق عادات صادر فرمانے کے وقت مکلف کو اس کی طرف نظر کرنا طبعاً واجب ہے۔ چونکہ عام مشاہدہ و تجربہ سے یہ بات پائے ثبوت کو پہونچ چکی ہے کہ جب کوئی ساحر ومفتری اور کا ہن کوئی حیرت انگیز کرتب دکھاتا ہے تو جہاں تک اس کے کرتب دکھانے کی خبر پہونچتی ہے لوگ اسے دیکھنے کے لئے طبعاً دوڑ پڑتے ہیں گو کہ اسلامی شریعت کی وجہ سے بعض مسلمان اس کے دیکھنے سے احتراز کرتے ہیں وہ بھی خواص اپنی دیانت و عفت اور تقوی طہارت کے سبب نفس پر دباؤ ڈال کر اس کو دیکھنے سے دور رہتے ہیں حالانکہ نفس طبع اس کو دیکھنے پر جبر کرتا ہے۔ جب طبیعت انسانیہ کی حالت ابھی ایسی ہے جب شریعت مطہرہ چار دانگ عالم میں پھیل چکی ہے مسلم غیر مسلم سب سحر و کہانت کی حیرت انگیز کرتب کو اختراعی ہونا یقینی جان رہے ہیں تب یہ حال ہے کہ غیر مسلم و مسلم اس کو دیکھنے کے لئے ٹوٹ پڑتے ہیں۔ تو اس وقت کے لوگوں کی طبیعت کا کیا حال ہوگا جب لوگ شریعت سے بالکل ناواقف ہوں ، جہالت عام ہو ، ہر نفسانی خواہشات کی تکمیل مقصود زندگی ہو تقاضائے طبیعت کو پورا کرنا ہر آخری کوشش ہوتی ہو ایسے پرفتن دور میں کوئی نبی تشریف لائیں چالیس سال مکمل اس معاشرہ میں زندگی بسر کریں ، وہاں کے باشندگان سب بڑے چھوٹے جوان بوڑھے ، مرد اور عورتیں ان کے اخلاق وکردار سے متاثر ہوں، بلکہ ان کے تقوی وطہارت اور عفت و پاکدامنی کو دیکھکر سب لوگ ان کو صادق الامین کہنے لگیں۔ ان حالات میں جب اللہ کا کوئی پیغمبر اگر معجز و امر خارق للعادة صادر کرتا ہے تو چنداں اس نبی کو یہ کہنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہوگی کہ میرے اس حیرت انگیز کارنامہ کو دیکھو بلکہ خودسب باقتناء طبع اس معجزہ کو دیکھنے پر مجبور ہوں گے گرچہ معجزہ دیکھ کر انکار کر دیں چنانچہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چالیس سالہ کی زندگی گزارنے کے بعد جب صفاء پہاڑ پر سے لوگوں کو آواز دیا تو ساری قومیں فورا حاضر ہو گئیں حتی کہ ابولہب جیسا خناس بھی حاضر آیا ....... حاصل یہ کہ نبی کی شخصیت ہی ایسی پاکیزہ اور دیدہ زیب ہوتی ہے کہ ہر شخص ان کو عظیم انسان کہنے لگتا ہے اس لئے ثبوت نبوت سے پہلے پہلے جو بھی معجزہ وہ صادر کریں گے لوگ ان کی شخصیت کے مدنظر اور اپنی طبیعت ونفس کے اقتضاء کو پورا کرنے کے لئے ضرور بالضرور معجزہ پر نظر کریں گے کیونکہ نفس حیرت انگیز چیز کے دیکھنے کا عادی اور خواہشمند رہتا ہے اس لئے میں نے کہا کہ معجزہ پر نظر کرنا طبعا واجب ہے لہذا معتزلہ کا یہ کہنا کہ اگر حکم شرعی ہوتو انعام رسول لازم آئے گا باطل محض کا العدم ہے۔
ثانياً: حکم کے عقلی نہ ہونے پر انجام رسل کا ملازمہ پیش کرنے سے قبل معتزلہ کو خیال کرنا چاہئے کہ وہ نبی آخر الزماں صلى الله عليه وسلم کی امت میں اب آپ نے کے بعد کسی نبی کی بعثت عقلا، شرعاً بالا جماع محال ممتنع
Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut. 261. ... The author says that the Ash'ari's answer in this discussion is considered very good, but the truth is that this answer reverts to my true answer, which is as follows. His statement: 'And the truth is that witnessing miracles is obligatory, etc.' In this phrase, the correct response to the Mu'tazila's proof is given. The gist of the proof is that looking at the proof and reasoning, although the prophet's failure is possible, Allah never realizes this possibility—that when the prophet shows a miracle, he would be incapacitated and silenced by a responsible person—because showing the miracle to the responsible person is obligatory upon Allah: rationally according to the Mu'tazila, and by habitual custom according to the Ahl al-Haqq (Ash'ari and Hanafi). Thus, the Mu'tazila say that grace (lutf) is obligatory upon Allah concerning His servants. By grace is meant that which keeps the servant away from evil deeds and makes him recognize good deeds; it is rationally obligatory upon Allah. Contrary to this, the Ash'ari and Hanafis say that this matter is obligatory upon Allah by habitual custom. The meaning of being obligatory by custom is that the divine practice (sunnat Allah) is established that when, according to His will and pleasure, a prophet is sent, the prophet's miracle is inevitably seen, even if the responsible person tries his utmost not to see it, his effort fails because Allah has made showing the miracle obligatory upon His generosity. Therefore, the responsible person sees it necessarily. Thus, in his view, the prophet's claim to prophethood becomes true, just as every observer and learner acquires habitual and necessary knowledge without choice after seeing. The summary is that when the prophet performs a miracle, he does not need to say to the responsible person, 'Look at my miracle.' Rather, his work is only to produce the miracle, and that's it! From this, the responsible person necessarily obtains sight; there is no need to say 'Look at my miracle' such that the prophet's failure and silence would necessarily follow. I say: Firstly, when the prophet produces a miracle and an extraordinary event, it is naturally obligatory for the responsible person to look at it. Since, through common observation and experience, it has been established that when a sorcerer, impostor, or soothsayer performs an astonishing trick, as far as the news of his trick reaches, people naturally rush to see it. Although due to Islamic law, some Muslims refrain from seeing it, they too—the elite, due to their piety, chastity, and purity—suppress their inclination and stay away, even though their natural self compels them to see it. When the state of human nature is such now, when the pure Shariah has spread across the world, and Muslims and non-Muslims know for certain that the astonishing tricks of sorcery and soothsaying are invented, even then people flock to see them. So what would be the condition of people at that time when they were completely ignorant of the Shariah, ignorance was widespread, fulfilling every carnal desire was the purpose of life, and satisfying natural inclination was the ultimate effort? In such a tumultuous era, a prophet arrives, lives a complete forty years in that society, the inhabitants—all great and small, young and old, men and women—are impressed by his character and conduct; indeed, seeing his piety, purity, and chastity, all people call him al-Sadiq al-Amin (the truthful and trustworthy). In these circumstances, when Allah's prophet produces a miracle and an extraordinary event, the prophet will hardly need to say, 'Look at my amazing feat'; rather, by natural impulse, they will be compelled to see the miracle, even if they deny it after seeing. Thus, the Prophet (peace be upon him), after living forty years, when he called the people from Mount Safa, all the tribes immediately gathered, even Abu Lahab, the treacherous one, came. The point is that the prophet's personality itself is so pure and beautiful that everyone considers him a great human being. Therefore, before the proof of prophethood, any miracle he produces, people will necessarily look at the miracle, considering his personality and to fulfill the demands of their nature and self, because the self is habituated and desirous of seeing astonishing things. Therefore, I said that looking at the miracle is naturally obligatory. Hence, the Mu'tazila's statement that if it were a legal command, the prophet's need would result, is pure non-existence. Secondly, before presenting the consequence of the prophet's failure based on the absence of rational obligation, the Mu'tazila should consider that in the ummah of the Final Prophet (peace be upon him), after his time, the sending of any prophet is rationally, legally, and by consensus, impossible and prohibited.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage from 'Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut' is a classic Hanafi usul dispute on the nature of obligation regarding witnessing miracles. The author begins by framing the issue: the Mu'tazila argue that it is rationally obligatory (wajib bi al-'aql) upon Allah to grant grace (lutf) to ensure that people witness a prophet's miracle; otherwise, if a person refuses to look, the prophet would be required to command them, potentially leading to his failure ('ajz). The Ash'ari and Hanafi position is that this obligation is based on habitual custom ('adah), not rational necessity. The author then provides his own detailed argument: first, he argues that human nature naturally compels people to look at astonishing things, as seen with sorcerers. Second, the prophet's impeccable character and the societal context further ensure that people will look at the miracle. Thus, the prophet does not need to issue a command; the miracle itself suffices. The author concludes that the Mu'tazila's fear of 'inam al-rasul (the prophet needing something) is groundless, and their rational obligation is false. The passage concludes with a second point that after Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), no prophet can be sent, so the entire debate is moot for this ummah.

Key Terms
رؤية المعجزات (ru'yat al-mu'jizat): Witnessing the miracles of a prophet, which is argued to be obligatory upon the responsible person.
لطف (lutf): Grace from Allah that keeps the servant from evil and leads to good; Mu'tazila claim it is rationally obligatory upon Allah.
عادة ('adah): Habitual custom; here the divine practice (sunnat Allah) that makes witnessing miracles inevitable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi/Ash'ari position presented in this passage, why do people inevitably witness a prophet's miracle without being commanded?
A) Because it is rationally obligatory for Allah to make them see it.
B) Because of habitual divine practice and natural human inclination.
C) Because the prophet directly commands them to look.
D) Because of a legal obligation from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi/Ash'ari view grounds the obligation to witness miracles in habitual custom and human nature, not rational necessity, thereby avoiding the Mu'tazila's problematic imposition of rational duties on Allah.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Hanafi Refutation of Rational Necessity in Divine Commands
Refuting Mu'tazila's arguments that divine commands must be rational and that miracles could be performed by liars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi-Maturidi refutation of the Mu'tazila's claim that divine commands must be rationally necessary.

Core Idea
Lying is a deficiency, and deficiency is rationally impossible for Allah — but that does not make commands rationally necessary.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute between the Hanafi/Maturidi school and the Mu'tazila on whether divine actions are subject to rational categories of good and evil. The source passage refutes two Mu'tazila arguments: first, that if commands were not rational, then reward of the messenger would not be necessary; second, that if lying were possible for God, miracles could appear on false prophets, closing the door of prophethood. The Hanafi response relies on the concept of wujub dhati (essential obligation) and the impossibility of deficiency in Allah, while also invoking the finality of prophethood to block the hypothetical.

Guided Path
1
State the two Mu'tazila arguments
Identify the two arguments presented by the Mu'tazila: (a) if divine commands are not rational, then the reward of the messenger would not be necessitated; (b) if commands are not rational, then lying from God would not be impossible, allowing miracles to appear on false prophets, thus closing the door of prophethood.
These arguments aim to show that rationality of commands is necessary for prophethood to be trusted.
2
Identify the Hanafi response to argument (a)
The Hanafi response: human nature compels people to look at miraculous events instinctively; no command is needed to necessitate looking. Therefore, the Mu'tazila's link between command and reward is invalid.
The author uses the example of Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) and the natural inclination to witness miracles.
3
Identify the Hanafi response to argument (b)
Lying is a deficiency (naqs), and deficiency is rationally impossible for Allah because it contradicts wujub dhati (essential obligation). The source states that whatever contradicts wujub dhati is a rational impossibility.
The Hanafi position is that while naqs is agreed to be impossible, this does not entail that commands are rationally necessitated; revelation determines good and evil.
4
Note the supplementary argument of finality
The author argues that after Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), no new prophet can come by consensus, so the scenario of a false prophet performing miracles is impossible. Hence, the Mu'tazila's hypothetical is moot.
This blocks the Mu'tazila's concern about the door of prophethood being closed.
5
Analyze the broader khilaf
The Mu'tazila affirm rational good and evil (qubh aqli), holding that actions are inherently good or evil. The Hanafi/Maturidi school holds that good and evil are determined by revelation, not pure reason.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Mu'tazila would judge some actions as rationally obligatory before revelation; Hanafis do not.

ثانياً: حکم کے عقلی نہ ہونے پر انجام رسل کا ملازمہ پیش کرنے سے قبل معتزلہ کو خیال کرنا چاہئے کہ وہ نبی آخر الزماں صلى الله عليه وسلم کی امت میں اب آپ کے بعد کسی نبی کی بعثت عقلا، شرعاً بالا جماع محال ممتنع ہے کہ آپ کی شریعت جامعہ کاملہ اور حاویہ ازمان و اوقات ہے پس جب حضور اے کے بعد کسی نبی کا آنا ہی ممتنع و محال ہے تو پھر معجزہ دیکھنے کے امر کا کیا سوال اور پھر اس پر مکلف کا نبی کو خاموش کرنے کا کیا مجال بلکہ تو اس محال است و محال است جنوں کے قبیل سے ہو گا لہذا استدلال محال کہ نبی کی بعثت محال ہے.. اور اگر استدلال کی بنیاد ما مضی انبیاء کرام کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے ہے تو بھی معتزلی استدلال نام نہیں ہوتا اسلئے کہ اسکا کوئی ثبوت نہیں کہ کسی نبی کے زمانہ میں کسی نبی کے ساتھ ایسا حادثہ پیش آیا ہو کہ مکلف نے ان کو خاموش و عاجز کر دیا ہو چنانچہ قطع نظر حقائق و شرائع کے عقول بھی اس کی تکذیب کرتی ہے۔ اور اگر صرف امکان وجواز ہی مراد ہے کہ حکم کو شرعی ماننے کی تقدیر پر انجام رسول کا امکان لازم آتا ہے تو جواب یہ ہے کہ امکان وقوع کو کب مستلزم ہے پھر امکان محض کے بل بوتے پر حکم الہی ایجاب و تحریم اور پھر اسکے ثمرات ثواب و عقاب کے وقوع استحقاق کا قول کرنا کس حد تک صحیح ہے الغرض معتز لی دلیل باطل ہے۔
متن المسلم : وثانيا انه لولاه لم يمتنع الكذب منه تعالى فلايمتنع اظهار المعجزات على يد الكاذب فينسدباب النبوة والجواب انه نقص وقدمر انه لانزاع فيه ومافى المواقف أن النقص فى الافعال يرجع الى القبح العقلى فممنوع لان ما ينافي الوجوب الذاتى كيفاً كان او فعلاً من الاستحالات العقلية وكذالك اثبته الحكماء ولكن يلزم على الاشاعرة امتناع تعذيب الطائع كماهو مذهنبا ومذهب المعتزلة فانه نقص يستحيل عليه تعالى
ترجمہ : اور ( معتزلہ نے حکم کے عقلی ہونے پر دوسری دلیل دیتے ہوئے کہا کہ اگر حکم عقلی نہ ہو تو اللہ تعالیٰ سے کذب ممتنع نہیں رہے گا پس منجزات کا اظہار بھی دست کاذب پر ممتنع نہ ہوگا اسطرح نبوت کا دروازہ بند ہو جائے گا اور جواب یہ ہے کہ کذب نقص ہے چنانچہ ماسبق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ نقص کے عقلی ہونے میں کوئی نزاع نہیں ہے اور جو مواقف میں ہے کہ نقص فی الافعال فتح عقلی کی طرف راجع ہے تو یہ ممنوع ہے کیونکہ جو وجوب ذاتی کے منافی ہو خواہ وہ کیف ہو یا فعل ، استحالات عقلیہ میں سے ہے چنانچہ اس لئے حکماء نے اسکو ثابت مانا ہے لیکن اشاعرہ کے مذہب پر طائع کی تعذیب کا ممتنع ہونا لازم
News reaches: people instinctively rush to see it. Although due to Islamic Shari'a some Muslims refrain from seeing it, they too, the elite, due to their piety, chastity, and purity, suppress their souls and stay away from seeing it, while the natural self compels them to see it. When the state of human nature is such, when the pure Shari'a has spread throughout the world, Muslims and non-Muslims all consider the amazing feats of magic and soothsaying as invented, then the situation is that non-Muslims and Muslims flock to see it. So what will be the state of people's nature at that time when people are completely unaware of Shari'a, ignorance is widespread, every fulfillment of carnal desires is the purpose of life, fulfilling the demands of nature is every final effort? In such a time of tribulation, a prophet comes, lives forty full years in that society, the inhabitants, all big and small, young and old, men and women, are influenced by his character and conduct, rather seeing his piety, purity, and chastity, all people call him truthful and trustworthy. Under these circumstances, if a prophet of Allah performs a miracle and a matter contrary to custom, then there is little need for that prophet to say 'look at this amazing feat of mine'; rather, they themselves, by the compulsion of nature, will be forced to look at the miracle, even if they deny it after seeing it. Thus, when the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) called out to the people from Mount Safa after living forty years, all the tribes immediately gathered, even Abu Lahab, a miscreant, came. The conclusion is that the Prophet's personality itself is so pure and beautiful that everyone calls him a great man. Therefore, before the proof of prophethood, whatever miracle he performs, people, considering his personality and to fulfill the demands of their nature and soul, will definitely and necessarily look at the miracle, because the soul is accustomed to and desirous of seeing amazing things. Therefore, I said that looking at the miracle is naturally obligatory. Hence, the Mu'tazila's statement that if the command is legal (shar'i), then the reward of the messenger becomes necessary is sheer falsehood and non-existent.
Secondly: Before presenting the necessary consequence of the messenger's reward for the non-rationality of the command, the Mu'tazila should consider that in the ummah of the Prophet of the End Times (peace be upon him), after him, the sending of any prophet is rationally and legally impossible by consensus. His Shari'a is comprehensive, perfect, and encompassing all times and places. So when after the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) the coming of any prophet is impossible and inconceivable, then what question of commanding to see a miracle? And then what scope for the obligated person to silence the prophet? Rather, this is impossibility upon impossibility, belonging to the category of madness. Hence, the argument is impossible because the sending of a prophet is impossible. And if the argument is based on looking at past prophets, then the Mu'tazilite argument is not even valid, because there is no proof that in the time of any prophet such an incident occurred that an obligated person silenced and incapacitated him. Thus, reason itself, disregarding realities and laws, refutes this. And if only possibility and permissibility are meant, that on the assumption of the command being legal, the possibility of the messenger's fate follows, then the answer is that possibility does not entail occurrence. Then, on the basis of mere possibility, to claim the occurrence of divine command of obligation and prohibition, and then its fruits of reward and punishment and entitlement to occurrence—to what extent is that correct? In short, the Mu'tazilite proof is false.
The text of al-Muslim: And secondly, that if it were not so, lying from Him, exalted, would not be impossible, so the manifestation of miracles at the hand of a liar would not be impossible, and thus the door of prophethood would be closed. The answer is that it is a deficiency, and it has passed that there is no dispute about it. And what is in al-Mawaqif that deficiency in actions refers to rational repugnance is denied, because whatever contradicts essential obligation, whether as a quality or an act, is among rational impossibilities. Thus, the philosophers have proven it. But upon the Ash'aris, the impossibility of punishing the obedient becomes necessary, as is our doctrine and the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, for it is a deficiency that is impossible for Him, exalted.
Translation: And (the Mu'tazila, presenting a second proof for the rationality of the command, said that if the command is not rational, then lying from Allah, exalted, would not be impossible, so the manifestation of miracles at the hand of a liar would not be impossible, thus the door of prophethood would be closed. The answer is that lying is a deficiency, and as has passed earlier, there is no dispute that deficiency is rationally [impermissible]. And what is in al-Mawaqif that deficiency in actions reverts to rational repugnance is denied, because whatever contradicts essential obligation, whether it be a quality or an act, is among rational impossibilities. Thus, the philosophers have established it. But upon the school of the Ash'aris, the impossibility of punishing the obedient becomes necessary, as is their doctrine and that of the Mu'tazila, for it is a deficiency that is impossible for Him, exalted.)
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila's arguments concerning the rationality of divine commands and the necessity of miracles for prophethood. The author, commenting on Musallam al-Thubut, first argues that miracles naturally attract people due to human nature, even before any command to look. He cites the example of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and the natural inclination to witness extraordinary events. Thus, the Mu'tazila's claim that if commands were not rational, then reward for the messenger would be necessitated is baseless. Secondly, the author argues that after the finality of prophethood, no new prophet can come, so the Mu'tazila's hypothetical scenario is impossible. Finally, the text of al-Muslim presents the Mu'tazila's second proof: if commands are not rational, then lying from God is not impossible, allowing miracles to appear on false prophets, thus closing the door of prophethood. The response is that lying is a deficiency (naqs), and deficiency in actions is rationally impossible because it contradicts essential obligation (wujub dhati). However, the Ash'aris face the consequence that punishing the obedient would also be a deficiency, which they must address. The commentary follows the order of the matn and refutes each point with rational arguments. The author maintains that the Mu'tazila's reliance on mere possibility is invalid, and that divine commands are established through revelation, not pure reason.

Key Terms
وجوب ذاتی (wujub dhati): Essential obligation, a property inherent to Allah's essence that prevents deficiency; any act contradicting it is rationally impossible.
نقص (naqs): Deficiency or imperfection; rationally impossible for Allah as it contradicts His perfection.
قبح عقلی (qubh aqli): Rational repugnance; an action considered evil by reason independent of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary refutation of the Mu'tazila's claim that if divine commands are not rational, then God could lie and miracles could appear on false prophets?
A) Lying is a deficiency (naqs), and deficiency is rationally impossible for God.
B) The command to look at a miracle is not rational but natural.
C) The finality of prophethood makes the scenario impossible.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila argument for rational necessity fails because deficiency (naqs) is rationally impossible for Allah, and the finality of prophethood renders their hypothetical moot.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Debate on Rational vs Revealed Rulings: Mu'tazila Argument and Response
Refuting Mu'tazila argument that rulings must be rational to avoid impossible consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Mu'tazila reductio argument against the Ash'ari position and explain the Hanafi/Maturidi response using the concept of deficiency (naqṣ).

Core Idea
Lying is a deficiency (naqṣ) — rationally evil — so it is impossible for Allah even without revelation.

The Mu'tazila argued that if rulings were purely revealed, lying from Allah would be rationally permissible before revelation, allowing false miracles and closing the door of prophethood. The Ash'ari/Maturidi response, accepted in Hanafi usul, is that deficiency (naqṣ) is rationally recognized as evil by all schools. Since lying is a deficiency, it is impossible for Allah even without revelation, preserving the proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
The Mu'tazila argue that if rulings are not rational but only revealed, then before revelation there is no prohibition on lying from Allah. This would make it possible for miracles to be performed by a liar, making it impossible to distinguish true prophets from false ones, thus closing the door of prophethood.
This is a reductio ad absurdum against the Ash'ari position.
2
Locate the core response: deficiency (naqṣ)
The response is that lying is a deficiency (naqṣ), and deficiency is rationally recognized as evil by all schools, including the Ash'aris. Therefore, lying is impossible for Allah even before revelation.
The concept of naqṣ is key; it bridges rational and revealed ethics.
3
Understand the three meanings of ḥusn and qubḥ
The commentary explains that good and evil have three meanings: 1) perfection vs. deficiency (rational), 2) beneficial vs. harmful (rational), 3) deserving praise/reward vs. blame/punishment (revealed). The first two are rational by consensus; only the third is revealed.
This distinction allows Ash'aris to accept rational evaluation of deficiency without accepting full rational moral obligation.
4
Evaluate how the response blocks the reductio
Since deficiency is rationally evil and lying is a deficiency, even before revelation lying is impossible for Allah. Thus, miracles cannot appear from a liar, and the proof of prophethood remains intact without requiring rational rulings for all acts.
The Mu'tazila argument collapses because it assumed no rational evaluation of acts before revelation.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The Mu'tazila conclude that all acts are inherently good or evil (rational). Ash'aris/Maturidis conclude that only deficiency/benefit is rational; moral obligation and desert of reward/punishment depend on revelation.
This difference affects many usul debates, e.g., on the status of acts before revelation.

The answer: it is a deficiency, and it has passed that there is no dispute about it. And what is in al-Mawaqif that deficiency in actions returns to rational ugliness is prevented, because whatever contradicts essential obligation, whether in quality or action, is among rational impossibilities, and thus the philosophers have affirmed it. Translation: And (the Mu'tazila, in presenting their second proof for the rationality of rulings, said: if the ruling is not rational, then lying from Allah would not be impossible; then the manifestation of miracles at the hand of a liar would not be impossible; thus the door of prophethood would be closed. And the answer is that lying is a deficiency. As has passed, there is no dispute that deficiency is rational. And what is in al-Mawaqif that deficiency in actions returns to rational ugliness is prevented, because whatever contradicts essential obligation, whether in quality or action, is among rational impossibilities; thus the philosophers have affirmed it. But upon the Ash'aris, the impossibility of punishing the obedient is necessary, as is our doctrine and the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, because it is a deficiency that is impossible for Allah. Commentary: His statement 'and secondly, if it were not for that, lying from Him would not be impossible' etc. In the above expression, the Mu'tazila's second proof (for the rationality of rulings) is mentioned. The gist of the proof: If the ruling is not rational but revealed, as the Ash'aris and Maturidis think, then lying from Allah would not be impossible; rather, lying would be permissible and possible for Him (as the misguided sect of Wahhabis believe today). Because on the assumption of its being revealed, the prohibition of lying would be a revealed ruling and a revealed prohibition; hence before revelation, lying would not be forbidden. And when it is not forbidden, it is not ugly. So rationally, it would be permissible for Allah to be described with lying, because there is no rational repugnance in it, whereas lying is rationally impossible for Allah because it is ugly. As for lying being revealedly ugly, that cannot be imagined in respect of Allah, because revealed ugliness is connected to revealed prohibitions that pertain specifically to servants. Therefore, lying being impossible for the Exalted due to revealed ugliness does not negate rational permissibility. And when lying remains permissible for Him, not impossible, then the manifestation of miracles at the hand of a liar would not be impossible, but permissible, because it is a branch of lying. Thus the door of prophethood would be closed, while it is open. The reason for the closing of the door of prophethood is that in that case, a truthful prophet could not be distinguished from a liar; indeed, there would be no confidence in his statement, and consequently nothing of the Sharia would be known. And you see. His statement 'and the answer is that it is a deficiency, and it has passed that there is no dispute about it' – from this expression, the answer to the Mu'tazila's mentioned proof is given. The summary of the answer: It has passed in the preceding that good and evil are used in three meanings: first, the attribute of perfection and deficiency; second, being in accordance or opposition with worldly objectives; third, deserving praise and reward or blame and punishment in this world and the Hereafter. The first two meanings, by agreement of the Mu'tazila, Maturidis, and Ash'aris, are rational. And it is clear and agreed that lying is a deficiency, and deficiency, even according to the Ash'aris, is rationally ugly. Therefore, lying, before revelation, is ugly according to the Ash'aris. Hence, its occurrence from Allah, indeed even its rational permissibility, is impossible. And when lying
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Mu'tazila's second argument for the rationality of rulings (ḥukm 'aqlī). The argument is a reductio ad absurdum: if rulings were purely revealed (sharʿī) and not rationally knowable, then lying (kadhib) from Allah would not be rationally impossible—it would only be prohibited by revelation, and before revelation there would be no prohibition. Consequently, miracles could be performed by false prophets, making it impossible to distinguish true prophets from liars, thus closing the door of prophethood (nubuwwa). The response, from the Ashʿarī (and Māturīdī) perspective, is that deficiency (naqṣ) is recognized rationally; even Ashʿarīs affirm that certain acts are rationally ugly in the sense of being imperfect or lacking. Lying is a deficiency, and deficiency is rationally impossible for Allah. Therefore, even before revelation, lying is impossible for Allah, and the argument collapses. The commentary explains that good and evil (ḥusn wa qubḥ) have three meanings: 1) perfection vs. deficiency (rational), 2) beneficial vs. harmful (rational), 3) deserving praise/reward vs. blame/punishment (revealed). The first two are rational by consensus. Thus, lying falls under deficiency, making it rationally impossible for Allah, preserving the possibility of miracles for true prophets.

Key Terms
كذب (kadhib): Lying; an act that is a deficiency (naqṣ), rationally known to be evil.
نقص (naqṣ): Deficiency; an attribute of imperfection that is rationally recognized as evil.
حكم عقلي (ḥukm 'aqlī): A ruling known by reason alone, independent of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila argument refuted in this passage, what would be the consequence if rulings were not rational?
A) Prophethood would be proven by miracles.
B) Lying from Allah would be rationally impossible.
C) The door of prophethood would be closed because miracles could appear through liars.
D) Truthful prophets would be easily distinguished.

Key Takeaway
Lying is a deficiency (naqṣ), rationally known to be evil; this agreed-upon fact refutes the Mu'tazila's reductio and preserves the proof of prophethood.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Are Rulings Rational or Revealed? The Impossibility of Lying by God
Refuting the Mu'tazila's proof that rulings are rational

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi-Maturidi position on the rational impossibility of lying by God and evaluate the Mu'tazila argument that rulings must be rational.

Core Idea
Lying is rationally impossible for God because it is a deficiency; revelation does not affect this.

The Mu'tazila argued that if rulings were only revealed, before revelation God could rationally lie, which would invalidate prophethood. Therefore, rulings must be rational. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi response: lying is a deficiency (naqs), and deficiency is rationally known to be impossible for God. We will trace the three meanings of good and evil (husn wa qubh) to see how the Hanafi school refutes the Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
State the Mu'tazila claim and their proof
The Mu'tazila assert that rulings must be rational (aqli) rather than purely revealed (shar'i). Their proof: if rulings were revealed only, then before revelation lying by God would be permissible, which would allow a false prophet to perform miracles, thus closing the door of prophethood.
This proof is the 'second proof' mentioned in the text.
2
Understand the three meanings of husn and qubh
The text explains that goodness and ugliness have three meanings: (1) attribute of perfection/deficiency, (2) worldly benefit/harm, (3) deserving reward/punishment. The first two are rationally known by all schools; the third is disputed.
This tripartite distinction is crucial for the Hanafi response.
3
Identify the Hanafi response using deficiency
Lying is a deficiency (naqs). Deficiency in the sense of attribute of perfection/deficiency is rationally ugly by agreement. Therefore, lying is rationally impossible for God even before revelation. So the Mu'tazila's inference fails.
The response shows that the impossibility of lying is rational, not dependent on revelation.
4
Analyze the objection from al-Mawaqif
The author of al-Mawaqif distinguishes deficiency in actions (like lying) from deficiency in attributes (like ignorance). He claims deficiency in actions is not unanimously rational. The sharh rebuts this, insisting that even deficiency in actions is rationally ugly because it is a deficiency.
This refinement strengthens the Hanafi position.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
If rulings were rational, God would be obligated to do what is best (al-salah wa al-aslah). The Hanafi-Ash'ari view affirms God's absolute freedom; reason alone does not obligate Him.
The practical difference affects theology and usul methodology.
