It will come as our school and the Mu'tazila's school holds, because it is a deficiency that is impossible for Allah. Commentary: His saying: "And secondly, that if not for that, lying would not be impossible from Him, exalted" etc. From the above phrase, the second proof of the Mu'tazila (that rulings are rational) is mentioned. The substance of the proof is that if the ruling is not rational but revealed, as the Ash'aris and Maturidis think, then lying upon Allah would not be impossible; rather, in His right, lying would be permissible and possible (as nowadays the deviant sect, the so-called Wahhabis, may Allah ruin them, believe). Because on the assumption of being revealed, the prohibition of lying would be a revealed ruling and a revealed prohibition. Therefore, before revelation, lying would not be forbidden. And when it is not forbidden, it is also not ugly. Thus, rationally, Allah's being characterized with lying would remain permissible, since rationally there is no repugnance in it. However, lying is rationally impossible for Allah because it is ugly. As for lying being revealedly ugly, in Allah's right that cannot be imagined because revealed ugliness is established and related to revealed prohibitions which are specific to servants. Therefore, lying's being impossible in Allah's right due to revealed ugliness does not negate rational permissibility. And when lying remains permissible in His right, not impossible and absurd, then the manifestation of a miracle at the hand of a liar would also not be impossible, but permissible, because it is a branch of lying. In this way, the door of prophethood would be closed, whereas it is open. The reason for the closure of the door of prophethood is that in this case, a truthful prophet cannot be distinguished from a liar, and his words cannot be relied upon; consequently, nothing of the Sharia can be known. And so on. His saying: "And the answer is that it is a deficiency, and it has already passed that there is no dispute about it." From this phrase, a response to the aforementioned proof of the Mu'tazila is given. The summary of the response is that it has passed earlier that husn (goodness) and qubh (ugliness) are used in three meanings: one is the attribute of perfection and deficiency; the second is being in accordance with or opposed to worldly aims; and the third is deserving praise and reward or blame and punishment in this world and the Hereafter. The first two meanings, by agreement of the Mu'tazila, Maturidis, and Ash'aris, are rational. And it is clear and agreed upon that lying is a deficiency, and deficiency in the view of the Ash'aris is also a rational ugliness. Therefore, even before revelation, lying is ugly in the view of the Ash'aris. Hence, its occurrence from Allah, nay, its rational permissibility, remains impossible. And when the permissibility of lying is rationally impossible even in the view of the Ash'aris, then the manifestation of a miracle at the hand of one who is characterized with an attribute like lying and deficiency is prohibited, because when the original is impossible, the branch is a fortiori impossible. Therefore, the manifestation of a miracle at the hand of a liar becomes impossible; thus, the closure of the door of prophethood does not follow. His saying: "And what is in al-Mawaqif: that deficiency in actions goes back to ugliness..." From this phrase, the author (matn) has objected to the statement of the author of al-Mawaqif. First, the statement of the author of al-Mawaqif is mentioned, then the explanation of the objection. Statement of al-Mawaqif: The author of al-Mawaqif said that deficiency is of two types: (1) deficiency in actions (naqs fi al-af'al), like lying, manifestation of miracle at the hand of a liar, etc. (2) deficiency in attributes (naqs fi al-sifat), like ignorance, incapacity, etc. And the first type, i.e., deficiency in actions, goes back to disputed rational ugliness (qubh 'aqli mukhtalif fihi). The meaning is that the deficiency of actions is not unanimously rational; rather, deficiency in actions is in the meaning of rational ugliness about which the Ash'aris and Mu'tazila differ. And that meaning is rationally deserving of blame and punishment. (In short, the deficiency that occurs in actions is not unanimously rational; rather, some consider it rational and others revealed). And in deficiency in actions, the consideration of disputed rational ugliness is because Allah, glorious is He, is autonomous in His actions. Thus, He can be deserving of praise and blame for His action, as it is not among rational impossibilities. Exalted is Allah above that, a great exaltation. Of course, the second type, i.e., deficiency in attributes, does not go back to disputed rational ugliness; rather, it is unanimously rational in the meaning of the attribute of perfection and deficiency. The reason is that Allah's attributes are non-volitional, and disputed ugliness cannot occur in non-volitional matters. The conclusion is that deficiency that occurs in actions is expressed in the meaning of deficiency deserving blame and punishment, like lying and manifestation of miracle at the hand of a liar. Therefore, in the view of the Ash'aris, in any case, this lying would be revealed (shar'i), which would not be prohibited from Allah. In contrast, deficiency that occurs in attributes is expressed in the meaning of deficiency of the attribute of perfection and deficiency, like ignorance and incapacity. Thus, in the view of the Ash'aris, Maturidis, and Mu'tazila, it will unanimously remain impossible, because this meaning
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh dispute between the Mu'tazila and the Ash'ari/Maturidi/Hanafi school on whether rulings are rational (aqli) or revealed (shar'i). The text first presents the Mu'tazila's second proof: if rulings were revealed only (as the Ash'aris claim), then before revelation there would be no prohibition on lying, so rationally God could lie. This would mean that a liar could perform miracles, making it impossible to distinguish a true prophet from a false one, thus closing the door of prophethood—a clear absurdity. The answer comes by distinguishing three meanings of good and evil (husn wa qubh): 1) attribute of perfection/deficiency, 2) worldly benefit/harm, 3) deserving reward/punishment. The first two are rationally known by all schools. Lying is a deficiency (naqs), and deficiency is rationally ugly even for the Ash'aris. So before revelation, lying is already known to be impossible for God, because it is a deficiency. Therefore, the Mu'tazila's argument fails: the impossibility of lying for God is rational, not dependent on revealed law. The text then addresses a subtle point from al-Mawaqif, which distinguishes deficiency in actions (like lying) from deficiency in attributes (like ignorance). Deficiency in actions is not unanimously rational; it is subject to dispute (some say rational, others say revealed). However, deficiency in attributes is agreed to be rational and absolutely impossible for God. The author of the sharh objects to this classification, defending the Ash'ari position that even deficiency in actions is ultimately rationally impossible for God because it is a deficiency. The entire discussion shows how usul al-fiqh debates have direct implications for the foundations of prophethood and the necessity of revelation.

Key Terms
حسن و قبح (husn wa qubh): Goodness and ugliness; three meanings: attribute of perfection/deficiency, worldly benefit/harm, and deserving reward/punishment.
نقص (naqs): Deficiency; an imperfection that is rationally known to be impossible for God.
كذب (kadhib): Lying; a paradigmatic example of a deficiency in action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core of the Hanafi response to the Mu'tazila's proof that rulings must be rational?
A) Lying is prohibited by revelation, so God cannot lie after revelation.
B) Lying is a deficiency, and deficiency is rationally impossible for God, so the argument fails.
C) The Mu'tazila admit that miracles are possible at the hand of a liar.
D) Prophethood is not proven by miracles but by testimony.

Key Takeaway
Lying is rationally impossible for God because it is a deficiency; this rational impossibility is agreed upon by all schools, refuting the Mu'tazila's argument that rulings must be rational.

Refuting the Distinction Between Defects in Actions and Attributes
Refuting al-Mawaqif's distinction between defects in actions and attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi argument against al-Mawaqif's distinction and evaluate the epistemological implications of rational vs. legal defects.

Core Idea
Any defect in Allah, whether in actions or attributes, is rationally impossible because it contradicts His necessary existence.

This lesson examines a key theological dispute that underpins Hanafi usul al-fiqh: Are defects in Allah's actions merely legally prohibited, or are they rationally impossible? The author of Muslim al-Thubut refutes al-Mawaqif's claim that defects in actions are only disputed rational ugliness, using the concept of wujub dhati (necessary existence). Understanding this refutation clarifies why Hanafis hold that miracles only appear on true prophets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
What is the exact point of disagreement between al-Mawaqif and the Hanafi author?
The issue is whether defects in actions (e.g., lying) are rationally impossible or merely legally prohibited.
2
Articulate al-Mawaqif's position
State al-Mawaqif's distinction between defects in actions and defects in attributes.
Al-Mawaqif claims defects in actions are subject to disputed rational ugliness, while defects in attributes are unanimously rational.
3
State the Hanafi objection
How does the Hanafi author reject this distinction? Identify the key premise.
The author argues that any defect – in action or attribute – contradicts Allah's necessary existence (wujub dhati), making it rationally impossible.
4
Trace the logical consequence
What practical implication does the author draw? How does this affect the proof of prophethood?
If defects in actions were only legal, a liar could perform miracles, undermining the proof of prophethood. Hanafis hold that miracles only appear on true prophets.
5
Determine the tarjih
Why does the author side with the rational impossibility of all defects?
The author cites that even non-religious philosophers recognize lying as impossible for God, reinforcing that it is rationally necessary.

قوله ومافى المواقف أن النقص فى الافعال يرجع الى القبح الخ اس عبارت سے ماتن نے صاحب مواقف کے قول پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔ پہلے صاحب مواقف کا قول ذکر کیا جاتا ہے پھر اعتراض کی تقریر ہوگی۔
قول مواقف : صاحب مواقف نے کہا ہے کہ نقص کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) نقص فی الافعال (افعال میں نقص ) جیسے کذب، اظہار مجزہ بر دست کا ذب وغیرہ۔ (۲) نقص فی الصفات ( صفات میں نقص) جیسے جہل و عجز وغیرہ۔ اور قسم اول یعنی نقص فی الافعال فتح عقلی متنازع فیہ کی طرف راجع ہے مطلب یہ ہے کہ افعال کا نقص اتفاقی عقلی نہیں ہے بلکہ نقص فی الافعال اس معنی کر فتح عقلی ہے جس میں اشاعرہ د معتزلہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ اور وہ معنی ہے عقلا ذم و عقاب کا مستحق ہونا۔
( الغرض افعال میں جو نقص ہو وہ بالا تفاق عقلی نہیں ہے بلکہ بعض کے نزدیک عقلی ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک شرعی ہے ) اور نقص فی الافعال میں فتح عقلی متنازع فیہ کا اعتبار اس لئے ہے کہ اللہ سبحانہ تعالیٰ اپنے افعال میں مختار ہے پس وہ اپنے فعل پر مدح و ذم کا مستحق ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ استحالات عقلیہ سے نہیں ہے تعالٰی اللہ عنہ ذالک علوا کبیر ... البته دوسری قسم یعنی نقص في الصفات فتح عقلی متنازع فیہ کی طرف راجع نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ بالا تفاق عقلی ہے جو صفت کمال و نقصان کے معنی میں ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے صفات غیر اختیار یہ ہیں اور فتح متنازع فی غیر اختیار یہ میں نہیں ہوسکتا۔ حاصل یہ کہ افعال میں جو نقص ہوتا ہے وہ نقص استحقاق ذم و عقاب کے معنی میں بولا جاتا ہے جیسے کذب واظہار معجزه بر دست کا ذب ۔ لہذا اشاعرہ کے نزدیک بہر حال یہ کذب شرعی ہوگا جو اللہ پر منع نہیں رہے گا۔ اس کے برعکس صفات میں جو نقص ہوتا ہے وہ نقص صفت کمال و نقصان کے معنی میں بولا جاتا ہے جیسے جہل و عجز وغیرہ لہذا اشاعرہ، ماتریدیہ اور معتزلہ ہر ایک کے نزدیک بالا تفاق ممتنع رہے گا کہ یہ معنی بالا تفاق معقلی ہے۔

مقصود صاحب مواقف :۔ اس تفصیل سے صاحب مواقف کا مقصود ا شاعرہ پر اعتراض کرنا ہے کہ کذب اگر چہ نقص ہے مگر وہ چونکہ افعال کے قبیل سے ہے لہذا امتنع نہ رہے گا کیونکہ نقص فی الافعال فتح متنازع فیہ کی طرف راجع ہے جو استحقاق ذم و ثواب کے معنی میں ہے جسکو شاعر ہ شرعی گردانتے ہیں اور ماتریدیہ معتزلہ نقلی مانتے ہیں ۔ جب کذب اشاعرہ کے نزدیک شرعی ہوا تو قبل شرع اس میں فتح نہیں پایا گیا لبند اللہ عز شانہ پھر رسول سے کذب ممتنع نہ رہے گا بلکہ جائز ہوگا نیہ حکم شرعی ہونے کی تقدیر پر باب نبوت کا مسدود ہو نا لا زم آئے گا حالانکہ وہ مفتوح ہے۔

قوله لان ما ينافي الوجوب الذاتي كيفا كان اوفعلا الخ جواب :۔ مائن نے اپنے قول ممنوع‘ سے صاحب مواقف کے نظریہ کی تردید کی ہے اور اپنے قول لان ماینا فی الوجوب الذاتی سے سند منع پیش کیا ہے کہ مواقف کا قول کہ نقص فی الافعال فتح عقلی متنازع فیہ کی طرف راجع ہے ممنوع ہے یعنی ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے ہیں کہ نقص فی الافعال کے عقلی ہونے میں اختلاف و تنازع ہے کہ اشاعرہ نقص فی الافعال کو شرعی مانتے ہیں اور اللہ عز شانہ کے لئے افعال میں نقص کو عقل ممتنع نہیں جانتے ایسا کیسے ہو سکتا ہے جب کہ نقص وجوب ذاتی کے منافی ہے اب وہ نقص صفات میں ہو خواہ افعال میں بہر حال صوت استحالات عقلیہ میں سے ہے جو اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے عقلا محال ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ نقص وجوب ذاتی ، کے صفات و افعال میں سے جس کسی کے بھی منافی ہو گا اس کے ساتھ واجب بالذات کا انصاف محال ہے کیونکہ اس میں کمال نہیں نقصان ہے اور نقص سے اس کی تنزیہ واجب ہے کہ کمالات ممکنہ اس کی ذات کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے واجبتہ الثبوت ہوتے ہیں ۔

قوله وكذالك اثبتة الحكماء
مصنف بر بنائے ترقی اپنی سند منع کی تائید میں فلاسفہ کے نظریہ کو پیش کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں که چنانچہ اس لئے کہ نقص فی الافعال و نقص فی الصفات دونوں وجوب ذاتی کے منافی ہیں، حکماء وفلاسفہ نے بھی کذب کو نقص متحمل سمجھ کر باری تعالیٰ کے ساتھ اس کا انصاف محال قرار دیا ہے، حالانکہ حکماء دیندار نہیں ہوتے کسی نبی کو مانتے نہیں تاہم اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے کذب کو ضرور محال سمجھتے ہیں تو پھر
The permissibility [of lying] is considered ugly by the Ash'aris, thus its occurrence from Allah, may His glory be exalted, is rationally impossible. And when the permissibility of lying is also rationally impossible according to the Ash'aris, then for one who is described with lying and defect like the attribute of ugliness, the manifestation of a miracle on his hand is also prohibited; because when the original is impossible, the derivative is all the more impossible. Therefore, the manifestation of a miracle on the hand of a liar becomes impossible, and then the closure of prophethood does not necessarily follow.

His statement: 'And what is in al-Mawaqif that defect in actions refers back to ugliness...' Through this expression, the author (al-Matin) objects to the statement of the author of al-Mawaqif. First, the statement of the author of al-Mawaqif is mentioned, then the objection will be presented.

The statement of al-Mawaqif: The author of al-Mawaqif said that defects are of two types: (1) Defect in actions – such as lying, manifestation of a miracle on the hand of a liar, etc. (2) Defect in attributes – such as ignorance, incapacity, etc. And the first type, i.e., defect in actions, refers back to rational ugliness which is subject to dispute. Meaning that defect in actions is not unanimously rational; rather, defect in actions is in the sense of rational ugliness about which the Ash'aris and the Mu'tazila disagree. And that sense is deservingness of blame and punishment rationally.

(In short, any defect in actions is not rational by consensus; rather, some consider it rational and others consider it legal.) And the consideration of disputed rational ugliness in defect in actions is because Allah, the Exalted, is free in His actions; thus He can be deserving of praise and blame for His action, as that is not among rational impossibilities – exalted is Allah above that with great exaltation. However, the second type, i.e., defect in attributes, does not refer back to disputed rational ugliness; rather, it is rational by consensus, in the sense of perfection and deficiency. The reason is that Allah's attributes are non-volitional, and disputed ugliness cannot occur in non-volitional matters. The conclusion is that the defect that occurs in actions is spoken of in the sense of deservingness of blame and punishment, such as lying and manifesting a miracle on the hand of a liar. Therefore, according to the Ash'aris, this lying is legal, which is not prohibited from Allah. On the contrary, the defect that occurs in attributes is spoken of in the sense of perfection and deficiency, such as ignorance and incapacity. Hence, according to the Ash'aris, Maturidis, and Mu'tazila, it is unanimously impossible because this meaning is unanimously rational.

The intent of the author of al-Mawaqif: Through this detailing, the author of al-Mawaqif intends to object to the Ash'aris: that although lying is a defect, since it is of the category of actions, it will not be impossible, because defect in actions refers back to disputed ugliness, which is in the sense of deservingness of blame and reward. The Ash'aris consider this legal, while the Maturidis and Mu'tazila consider it transmitted. When lying is legal according to the Ash'aris, then before revelation, ugliness is not found in it. Thus, lying is not impossible from Allah; rather, it becomes permissible. Given that it is a legal ruling, the closure of the door of prophethood necessarily follows, whereas it is open.

His statement: 'Because that which contradicts necessary existence, whether it is a quality or an action...' The answer: The author (al-Matin) has refuted the theory of the author of al-Mawaqif with his statement 'it is prohibited' and has presented the proof of prohibition with his statement 'because that which contradicts necessary existence...'. That the statement of al-Mawaqif that defect in actions refers back to disputed rational ugliness is prohibited, meaning we do not accept that there is disagreement and dispute regarding the rationality of defect in actions. That the Ash'aris consider defect in actions to be legal and do not consider it rationally impossible for Allah. How can that be when defect contradicts necessary existence? Whether it is in attributes or actions, in any case, it is among rational impossibilities, which is rationally impossible for Allah, the Exalted. The conclusion is that defect contradicts necessary existence; whichever of attributes or actions it contradicts, it is impossible for the Necessary Being to be described with it, because it is not perfection but deficiency, and it is necessary to declare Him free from deficiency. Since possible perfections, when attributed to His essence, become necessarily established.

His statement: 'And similarly, the philosophers have affirmed it.' The author, to strengthen his proof of prohibition, presents the theory of the philosophers, saying that since defect in actions and defect in attributes both contradict necessary existence, the philosophers and sages have also considered lying to be a defect and have declared its being described with the Exalted to be impossible. Even though the philosophers are not religious and do not believe in any prophet, they still consider lying from Allah to be definitely impossible. So then
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a theological dispute within a usul al-fiqh commentary. The author (al-Matin, commentator of Muslim al-Thubut) critiques a statement from al-Mawaqif. Al-Mawaqif had distinguished between defects in actions (e.g., lying) and defects in attributes (e.g., ignorance), arguing that defect in actions is only 'ugly' by disputed rational assessment (some say rational, some say legal), while defect in attributes is unanimously rational. From this, al-Mawaqif concluded that lying (a defect in actions) could be permissible from Allah before revelation, which would imply that a liar could perform miracles, thus opening the door for false prophets. The author refutes this by asserting that any defect – whether in actions or attributes – is rationally impossible for Allah because it contradicts His necessary existence (wujub dhati). He supports this by citing that even non-religious philosophers recognize that lying is impossible for God. The Hanafi position aligns with the author: defect in any form is rationally impossible for Allah, and miracles cannot appear on the hand of a liar. This argument reinforces the necessity of prophethood and the impossibility of false claims.

Key Terms
نقص (nuqs): Defect or deficiency; the opposite of perfection (kamal).
وجوب ذاتی (wujub dhati): Necessary existence; the attribute of Allah that He must exist and His perfection is inherent.
قبح عقلی (qabah aqli): Rational ugliness; an act being inherently evil in reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author rejects al-Mawaqif's distinction between defects in actions and attributes?
A) Because defects in actions are not real defects
B) Because any defect contradicts Allah's necessary existence and is therefore rationally impossible
C) Because the Ash'aris have proven that defects in actions are only legally prohibited
D) Because the philosophers agreed that only defects in attributes are impossible

Key Takeaway
Defects in Allah's actions are rationally impossible, not merely legally prohibited, because they violate His necessary perfection.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
Impossibility of Lying for Allah: Rational vs Revealed
Refuting the view that deficiency in actions is only revealed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of wujub dhati to evaluate the rational impossibility of lying for Allah and critique the Ash'ari position.

Core Idea
Deficiency in actions contradicts essential necessity, making lying rationally impossible for Allah.

This passage presents a key usuli dispute: does rational necessity (wujub dhati) extend to Allah's actions, or only to His attributes? The author refutes the Ash'ari claim that deficiency in actions is only a revealed prohibition. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi commitment to rational proofs in theology and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dispute is whether deficiency in actions is rationally impossible or merely prohibited by revelation. The passage centers on the concept of wujub dhati (essential necessity) and its implications for Allah's attributes and actions.
2
State the Ash'ari position and its dalil
The Ash'aris hold that deficiency in actions is only prohibited by revelation (shar'i), not rationally impossible. They distinguish between deficiency in essence (which is rationally impossible) and deficiency in actions (which is contingent).
3
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
The Hanafis affirm that any deficiency, whether in attributes or actions, contradicts wujub dhati. Therefore, it is rationally impossible for Allah. The proof is that wujub dhati implies absolute perfection, and any deficiency negates that perfection.
The author uses the phrase 'لان ما ينافي الوجوب الذاتي كيفا كان اوفعلا' (because that which contradicts essential necessity, however it may be, whether attribute or action) as the core argument.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The author refutes the Ash'ari view by arguing that the same essential necessity applies to both attributes and actions. He strengthens his argument by noting that even philosophers (who do not follow revelation) affirm that lying is impossible for Allah, showing that reason alone suffices.
The philosophers' agreement is cited as a supporting proof (dalil) that the impossibility is rational, not merely scriptural.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If deficiency in actions were only revealed, then before revelation lying would be permissible. This would mean that a prophet could potentially lie, which would undermine the very proof of prophethood (since revelation confirms the prophet's truthfulness). Thus, the Ash'ari position leads to an unacceptable consequence.
This practical consequence demonstrates why the rational impossibility view is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالا تفاق معقلی ہے۔ مقصود صاحب مواقف :۔ اس تفصیل سے صاحب مواقف کا مقصود ا شاعرہ پر اعتراض کرنا ہے کہ کذب اگر چہ نقص ہے مگر وہ چونکہ افعال کے قبیل سے ہے لہذا امتنع نہ رہے گا کیونکہ نقص فی الافعال فتح متنازع فیہ کی طرف راجع ہے جو استحقاق ذم و ثواب کے معنی میں ہے جسکو شاعر ہ شرعی گردانتے ہیں اور ماتریدیہ معتزلہ نقلی مانتے ہیں ۔ جب کذب اشاعرہ کے نزدیک شرعی ہوا تو قبل شرع اس میں فتح نہیں پایا گیا لبند اللہ عز شانہ پھر رسول سے کذب ممتنع نہ رہے گا بلکہ جائز ہوگا نیہ حکم شرعی ہونے کی تقدیر پر باب نبوت کا مسدود ہو نا لا زم آئے گا حالانکہ وہ مفتوح ہے۔
قوله لان ما ينافي الوجوب الذاتي كيفا كان اوفعلا الخ جواب :۔ مائن نے اپنے قول ممنوع‘ سے صاحب مواقف کے نظریہ کی تردید کی ہے اور اپنے قول لان ماینا فی الوجوب الذاتی سے سند منع پیش کیا ہے کہ مواقف کا قول کہ نقص فی الافعال فتح عقلی متنازع فیہ کی طرف راجع ہے ممنوع ہے یعنی ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے ہیں کہ نقص فی الافعال کے عقلی ہونے میں اختلاف و تنازع ہے کہ اشاعرہ نقص فی الافعال کو شرعی مانتے ہیں اور اللہ عز شانہ کے لئے افعال میں نقص کو عقل ممتنع نہیں جانتے ایسا کیسے ہو سکتا ہے جب کہ نقص وجوب ذاتی کے منافی ہے اب وہ نقص صفات میں ہو خواہ افعال میں بہر حال صوت استحالات عقلیہ میں سے ہے جو اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے عقلا محال ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ نقص وجوب ذاتی ، کے صفات و افعال میں سے جس کسی کے بھی منافی ہو گا اس کے ساتھ واجب بالذات کا انصاف محال ہے کیونکہ اس میں کمال نہیں نقصان ہے اور نقص سے اس کی تنزیہ واجب ہے کہ کمالات ممکنہ اس کی ذات کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے واجبتہ الثبوت ہوتے ہیں ۔ قوله وكذالك اثبتة الحكماء
مصنف بر بنائے ترقی اپنی سند منع کی تائید میں فلاسفہ کے نظریہ کو پیش کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں که چنانچہ اس لئے کہ نقص فی الافعال و نقص فی الصفات دونوں وجوب ذاتی کے منافی ہیں، حکماء وفلاسفہ نے بھی کذب کو نقص متحمل سمجھ کر باری تعالیٰ کے ساتھ اس کا انصاف محال قرار دیا ہے، حالانکہ حکماء دیندار نہیں ہوتے کسی نبی کو مانتے نہیں تاہم اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے کذب کو ضرور محال سمجھتے ہیں تو پھر
اشاعرہ ایسا قول کیونکر کر سکتے ہیں جس کا بطلان بداعت عقل سے ثابت ہو۔
This is a rational agreement. The intent of the author of Mawaqif: With this detail, the author of Mawaqif intends to object to the Ash'aris that lying, although it is a deficiency, since it is of the category of actions, therefore it would not be impossible, because deficiency in actions refers to a concept that is disputed, which is in the sense of deserving blame and reward, which the Ash'aris consider as revealed, while the Maturidis and Mu'tazilites consider it rational. When lying is revealed in the view of the Ash'aris, then before revelation there is no [؟] found in it. [Because] Allah, may His glory be exalted, then lying from a messenger would not be impossible, but would be permissible. [؟] on the assumption of being a revealed ruling, the door of prophethood would be closed, whereas it is open. His statement: 'Because that which contradicts essential necessity, however it may be, whether an attribute or an action, etc.' Answer: The author refutes the view of the author of Mawaqif with his statement 'prevented' and presents evidence for prevention with his statement 'because that which contradicts essential necessity' that the statement of Mawaqif that 'deficiency in actions refers to a rational concept that is disputed' is prevented, meaning we do not accept that there is disagreement about the rationality of deficiency in actions, because the Ash'aris consider deficiency in actions as revealed and do not regard reason as deeming deficiency in actions impossible for Allah, may His glory be exalted. How can this be when deficiency contradicts essential necessity? Now, whether that deficiency is in attributes or in actions, in any case it is among rational impossibilities, which is rationally impossible for Allah, the Exalted. The conclusion is that deficiency contradicts essential necessity in whichever of attributes and actions it may be, its association with the Necessarily Existent is impossible because in it there is not perfection but deficiency, and it is necessary to declare Him free from deficiency, because the possible perfections, when attributed to His essence, are necessarily established. His statement: 'And similarly the philosophers have affirmed it.' The author, in support of his evidence of prevention, presents the view of the philosophers, saying that just as deficiency in actions and deficiency in attributes both contradict essential necessity, the philosophers and wise men also considered lying to be a deficiency and ruled its association with Allah, the Exalted, as impossible, even though the philosophers are not religious and do not believe in any prophet. Nevertheless, they certainly consider lying to be impossible for Allah, the Exalted. So how can the Ash'aris make a statement whose falsehood is proven by intuitive reason?
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage contains a dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Ash'ari school and the Maturidi/Mu'tazili school regarding whether lying (kadhib) is impossible for Allah due to rational necessity or only due to revelation. The author refutes the Ash'ari claim that deficiency in actions is a rationally debatable issue, arguing that any deficiency, whether in attributes or actions, contradicts the essential necessity (wujub dhati) of Allah, making it rationally impossible. The philosophers also affirm this, showing the strength of the rational argument. The Ash'ari position that lying is only prohibited by revelation leads to the problem that before revelation, lying would be permissible, which would undermine the consistency of prophethood. The author presents a rational proof (dalil aqli) that deficiency in any form cannot be attributed to Allah.

Key Terms
نقص (naqṣ): Deficiency or imperfection that contradicts the perfection of Allah
وجوب ذاتي (wujūb dhātī): Essential necessity – the attribute of being necessarily existent in and of itself, which implies absolute perfection
امتناع عقلي (imtinā' 'aqlī): Rational impossibility – that which reason deems impossible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is lying (kadhib) impossible for Allah?
A) Because revelation prohibits it
B) Because it is a deficiency that contradicts essential necessity
C) Because prophets cannot lie
D) Because it is illogical

Key Takeaway
Lying is rationally impossible for Allah because it contradicts the essential necessity (wujub dhati) of His perfection, a principle affirmed by reason and even by philosophers.

The Hanafi Objection Against Ash'ari on Punishing the Obedient
Objection and response on ta'dhib al-ta'i'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of essential necessity (wujub dhati) to evaluate the rational possibility of punishing the obedient and derive the difference between Hanafi and Ash'ari positions.

Core Idea
If lying is impossible for Allah due to deficiency, then punishing the obedient is equally impossible — the same essential necessity applies.

In the previous lesson, the Hanafi school defended the proof of prophethood by arguing that lying is rationally impossible for Allah because it is a deficiency (naqs). The author now raises a further objection: if you accept that, then you must also accept that punishing the obedient (ta'dhib al-ta'i') is impossible, for the same reason. This challenges the Ash'ari position, which considers such punishment permissible. In this lesson, we unpack that argument and the Ash'ari counter-response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shared premise
Recognize that both Hanafis and Ash'aris accept that lying is impossible for Allah because it is a deficiency that contradicts essential necessity (wujub dhati). This premise is the starting point.
The premise is derived from rational necessity, not revelation.
2
Recognize the analogy
Observe that punishing the obedient is also a deficiency (naqs), just like lying. The Hanafi argument draws an analogy between the two.
The deficiency in punishing the obedient is that it inflicts harm without cause, which reason deems blameworthy.
3
Apply the principle
Apply the same rule: if deficiency makes lying impossible, then deficiency makes punishing the obedient impossible. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that it is rationally impossible (mumtani' dhatan).
This is a qiyas (analogy) based on the common illa of deficiency.
4
Understand the Ash'ari response
Ash'aris distinguish between deficiency in attributes (which is impossible) and deficiency in actions (which is not inherently impossible). They argue that the occurrence of an imperfect action from Allah is not rationally impossible, though they affirm that Allah does not do such actions.
This response preserves Ash'ari voluntarism but may conflict with the idea that essential necessity covers actions as well.

Source Text

بلکہ اشاعرہ پر یہ اعتراض بھی وارد ہوگا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے تعذیب عاصی بھی جائز نہ ہو اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے اختیار سے عاصی نہیں بنا ہے کہ اس کو اس کی قدرت حاصل نہیں ہے بلکہ اللہ عز شانہ کے کرنے سے عاصی ہوا ہے پس جب وہ عاصی جعل باری تعالیٰ سے عاصی ہوا تو اس پر تعذیب کہ تم عاصی
کیوں ہوئے ایسا نقص ہے جس سے اللہ عز شانہ کی تنزیہ یہ واجب ہے اس لئے کہ نقص محال ہے۔ اشاعرہ کی طرف سے جواب : بعض اعاظم نے اشاعرہ پر وارد ہوئے اعتراض کا جواب دیا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ اشاعرہ گرچہ افعال کے حسن و قبح کے شرعی ہونے کے قائل ہیں لیکن اس معنی کر کہ حسن و قبح آخرت میں ثواب و عقاب کے استحقاق کے معنی میں ہے مگر اس کے ساتھ ان لوگوں نے اسبات کا بھی اعتراف کیا ہے کہ بعض افعال و بعض صفات نفس الامر میں بغیر درود شرع و شارع کامل و ناقص ہو سکتے ہیں تا ہم صفت ناقصہ نسبت کرتے ہوئے جناب باری کی طرف ان کے نزدیک بھی محال ہے۔ رہے افعال کاملہ و ناقصہ کا صدور تو اللہ رب العتزت شانہ سے محال ذاتی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی شان
His statement: 'But the Ash'aris would be required to hold the impossibility of punishment, etc.' Through this expression, the author intends to say that on the assumption that lying is a revealed deficiency and impossible for Allah, the Exalted, the objection of the closing of the door of prophethood would be removed from the Ash'aris. However, another objection would arise against the Ash'aris: that punishment of the obedient and the non-disobedient by Allah is also impossible, just as we, the Hanafis and Mu'tazilites, hold that punishment of the obedient is impossible, because it is a deficiency, and deficiency is impossible in the dignity of Allah, the Exalted. Although the Ash'aris consider punishment of the obedient permissible, even though in the punishment of the obedient there is such a concept whose deficiency and blameworthiness reason comprehends, or which is in the sense of rational deficiency and blameworthiness. The conclusion is that if lying is impossible for Allah because it is a concept and deficiency that contradicts essential necessity, then by the same cause punishment of the obedient would also be impossible because both are equal in deficiency. Yet the Ash'aris consider punishment permissible. That is why the author, in responding to the Mu'tazilite argument, indicated with the word 'but' (lakin) of interruption that the mentioned response will not be beneficial for the Ash'aris. Rather, another objection will arise against the Ash'aris: that punishment of the disobedient by Allah is also not permissible, because he did not become disobedient by his own choice, as he does not have power over that, but rather became disobedient by the action of Allah, may His glory be exalted. So when he became disobedient by the creation of Allah, the Exalted, then punishing him saying 'why did you disobey' is a deficiency from which it is obligatory to declare Allah, may His glory be exalted, free, because deficiency is impossible. Response from the Ash'aris: Some great scholars have given a response to the objection raised against the Ash'aris. It is that although the Ash'aris hold that the goodness and badness of actions are revealed, meaning that goodness and badness are in the sense of deserving reward and punishment in the afterlife, nevertheless they also acknowledge that some actions and some attributes can be perfect and imperfect in the reality of the matter without the confirmation of revelation and the Lawgiver. However, attributing an imperfect attribute to the Exalted is also impossible in their view. As for the occurrence of perfect and imperfect actions, it is not inherently impossible (dhati) from Allah, the Lord of Might, because His dignity...
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage continues the dispute by raising an objection: if lying is impossible for Allah because it is a deficiency, then punishing the obedient (ta'dhib al-ta'i') should also be impossible, as it is also a deficiency. The Hanafi and Mu'tazili positions hold that punishing the obedient is impossible, while Ash'aris consider it permissible. The author argues that the same reasoning applies. Furthermore, punishing the disobedient is also problematic because the disobedient person became disobedient by Allah's action, so punishing him would be a deficiency. The Ash'ari response acknowledges that some actions and attributes can be perfect or imperfect in themselves, but attributing imperfect actions to Allah is impossible, though the actual occurrence of such actions from Allah is not inherently impossible (not dhati imtina'). This distinction attempts to resolve the inconsistency but the passage implies it may not be fully satisfactory.

Key Terms
تعذيب الطائع (ta'dhīb al-ṭā'i'): Punishing the obedient person for no sin
نفس الأمر (nafs al-amr): The reality of the matter independent of revelation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is punishing the obedient (ta'dhib al-ta'i') impossible for Allah?
A) Because it is prohibited by revelation
B) Because it is a deficiency that contradicts essential necessity
C) Because the obedient deserve reward
D) Because it would be unjust

Key Takeaway
Punishing the obedient is rationally impossible for the Hanafi school because it is a deficiency, just like lying — both are excluded by essential necessity.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Ash'ari Defense on Impossibility of Lying and Punishment of the Obedient
Explaining the Ash'ari response to objections about God's actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between essential and customary impossibility in the Ash'ari framework and explain the Hanafi objection regarding punishing the obedient.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari distinction between essential and customary impossibility is key to their defense against the Hanafi objection.

This passage addresses a rational dispute between the Hanafis and Ash'aris about what actions are impossible for God. The Hanafis argue that if lying is impossible because it is a defect, then punishing the obedient must also be impossible. The Ash'aris respond by distinguishing between two types of impossibility: essential (based on God's essence) and customary (based on divine wisdom and custom). This distinction allows them to hold that punishing the obedient is not essentially impossible, only contrary to God's custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi objection
The Hanafis argue that punishing the obedient (ta'dhib al-taa'i') is impossible because it is a defect (naqs), just like lying. Since both are defects, the Ash'ari must accept both as impossible or neither.
This objection appears at the start of the passage.
2
Locate the Ash'ari response
The Ash'ari respond by distinguishing essential impossibility (imtinā‘ dhātī) from customary/istihsānī impossibility (imtinā‘ ‘ādī wa istihsānī). Lying is essentially impossible; punishing the obedient is only customarily impossible.
Essential impossibility relates to God's essence and will; customary impossibility is based on wisdom and divine custom.
3
Understand the distinction
Essential impossibility means the act cannot be attributed to God at all due to His nature (e.g., defectiveness). Customary impossibility means the act is not impossible in itself but is contradictory to God's wisdom and established custom, so it does not occur.
Hanafis do not accept this distinction; they hold that any defect is essentially impossible for God.
4
Apply the distinction to the dispute
According to the Ash'ari, punishing the obedient is not essentially impossible because God's essence and will are not limited. However, due to divine wisdom, it does not happen in reality (customary impossibility). Thus the objection fails.
The Ash'ari position is that God can do anything, but His actions follow wisdom.
5
Evaluate the effect on the objection
The Hanafi objection assumes a single type of impossibility. Once the Ash'ari introduce two types, they can consistently hold that lying is essentially impossible while punishing the obedient is only customarily impermissible.
This shows how a metaphysical distinction can resolve a rational argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بلکہ اشاعرہ پر یہ اعتراض بھی وارد ہوگا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے تعذیب عاصی بھی جائز نہ ہو اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے اختیار سے عاصی نہیں بنا ہے کہ اس کو اس کی قدرت حاصل نہیں ہے بلکہ اللہ عز شانہ کے کرنے سے عاصی ہوا ہے پس جب وہ عاصی جعل باری تعالیٰ سے عاصی ہوا تو اس پر تعذیب کہ تم عاصی کیوں ہوئے ایسا نقص ہے جس سے اللہ عز شانہ کی تنزیہ واجب ہے اس لئے کہ نقص محال ہے۔ اشاعرہ کی طرف سے جواب : بعض اعاظم نے اشاعرہ پر وارد ہوئے اعتراض کا جواب دیا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ اشاعرہ گرچہ افعال کے حسن و قبح کے شرعی ہونے کے قائل ہیں لیکن اس معنی کر کہ حسن و قبح آخرت میں ثواب و عقاب کے استحقاق کے معنی میں ہے مگر اس کے ساتھ ان لوگوں نے اثبات کا بھی اعتراف کیا ہے کہ بعض افعال و بعض صفات نفس الامر میں بغیر دَرْدِ شرع و شارع کامل و ناقص ہو سکتے ہیں تاہم صفت ناقصہ نسبت کرتے ہوئے جناب باری کی طرف ان کے نزدیک بھی محال ہے۔ رہے افعال کاملہ و ناقصہ کا صدور تو اللہ رب العزت شانہ سے محال ذاتی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی شان فعال لما یرید ہے البتہ حکمت وجود اور مصلحت کاملہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے سنت الہیہ جاری ہونے اور عادت الہیہ قائم ہونے کے موافق کمالات و ناقصات کا صدور ممتنع بالغیر ہے لیکن ذات باری تعالیٰ اور اس کے ارادہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے ان افعال کا صدور محال نہیں ہے۔ الغرض اللہ عز شانہ کی طرف کسی فعل کے وجوب و امتناع کی نسبت عادی و استحسانی ہے لہذا اشاعرہ پر امتناع تعذیب طائع کا الزام دینا لازم نہ آئے گا کیونکہ امتناع تعذیب سے مراد اگر امتناع ذاتی ہے یعنی یہ کہ اللہ عز شانہ کی نفس ذات اور اس کے ارادہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے تعذیب ممتنع ہے تو یہ غیر لازم ہے اور اگر امتناع عادی واستحسانی مراد ہے یعنی یہ کہ نظر کرتے ہوئے عادت الہیہ کے جاری ہونے کی طرف یا مصالح و حکم کے رعایت کی طرف تعذیب ممتنع ہے تو یہ لازم ہے مگر اشاعرہ کے نزدیک ممتنع نہیں ہے یونہی تعذیب عاصی ، تعذیب طائع کی طرح اللہ عز شانہ کی نفس ذات وارادہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے ممتنع نہیں ہے
گوکہ مصلحت و حکمت کی رعایت کے سبب موافق عادت ممتنع ہے لیکن حقیقت میں یہ ممتنع نہیں۔
The commentary on Muslim al-Thubut: page 267. How can the Ash'ari say something whose invalidity is proven by the primacy of reason? His statement: "But it follows upon the Ash'ari that punishment is impossible, etc." With this phrase, the author means that: By accepting that lying is an intellectual defect and impossible for God, the objection regarding the closure of the door of prophethood is removed from the Ash'ari. However, another objection arises against the Ash'ari: that punishing the obedient and one who is not disobedient is also impossible for God—just as we, the Hanafi community, and the Mu'tazila hold that punishing the obedient is impossible because it is a defect, and defect is impossible in the status of God. While the Ash'ari consider punishing the obedient permissible, even though in punishing the obedient there is such a [defect?] that reason [cannot?] identify its defectiveness and blameworthiness, or that reason is in the sense of [defect?] and blame. The conclusion: If lying is impossible for God because it is a [defect?] and deficiency that contradicts essential obligation, then with the same cause, punishing the obedient would also be impossible because both are equal in deficiency. Since the Ash'ari deem punishment permissible, for this reason the author, while responding to the Mu'tazila's argument, indicated with the conjunction 'lākin' (but) that the mentioned response will not be beneficial for the Ash'ari. Rather, this objection also arises against the Ash'ari: that punishing the disobedient is also not permissible for God, because a person does not become disobedient by his own choice—he does not have the power for that. Rather, he becomes disobedient by the doing of God. So when he became disobedient by God's making, then punishing him with 'why did you become disobedient' is such a defect that God's transcendence is necessary from it, because defect is impossible. Response from the Ash'ari: Some great scholars have answered the objection raised against the Ash'ari. It is that: Although the Ash'ari believe in the Shar'i nature of good and evil (husn and qubh)—meaning that good and evil in the sense of deserving reward and punishment in the afterlife—nevertheless they also acknowledge the affirmation that some actions and some attributes in re (nafs al-amr) can be perfect and imperfect without the coming of the Law and the Lawgiver. However, attributing a defective attribute to God is also impossible according to them. As for the occurrence of perfect and imperfect actions from God, it is not essentially impossible because His status is 'Doer of whatever He wills'. However, with regard to the existence of wisdom and perfect benefit, in accordance with the divine sunna being operative and the divine custom being established, the occurrence of perfections and imperfections is impossible by reason of another (mumtani‘ bi’l-ghayr). But with respect to God's essence and His will, the occurrence of these actions is not impossible. In short, the attribution of obligation (wujūb) and impossibility (imtinā‘) to any action from God is customary and istihsānī. Therefore, the objection of impossibility of punishing the obedient does not necessarily apply to the Ash'ari. Because if by 'impossibility of punishment' is meant essential impossibility—i.e., that punishment is impossible with regard to God's essence and His will—then this is not necessary. And if customary and istihsānī impossibility is meant—i.e., that punishment is impossible with regard to the divine custom being operative or with regard to observing benefits and wisdoms—then this is necessary, but the Ash'ari do not consider it impossible. Similarly, punishing the disobedient, like punishing the obedient, is not impossible with regard to God's essence and will, even if due to the observance of wisdom and benefit, it is impossible according to custom. But in reality, it is not impossible.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is an excerpt from a Hanafi usul commentary discussing a dispute between the Hanafis/Mu'tazila and the Ash'aris regarding the impossibility of certain actions for God. The author begins by noting that the Ash'ari claim that lying is impossible for God due to it being a defect (naqs) raises a new objection: if lying is impossible because it is a defect, then punishing the obedient (ta'dhib al-taa'i') is also a defect and should be impossible. The Hanafis and Mu'tazila hold that punishing the obedient is indeed impossible, but the Ash'aris permit it. The objection is that this inconsistency undermines the Ash'ari position. The author then presents a defense from some Ash'ari scholars: they distinguish between essential impossibility (imtinā‘ dhātī) and customary impossibility (imtinā‘ ‘ādī wa istihsānī). Essential impossibility pertains to God's essence and will, and they agree that attributing a defective attribute to God is essentially impossible. However, the occurrence of perfect and imperfect actions from God is not essentially impossible because God is 'Doer of whatever He wills'. Rather, it is impossible by reason of another (mumtani‘ bi’l-ghayr) due to the divine custom (sunnat Allāh) and wisdom (ḥikma). Thus, the impossibility of punishing the obedient is customary and istihsānī, not essential, so it does not necessarily apply. The passage concludes that the objection is based on a misunderstanding of the type of impossibility claimed by the Ash'aris.

Key Terms
امتناع ذاتی (imtinā‘ dhātī): Impossibility that pertains to God's essence and will; what cannot be attributed to God due to His nature.
امتناع عادی واستحسانی (imtinā‘ ‘ādī wa istihsānī): Impossibility based on divine custom (sunnat Allāh) and consideration of benefit and wisdom, not on God's essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi objection to the Ash'ari position on punishing the obedient?
A) The Ash'ari hold that punishing the obedient is impossible, contradicting their own principle.
B) If lying is impossible because it is a defect, then punishing the obedient, also a defect, should be impossible.
C) The Ash'ari deny that God can punish the disobedient, which is rationally necessary.
D) The Ash'ari believe that reason cannot determine good and evil at all.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari defense against the Hanafi objection relies on distinguishing essential impossibility (based on God's essence) from customary impossibility (based on divine wisdom), allowing them to hold that lying is essentially impossible while punishing the obedient is only customarily impossible.

Rational Obligation of Gratitude: Ash'ari vs Hanafi
Matn refutes Ash'ari proof and presents Mu'tazila counter-evidence on gratitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Ash'ari proof against the rational obligation of gratitude and evaluate the Hanafi refutation using the three arguments presented in the matn.

Core Idea
Gratitude is rationally obligatory; hardship does not negate benefit, and reason can perceive worldly benefits like security from punishment.

This usul dispute examines whether gratitude to the benefactor (shukr al-mun'im) is obligatory by reason alone, independent of revelation. The Ash'ari argue that it is not, citing the hardship of gratitude and reason's inability to grasp the Hereafter. The matn refutes each point, then presents the Mu'tazila counter-proof based on security from punishment. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to evaluate rational arguments in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ash'ari proof
Read the first part of the source passage where the Ash'ari argue that gratitude cannot be rationally obligatory because it involves hardship with no worldly benefit and reason cannot know the Hereafter.
Look for the three premises: no worldly benefit, no Hereafter benefit, and absolute negation.
2
Analyze the first refutation
The matn argues that the Ash'ari's own acceptance of rational rulings (ḥusn wa qubḥ) contradicts their claim that reason cannot comprehend the Hereafter.
This is a self-contradiction (tanāquḍ) argument.
3
Analyze the second refutation
If the Ash'ari proof were sound, it would negate all rational obligations, not just gratitude. This is absurd because obligation is accepted in other cases.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Analyze the third refutation and Mu'tazila proof
The matn refutes the claim that hardship has no benefit, citing examples like health and the Quranic verse on jihad. Then presents the Mu'tazila proof: gratitude leads to security from punishment, which is a worldly benefit.
Understand how the Mu'tazila turn the Ash'ari's own premise against them.

منعم کے عقلا واجب ہونے پر معتزلہ کی دلیل ذکر کی ہے تا کہ اشاعرہ پر منع اور اس کی دلیل پر معارضہ قائم ہو جائے ۔ دلیل : کا حاصل یہ ہے اشاعرہ کی دلیل کا مقدمہ کہ شکر میں بندہ کے لئے دنیا میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے ممنوع ہے اس لئے شکر احتمال عقاب سے امن کو ستلزم ہے برخلاف ترک شکر کے کہ اس میں عقاب کا احتمال ہے اور ہر وہ چیز جو ترک شکر کے سبب عقاب سے امن کو ستلزم ہے وہ واجب ہے لہذا شکر منعم عقلا واجب ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ دنیا میں عقاب سے مامون ہونا دنیاوی فائدہ ہے پس شکر منعم دنیا میں خالی از فائدہ نہ ہوا۔ قوله وعورض اولا بانه تصرف في ملك الغير بغير الخ معتزلہ کی دلیل مذکور پر مختصر ابن حاجب اور تحریر ابن ہمام میں دو طریقے سے معارضہ قائم کیا گیا ہے درج
He is independent, pure, and exalted; otherwise need of the other would be necessary, and need accompanies possibility and contingency, which opposes necessary existence. In this, there is also no benefit attached to the servant, because if there were any benefit for the servant, it would be in the world or the Hereafter; both benefits are negated. The worldly benefit is negated because gratitude involves such hardship upon the self that has no share or portion in the world, and where there is no share or portion, no worldly benefit accrues. As for the Hereafter benefit, it is also negated because the intellect has no power or scope to comprehend the affairs of the Hereafter, since the Hereafter is among the unseen matters that cannot be perceived by reason. In short, when benefit is absolutely negated, gratitude to the benefactor is not rationally obligatory. He said: I say, after accepting what the Mu'tazila claimed as it is... The Ash'aris presented the above proof that gratitude is not rationally obligatory. The matn refuted this proof with three reasons. In the above expression, the first of the three reasons is explained. First reason: After accepting the Mu'tazila claim of the intrinsic goodness and evil and the rational nature of rulings, the Ash'ari's statement that reason has no power and strength to comprehend the Hereafter is problematic, because when you accept the rational nature of rulings, you have effectively acknowledged the scope of reason in comprehending the Hereafter; then claiming the lack of scope of reason is tantamount to refuting your own statement. His statement: "But if this is complete, it would entail the negation of obligation" is the second reason. From this expression, the second refutation of the mentioned Ash'ari proof is given. The elaboration of the refutation is that if your mentioned proof is sound, it would necessarily lead to the absolute negation of obligation—that is, no matter, whether it is the obligation of gratitude or something else, the proof would require that nothing be rationally obligatory. Because the formulation of the proof applies also to the negation of absolute obligation, in that it would be said: nothing is rationally obligatory because if something were obligatory, it would be obligatory due to some benefit; otherwise it would be futile and vain. And benefit is absolutely non-existent because if there were a benefit, it would be either for Allah or for the servant. Allah cannot have a benefit because He is independent of benefit, and the servant also cannot have a benefit—in the world because it is hardship, and in the Hereafter because reason has no scope to comprehend the Hereafter. In short, the proof indicates the negation of absolute obligation, whereas the context of speech, on the assumption of accepting absolute obligation, shows that the discussion is specifically about the negation of the obligation of gratitude. His statement: "And that hardship does not negate benefit, for gifts are according to the degree of hardship" is the third reason. In this expression, the third refutation of the mentioned Ash'ari proof is given. The elaboration is that the claimant's statement that gratitude is hardship is accepted, but we do not accept that hardship is without benefit, because hardship has numerous benefits, such as the preservation of physical health, the correct and sound functioning of external and internal bodily organs, increase in sustenance, and repelling famine, etc., and that gifts and rewards are commensurate with hardships. Thus Allah Almighty said: "And those who strive for Us, We will surely guide them to Our ways." Behold, jihad is a great hardship, yet it entails benefit: repelling disbelievers, expanding the sphere of Islam, and obtaining spoils of war, etc. Therefore, the absolute negation of benefit from hardship is incorrect. His statement: "They said it entails security from the possibility [of punishment]"... In the above expression, the matn mentioned the Mu'tazila's proof for the rational obligation of gratitude to the benefactor, so that a refutation [of the Ash'ari] and a counter-argument to his proof could be established. The gist of the proof is that the Ash'ari's premise that gratitude has no worldly benefit for the servant is rejected, because gratitude entails security from the possibility of punishment, unlike abandoning gratitude which involves the possibility of punishment, and everything that entails security from punishment due to abandoning gratitude is obligatory; therefore gratitude to the benefactor is rationally obligatory. And it is clear that being secure from punishment in the world is a worldly benefit, so gratitude to the benefactor is not devoid of worldly benefit. His statement: "And it is objected, first, that it is a disposition of another's property without permission, etc." In Mukhtasar Ibn Hajib and Tahrir Ibn Hammam, a counter-objection to the mentioned Mu'tazila proof is established in two ways.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh regarding the rational obligation of gratitude to the benefactor (shukr al-mun'im). The Ash'ari school argues that it is not rationally obligatory, while the Mu'tazila (and the matn author, following the Maturidi position) hold that it is rationally obligatory. The matn refutes the Ash'ari proof with three reasons. First, the Ash'ari argument that reason cannot comprehend the Hereafter contradicts their own acceptance of rational rulings (ḥusn wa qubḥ). Second, the Ash'ari proof, if valid, would negate all rational obligation, not just gratitude, which is absurd. Third, the claim that hardship (as in gratitude) has no worldly benefit is false; hardship brings benefits like health, sustenance, and guidance, as evidenced by the Quranic verse on jihad. Then the matn presents the Mu'tazila's own proof: gratitude leads to security from punishment (which is a worldly benefit), and security from punishment is a benefit; therefore, gratitude is rationally obligatory. The commentary notes that later works like Mukhtasar Ibn Hajib and Tahrir Ibn Hammam object to the Mu'tazila proof on two grounds, but these are not elaborated here.

Key Terms
شکر منعم (shukr al-mun'im): Gratitude to the benefactor (Allah) for His blessings, which the matn argues is rationally obligatory.
الامن من احتمال العقاب (al-amn min ihtimal al-'iqab): Security from the possibility of punishment, which gratitude is said to entail, making it beneficial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the first refutation of the Ash'ari proof as presented in the matn?
A) The Ash'ari argument is self-contradictory because accepting rational rulings implies reason can comprehend the Hereafter.
B) Gratitude is a hardship that has no benefit at all.
C) The Ash'ari proof only applies to gratitude, not to other obligations.
D) The Mu'tazila have a stronger proof from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi refutation of the Ash'ari proof establishes that gratitude is rationally obligatory on the basis of worldly benefit (security from punishment) and the broader principle that hardship does not negate benefit.

Hardship Does Not Negate Benefit: Rebutting the Ash'ari Proof on Shukr
Third rebuttal of Ash'ari proof on shukr using mashaqqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi/Mu'tazili rebuttal to the Ash'ari argument that gratitude is not obligatory due to hardship, and cite the Quranic evidence that hardship yields benefits.

Core Idea
Hardship does not negate benefit; even the greatest struggle yields great gains.

The Ash'ari school argued that gratitude (shukr) cannot be rationally obligatory because it involves hardship without any clear benefit. This lesson presents a third rebuttal from a Hanafi usul commentary, which demonstrates that hardship is often accompanied by immense benefits, both worldly and religious. The rebuttal uses a powerful Quranic verse about jihad to prove that even extreme hardship brings reward.

Guided Path
1
State the Ash'ari Position
Identify the core claim: gratitude is not rationally obligatory because it involves hardship (mashaqqah) and no apparent benefit.
This is the premise being rebutted.
2
Articulate the Rebuttal
The commentator argues that hardship does not automatically negate benefit. He lists worldly benefits of hardship (health, provision, etc.) and cites the Quranic verse on jihad.
The rebuttal targets the Ash'ari assumption that hardship is always without benefit.
3
Analyze the Quranic Evidence
Examine Surah al-Ankabut 29:69: 'And those who strive in Our cause, We will surely guide them to Our paths.' The verse shows jihad involves hardship yet yields guidance and worldly gains.
The verse is used as a proof (dalil) that hardship can bring benefit.
4
Understand the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If the Ash'ari argument were accepted, there would be no rational basis for punishment for ingratitude. The rebuttal preserves the possibility of rational obligation.
The practical consequence: rational obligation of gratitude remains viable.

غرض یہ کہ دلیل مطلق وجوب کی نفی پر دلالت کر رہی ہے جب کہ انداز گفتگو و علی التنزل سے ظاہر ہے کہ مطلق وجوب کو تسلیم کر لینے کے بعد خاص و جوب شکر کی نفی پر گفتگو ہے۔ قوله "مع أن المشقة لاينفى الفائدة فان العطايا على متن الخ وجہ سوم :۔ اس عبارت میں اشاعرہ کی دلیل مذکور کا تیسرا رد ہے، رد کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ وجوب شکر کی نفی پر مستندل کا قول کہ شکر مشقت ہے مسلم ہے لیکن ہم یہ تسلیم نہیں کرتے ہیں کہ مشقت بے فائدہ ہوتی ہے کیونکہ مشقت کے بیشمار فائدے ہوتے ہیں مثلا جسمانی صحت برقرار رہتی ہے، اعضاء جسمانیہ ظاہر و باطنہ صحیح سلامت اور متحرک رہتے ہیں ، رزق میں زیادتی ہوتی ہے اور قحط دور ہوتا ہے وغیرہ کہ عطائیں اور انعامات ہمشقتوں کے مطابق ہوتی ہیں چنانچہ اللہ تعالیٰ عزشانہ کا ارشاد ہے والذين جاهدوا فينا لنهدينهم سبلنا ۔ دیکھو جہاد اعظم مشاق ہے تا ہم اس میں بھی فائدہ مرتب ہوتا ہے کہ کفار کو دفع کیا جاتا ہے اسلام کا دائرہ وسیع ہوتا ہے اور اموال غنیمت حاصل ہوتے ہیں وغیرہ لہذا
مشقت سے فائدہ کی نفی مطلقاً صحیح نہیں ۔
Because the intellect has no scope in comprehending matters of the Hereafter. In short, the evidence indicates the negation of absolute obligation, while the style of speech and 'alā al-tanazzul show that after admitting absolute obligation, the discussion is about the negation of specific obligation of gratitude. The statement: 'Even though hardship does not negate benefit, for gifts are in accordance with hardship, etc.' is the third rebuttal. The presentation of the rebuttal is that the claimant's statement that gratitude is hardship is accepted, but we do not accept that hardship is without benefit, because hardship has numerous benefits, e.g., physical health is maintained, external and internal bodily organs remain sound and active, provision increases, famine is removed, etc., that gifts and rewards are proportional to hardships. Indeed, Allah Most High says: 'And those who strive in Our cause, We will surely guide them to Our paths.' See, the greatest jihad is extremely hard, yet it also brings benefit: the disbelievers are repelled, the sphere of Islam expands, war spoils are obtained, etc. Therefore, the absolute negation of benefit from hardship is incorrect.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a third rebuttal of the Ash'ari argument that gratitude (shukr) is not rationally obligatory because it involves hardship without benefit. The commentator explains that the Ash'ari evidence only negates absolute obligation, but after accepting absolute obligation, the discussion is about specific obligation of gratitude. The rebuttal argues that even if gratitude involves hardship, hardship is not without benefit. The commentator lists worldly benefits: physical health, sound organs, increased provision, prevention of famine. Gifts and rewards are proportional to hardship. A Quranic verse is cited: 'And those who strive in Our cause, We will surely guide them to Our paths' (29:69). Jihad involves great hardship yet yields benefits like repelling disbelievers, expanding Islam, and acquiring spoils. Thus, the claim that hardship negates benefit is absolutely false.

Key Terms
مشقت (mashaqqah): Hardship or difficulty involved in performing an action.
وجوب عقلی (wujūb 'aqlī): Obligation established by reason, independent of divine revelation.
شکر منعم (shukr al-mun'im): Gratitude to the Benefactor (God) for His blessings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the third rebuttal against the Ash'ari argument?
A) Gratitude is not obligatory because it involves hardship.
B) Hardship does not negate benefit, as shown by jihad and other examples.
C) The Quranic verse about jihad proves that gratitude is not obligatory.
D) The Ash'ari argument is accepted without rebuttal.

Key Takeaway
Hardship alone does not negate benefit; therefore, the Ash'ari argument that gratitude is not obligatory due to hardship is refuted.

Mu'tazili Proof for Rational Obligation of Gratitude: Two Objections and Responses
Mu'tazili proof with two objections and responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the Mu'tazili proof for the rational obligation of gratitude, identify the two major objections from Ash'ari scholars, and evaluate the Mu'tazili responses using Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
Gratitude to Allah is rationally obligatory because it entails safety from punishment—a clear worldly benefit.

This passage from 'Ashraf al-Nu'ut' presents a classic usul dispute: can reason alone establish an obligation before revelation? The Mu'tazila argue that gratitude to the Benefactor is rationally obligatory, using a premise about safety from punishment. The Ash'ari scholars object that such gratitude without divine command is a forbidden disposition in Allah's property. In response, the Mu'tazila invoke rational permission and analogies to harmless acts like seeking shade. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to analyze the role of reason (ʿaql) in deriving legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Reconstruct the Mu'tazili proof
Identify the premises: (1) gratitude entails safety from punishment; (2) abandoning gratitude entails risk of punishment; (3) anything that brings safety from punishment is obligatory. Conclude that gratitude is rationally obligatory.
The proof relies on worldly benefit (safety) to counter the Ash'ari claim that gratitude has no benefit.
2
Understand the first objection
Gratitude involves using one's heart and limbs, which belong to Allah. Without His command, this is a disposition in His property without permission, which is forbidden. Thus gratitude would be forbidden, not obligatory.
This objection is based on the principle that using another's property without permission is prohibited.
3
Analyze the first response
The Mu'tazila admit there is no sharʿi (revealed) permission before revelation, but they assert there is rational permission (idhn ʿaqlī), which they equate to the permission of the Lawgiver because reason is considered an inner messenger.
This response highlights the Mu'tazili view that reason is an independent source of obligation.
4
Examine the second response
Gratitude is compared to seeking shade from a wall or light from a lamp—acts that cause no harm to the owner and thus require no explicit permission. Similarly, gratitude causes no harm to Allah, so it is permissible and indeed obligatory.
This is an analogical argument (qiyas) based on the illa of no harm.
5
Evaluate the dispute
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf: if gratitude is rationally obligatory, ingratitude merits punishment even without revelation; if not, there is no rational basis for punishment. Assess which response is stronger in Hanafi usul, where reason is a source but often requires corroboration.
The Hanafi school generally holds that reason alone can establish some obligations (e.g., knowing Allah) but many details require revelation.

قوله "قالوا انه يستلزم الامن من احتمال الخ
درج بالا عبارت میں ماتن نے شکر منعم کے عقلا واجب ہونے پر معتزلہ کی دلیل ذکر کی ہے
تا کہ اشاعرہ پر منع اور اس کی دلیل پر معارضہ قائم ہو جائے ۔ دلیل : کا حاصل یہ ہے اشاعرہ کی دلیل کا مقدمہ کہ شکر میں بندہ کے لئے دنیا میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے ممنوع ہے اس لئے شکر احتمال عقاب سے امن کو ستلزم ہے برخلاف ترک شکر کے کہ اس میں عقاب کا احتمال ہے اور ہر وہ چیز جو ترک شکر کے سبب عقاب سے امن کو ستلزم ہے وہ واجب ہے لہذا شکر منعم عقلا واجب ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ دنیا میں عقاب سے مامون ہونا دنیاوی فائدہ ہے پس شکر منعم
دنیا میں خالی از فائدہ نہ ہوا۔
قوله وعورض اولا بانه تصرف في ملك الغير بغير الخ
معتزلہ کی دلیل مذکور پر مختصر ابن حاجب اور تحریر ابن ہمام میں دو طریقے سے معارضہ قائم کیا گیا ہے درج
بالا عبارت میں مائن نے پہلا معارضہ ذکر کیا ہے۔
معارضہ اولی: یہ ہے کہ بغیر امر شارع کے شکر کرنا ملک غیر میں اس کی اجازت کے بغیر تصرف کرنا ہے اس لئے کہ عبد شاکر اپنے تمام قوی و اعضاء اور اموال کے ساتھ اللہ تعالیٰ کی ملک ہے اور شکر اس وقت ادا ہو سکتا ہے جب بندہ قلب کو ذکر الہی کی طرف پھیرے، اور اعضاء جوارح کو اسی چیز میں استعمال کرے جس کے لئے اس کی تخلیق ہوئی ہے پس اسطرح قلب کو پھیرنا اور اعضاء کو استعمال کرنا ملک غیر میں بلا اجازت مالک تصرف کرنا ہے اور مالک کی اجازت کے بغیر اس کی ملک میں تصرف کرنا حرام ہے لہذ ا شکر حرام۔ الغرض ترک شکر کے سبب عقاب کا احتمال اور اداء شکر کے سبب عقاب سے امن نہیں ہو سکتا۔
قوله ويجاب بل بالاذن العقلى
جواب معارضہ :۔ معارضہ مذکورہ کا دو جواب دیا گیا ہے ایک جواب کی طرف مائن نے درج بالا عبارت میں اشارہ کیا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ شکر قبل ورود شرع ملک غیر میں بلا اذن شرعی تصرف کرنا ہے مگر ہم یہ تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ اس تصرف میں علی الاطلاق اذن ہی نہیں ہے چونکہ یہ تصرف اذان عقلی سے ثابت ہے اور اذن عقلی در حقیقت اذن شارع ہے کیونکہ معتزلہ معقل کو رسول باطن مانتے ہیں۔
قوله على انه مثل الاستظلال والاستصباح.
اس میں معارضہ مذکورہ کے دوسرے جواب کی طرف اشارہ ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے شکر ایک ایسا فعل ہے جس کے لئے مالک کی اجازت درکار نہیں۔ اس لئے کہ شکر کے سبب ملک غیر میں تصرف کرنا ایسا ہی ہے جیسے غیر کی دیوار کے سایہ میں اس کی اجازت کے بغیر بیٹھنا اور جیسے دوسرے شخص کے چراغ کی روشنی سے اسکی اذن کے بغیر روشنی حاصل کرنا پس جس طرح صاحب جدار و مصباح سے اس کی اجازت کے بغیر سامیہ وروشنی حاصل کرنا جائز ہے حاجت اذن نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ ہر وہ چیز جس میں مالک کا کوئی نقصان نہ ہو اس کو بلا اذن مالک استعمال کرنا جائز ہے اسی طرح رب مشکور کی ملک میں اس کی اذن کے بغیر بطور ادا، شکر تصرف کرنا جائز ہے کہ اس میں مالک کا کوئی ضرر نہیں، چنانچہ عقل اتنا جانتی
The statement: 'They said that it entails safety from the possibility of punishment,' etc. In the above phrase, the matn mentioned the Mu'tazila's proof for the rational obligation of gratitude to the Benefactor, so that a prohibition (man') against the Ash'ariyya and a counterargument (mu'āraḍa) on their evidence could be established. The summary of the proof is: The Ash'ari premise that gratitude has no benefit for the servant in this world is rejected, because gratitude entails safety from the possibility of punishment, unlike abandoning gratitude, which entails the possibility of punishment. And everything that entails safety from punishment due to abandoning gratitude is obligatory. Therefore, gratitude to the Benefactor is rationally obligatory. And it is clear that being safe from punishment in this world is a worldly benefit, so gratitude to the Benefactor is not devoid of benefit in this world. The statement: 'And it was first objected that it is a disposition in the property of another without his permission,' etc. Two objections against the mentioned Mu'tazili proof were established in Mukhtaṣar Ibn Ḥājib and Taḥrīr Ibn al-Humām. The first objection is: Performing gratitude without the command of the Lawgiver is a disposition in the property of another without his permission, because the grateful servant with all his faculties, organs, and wealth belongs to Allah. Gratitude is performed when the servant turns his heart to the remembrance of Allah and uses his limbs for that which they were created. Thus, turning the heart and using limbs is a disposition in the property of another without the owner's permission, and such disposition without permission is forbidden. Therefore, gratitude is forbidden. Consequently, there is no possibility of safety from punishment through performing gratitude, and the possibility of punishment through abandoning it. The statement: 'And it is answered, rather by rational permission.' The response: Two answers are given. The first, hinted at in the matn, is that we admit that gratitude before the advent of revelation is a disposition in the property of another without shar'i permission, but we do not admit that there is absolutely no permission. Since this disposition is established by rational permission (idhn 'aqlī), and rational permission is in reality the permission of the Lawgiver because the Mu'tazila consider reason as the inner messenger. The statement: 'Rather, it is like seeking shade and seeking light.' This indicates the second answer: Gratitude is an act that does not require the owner's permission. Disposition in another's property through gratitude is like sitting in the shade of another's wall without his permission, or benefiting from another's lamp without his permission. Just as it is permissible to obtain shade and light from the owner of the wall and lamp without permission, because there is no need for permission whenever there is no harm to the owner, similarly, disposition in the property of the Benefactor Lord to perform gratitude without His permission is permissible because there is no harm to the Owner. Reason knows this much.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite proof for the rational obligation of gratitude to the Benefactor, followed by two objections and responses. The proof: The Ash'ari claim that gratitude has no worldly benefit is false because gratitude entails safety from punishment (a worldly benefit), while abandoning gratitude entails the risk of punishment. Since anything that prevents punishment through abandoning something is obligatory, gratitude is rationally obligatory. The first objection (from Ibn al-Hajib and Ibn al-Humam): Gratitude without divine command is a disposition in Allah's property without permission, which is forbidden, so gratitude is forbidden, not obligatory. First response: Although there is no shar'i permission before revelation, there is rational permission, which is equivalent to shar'i permission because Mu'tazila consider reason as an internal messenger. Second response: Gratitude is like seeking shade from a wall or light from a lamp—acts that do not harm the owner and thus require no permission. Since gratitude causes no harm to Allah, it is permissible and indeed obligatory rationally.

Key Terms
شکر منعم (shukr al-mun'im): Gratitude to the Benefactor (Allah).
معارضہ (mu'āraḍa): A counterargument or objection raised against a proof.
اذن عقلی (idhn 'aqlī): Permission derived from reason, considered by Mu'tazila as equivalent to shar'i permission.
استظلال (istiẓlāl): Seeking shade; used as analogy for permission to use another's property without explicit permission when no harm occurs.
استصباح (istiṣbāḥ): Seeking light from a lamp; another analogy for permission without explicit consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How do the Mu'tazila respond to the objection that gratitude without divine command is a forbidden disposition in Allah's property?
A) They admit gratitude is forbidden and reject its obligation.
B) They argue that rational permission suffices and that gratitude is like seeking shade or light, which causes no harm.
C) They claim that all actions before revelation are permissible.
D) They rely on a hadith about gratitude.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili defense of rational obligation of gratitude introduces key usul concepts: rational permission (idhn ʿaqlī) and analogical reasoning (qiyas) in the absence of revelation.
